Update Release 2211-jdk21.9 (New Features)
================================================================================
This release contains new features, bug fixes, and security improvements.

--- Fixed Issues ---

| Priority  | Key        | Component         | Summary |
|-----------|------------|-------------------|---------|
| Very High | CXEC-58223 | platform          | UserPasswordEncodingValidator wrongly complains about unchanged attributes - reset password flows broken |
| Medium    | CXEC-57827 | platform          | Media folder synchronization failing when moved between staged and online catalogs |
| High      | CXEC-38669 | platform          | Session expiry doesn't work for abandoned sessions |
| High      | CXEC-60235 | smartedit         | Vulnerability in fast-xml-parser 5.3.4 |
| High      | CXEC-60446 | smartedit         | Vulnerability in fast-xml-parser 5.3.7 |
| High      | CXEC-60236 | npm-ancillary     | Vulnerability in minimatch 10.1.1 |
| High      | CXEC-60237 | npm-ancillary     | Vulnerability in minimatch 9.0.5 |
| High      | CXEC-60441 | npm-ancillary     | Vulnerability in minimatch 10.2.2 |
| High      | CXEC-60238 | npm-ancillary     | Vulnerability in tar 7.5.7 |
| High      | CXEC-60251 | datahub           | Datahub no logs printed in v1/v2 version (see 3722717) |
| High      | CXEC-60253 | datahub           | Datahub data encoding issues (see 3721562) |
| High      | CXEC-60521 | platform          | Wrong composedtypes table is used to obtain Composed Types data during update system on 2211-jdk21.8 Preview |
| Medium    | CXEC-59056 | platform          | Validation framework failure on system update and startup |
| High      | CXEC-56121 | commerce-services | Standard integration flow is failing because of General Splitter Configuration "STOP ON EXCEPTION" checked (see 3656716) |
| High      | CXEC-57731 | platform          | Password check fallback policies are not triggered correctly |
| High      | CXEC-57748 | cust-mgmt-whole   | Missing authentication restriction for API in OrgCustomerManagementController (see 3685255) |
| High      | CXEC-57749 | cust-mgmt-whole   | Vulnerability in Jersey 3.1.9 |
| High      | CXEC-58124 | cust-mgmt-whole   | De-release Google Recaptcha V2 integration |
| High      | CXEC-58397 | integration-apis  | Product attribute is updated on batch save even when Optional.empty() is returned |
| Medium    | CXEC-57432 | platform          | Safeguard media streaming from the URL and resources (see Media URLs for External Data References) |
| Medium    | CXEC-57443 | platform          | Improve Media entry naming in ImpEx Export (see Adjusting Media#getFileName Method) |
| Medium    | CXEC-55322 | search-and-nav    | Vulnerability in Jetty: Java based HTTP/1.x, HTTP/2, Servlet, WebSocket Server 10.0.24 |
| Medium    | CXEC-56808 | platform          | quartz 2.5.0 not able to trigger schedules in short months |
| Medium    | CXEC-57439 | platform          | HAC access in Turkish locale |
| Medium    | CXEC-57696 | platform          | Hac ERR_TOO_MANY_REDIRECTS after update is complete for JDK21 |
| Medium    | CXEC-58114 | api-registry      | Ping destination doesn't work in JDK21 |
| Medium    | CXEC-58358 | platform          | Vulnerability in Apache Log4j 2.25.2 |

NOTE: CXEC-59056 "Validation framework failure on system update and startup" — potential fix for
validationModelPatch Spring BeanWrapper fluent setter issue. Monitor if MethodInvokingBean workarounds
can be removed once jdk21.9 is available on D2.

--- Security-Related Notes ---
No new SAP notes that provide some security-related information.

--- Deprecation Status Changes ---
No new APIs, modules, or extension deprecations.

--- API, Data Model, and Spring Framework Changes ---

  15. defaultOAuth2ClientCredentialsGrantRequestEntityConverter — restructured
  16. defaultClientAuthenticationMethodValidatingRequestEntityConverter — restructured

  21. defaultB2BUnitFacade — restructured
  26. defaultB2BUnitFacade — restructured

--- Library Changes ---

Deleted:
  Platform: org.apache.ws.security:wss4j 1.6.19

New:
  Platform: com.networknt:json-schema-validator 1.5.9
  Platform: com.googlecode.owasp-java-html-sanitizer:java10-shim 20260102.1
  Platform: com.googlecode.owasp-java-html-sanitizer:java8-shim 20260102.1

Upgraded (key ones):
  org.springframework:spring-beans         6.2.11 → 6.2.12   *** SPRING STILL 6.2.12 — hacSqlServerErrorObjectMapper bug NOT resolved by upgrade ***
  org.springframework:spring-core          6.2.11 → 6.2.12
  org.springframework:spring-context       6.2.11 → 6.2.12
  org.springframework:spring-webmvc        6.2.11 → 6.2.12
  org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-core      2.24.1 → 2.25.3
  org.apache.logging.log4j:log4j-api       2.24.1 → 2.25.3
  joda-time:joda-time                      2.13.0 → 2.14.0
  ma.glasnost.orika:orika-core-sap-commerce 2.5.7 → 2.5.8
  io.netty:netty-*                         4.1.128.Final → 4.1.130.Final
  org.jgroups:jgroups                      4.0.24.Final → 5.4.11.Final
  com.jayway.jsonpath:json-path            2.9.0 → 2.10.0
  com.azure:azure-json                     1.3.0 → 1.5.0
  org.assertj:assertj-core                 3.27.3 → 3.27.7
  com.ibm.icu:icu4j                        76.1 → 78.1
  org.apache.xmlgraphics:fop-core          2.10 → 2.11

Third-Party Compatibility:
  JRE/JDK: SapMachine 21.0 (required)
  Apache Tomcat: 10.1.52 (bundled) — UPDATED from previous
  Spring: 6.2.12
  Spring Security: 6.5.5
  Solr: 9.10 (latest), 9.8 (valid until July 15, 2026)

--- Upgrading to 2211-jdk21.9 ---

Tomcat Update: Apache Tomcat updated to 10.1.52.

Administration Console: Orphaned Media Files in Cleanup Tab — fixed.

Relative Tax Calculations: New formula applied for mixed gross price entries.

Number Series Generation: Improved reliability for unique number ranges.

Deprecations:
  - convertDocumenOperationType(SnDocumentOperationType) → use convertDocumentOperationType(SnDocumentOperationType)
  - getCommonI18NService() / setCommonI18NService(CommonI18NService) deprecated — will be removed in future release

Upgrading Core Accelerator Module (javax → jakarta):
  - Update external-dependencies.xml: javax.servlet.jsp.jstl → jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl:3.0.1
  - Add jsoup 1.21.2 dependency if storefront uses jsoup
  - Update dependencies.gradle libraries entry
  - Update .classpath entry
  - Run: ant clean all
  NOTE: Already completed in our migration.

Adjusting Media#getFileName Method:
  Behavior changed — now uses data PK + file extension as standard format.
  To restore legacy behavior: set media.get.file.name.legacy.enabled=true
  ACTION REQUIRED: Evaluate if this impacts any media download or display functionality.

Features in Rollout Phases:
  - Activating Validation for Password Reset:
    toggle.forgottenpasswordscontroller.doresetpassword.validation.enabled=true
  - New default API endpoints (deactivated by default in jdk21.8, may activate in future):
    getSubscriptionBills, getSubscriptionBill, createASMSessionEvent,
    getWishlistEntries, addWishlistEntry, removeWishlistEntry,
    getWishlist, getWishlists, createWishlist, updateWishlist, removeWishlist
    To keep deactivated: add to commercewebservices.api.restrictions.disabled.endpoints in manifest.json

Release Notes for 2211-jdk21 Updates
Each update release section includes the information you need to upgrade to that release and, if applicable, to implement new features and innovations.
To improve security and performance and provide the latest, future-proof technology, this version introduces a framework update. For more information, see Continuous Innovation in SAP
Commerce Cloud 2211.

Preview of the March Update Release (New Features)
This 2211-jdk21.8 preview release gives you the opportunity to implement and test new features in your development and staging environments before they're available productively in the
March update.
Update Release 2211-jdk21.7
This release contains only bug fixes and security improvements.
Update Release 2211-jdk21.6
This release contains only bug fixes and security improvements.
Update Release 2211-jdk21.5 (New Features)
This release contains new features, bug fixes, and security improvements.
Update Release 2211-jdk21.4
This release contains only bug fixes and security improvements.
Update Release 2211-jdk21.2
This release contains only bug fixes and security improvements.
Update Release 2211-jdk21.1
The September 2025 framework update brings important changes such as an upgrade to JDK 21 and Spring 6. Additionally, some deprecated extensions are removed.

Preview of the March Update Release (New Features)
This 2211-jdk21.8 preview release gives you the opportunity to implement and test new features in your development and staging environments before they're available productively in the March
update.
There are features reaching new rollout phases (activated by default and available out-of-the-box) in this release. For more information, see Features in Rollout Phases.

Upgrading to 2211-jdk21.8
There are upgrade steps. Apply the relevant steps to your custom code.

 Note
This upgrade information is provided as a preview. You can perform the upgrade in your staging and test environments until the release is available for productive use with the March update.

Tomcat Update
Apache Tomcat has been updated to 10.1.52 to ensure improved security. For more information, see Third-Party Compatibility.

Caching
The following configuration properties have been introduced for monitoring media cache stream statistics (disabled by default).

Property and Value

Description

media.cache.local.stream.stats.enabled=false

Enables or disables stream statistics collection, disabled by default.

media.cache.local.stream.check.interval.seconds=300

Interval in seconds for updating statistics, the default value is 300.

media.cache.local.stream.max.open.seconds=15

Maximum allowed duration in seconds after which a stream is considered as potentially problematic,
the default value is 15.

media.cache.local.stream.debug.stack=false

Enables stack trace logging for streams exceeding the maximum open duration, disabled by default.

These properties enable monitoring of MediaCacheFileInputStream instances to detect streams that aren't properly closed, which can prevent cached files from being removed from disk
during eviction. Statistics are also available over JMX for monitoring. For more details, see Media Cache Streams Management.

Administration Console: Orphaned Media Files in Cleanup Tab
We have fixed an issue with the orphaned media files in the Administration Console ( Maintenance

Cleanup

Orphaned Media Files ). Previously, when administrators navigated to this tab to

identify and remove unused media files, the system would fail to load any data, displaying an empty table even when orphaned media files existed in the system. The problem persisted even after
refreshing the page.
The fix replaces inconsistent tab detection methods with a standardized getSelectedTabIndex() function, ensuring the Orphaned Media Files tab properly launches its data loading function.
As a result, the table is now correctly populated with orphaned media files, including file names, paths, and associated data. Administrators can see exactly which media files are orphaned and take
appropriate cleanup actions.

Relative Tax Calculations
We have fixed an issue when calculating the relative tax of an entry with a mixed gross price. When calculating the relative tax of an entry or cart with a gross price, we use the gross price directly
and we didn't deduct the fixed tax. The old formula implemented in this case is applied to the relative tax value, such as value = entryTotalValue * percentageTaxValue / (100 +

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

11

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
percentageTaxValue), which isn't correct. The new formula is: applied relative tax value = (entryTotalValue - applied fixed tax value) * percentageTaxValue / (100 + percentageTaxValue). For
example, Tax 1 has a 10% rate, Tax 2 is 1 EUR, and the product gross price is 12 EUR. Then, the applied relative tax value is (12 - 1) * 10 / (100 + 10) = 1 EUR.

Number Series Generation Improvement
The number series generation has been improved for reliability when fetching unique number ranges.

Deprecations
The convertDocumenOperationType(SnDocumentOperationType) method is deprecated due to a typo in its name. Update your code to use

convertDocumentOperationType(SnDocumentOperationType) instead of the misspelled version.
We have deprecated the following methods as the CommonI18NService is no longer used by this populator:

getCommonI18NService()
setCommonI18NService(CommonI18NService)
These methods will be removed in a future release. If you have extended this populator and rely on these methods, you should refactor your code to remove dependencies on the

CommonI18NService.

Upgrading Core Accelerator Module
If your extensions are generated from the yacceleratorstorefront template, perform the following steps to upgrade from javax to jakarta.

Context
If you are still using an older accelerator version, the required dependency upgrades that are normally handled by acceleratorstorefrontcommons are not applied automatically. In this case,
you must manually upgrade the dependencies in your custom storefront extensions or migrate to the latest storefront module.

Procedure
1. Open the external-dependencies.xml file in your storefront extension and update the following dependency.
/* before */
<dependency>
<groupId>org.glassfish.web</groupId> <artifactId>javax.servlet.jsp.jstl</artifactId>
<version>1.2.5</version>
</dependency>

/* after */
<dependency>
<groupId>org.glassfish.web</groupId>
<artifactId>jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl</artifactId>
<version>3.0.1</version>
</dependency>
2. If the storefront uses jsoup, add or update the following dependency:
<dependency>
<groupId>org.jsoup</groupId>
<artifactId>jsoup</artifactId>
<version>1.21.2</version>
</dependency>
3. Open the dependencies.gradle file in your storefront extension and update the following dependency.
/* before */
libraries << "org.glassfish.web:javax.servlet.jsp.jstl:1.2.5"
/* after */
libraries << "org.glassfish.web:jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl:3.0.1"
4. If the storefront uses jsoup, add or update the following dependency:
libraries << "org.jsoup:jsoup:1.21.2"
5. Open the .classpath file in your storefront extension and update the following dependency.
/* before */
<classpathentry exported="false" kind="lib" path="web/webroot/WEB-INF/lib/javax.servlet.jsp.jstl-1.2.5.jar"/>
/* after */
<classpathentry exported="false" kind="lib"
path="web/webroot/WEB-INF/lib/jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl-3.0.1.jar"/>
6. If the storefront uses jsoup, add or update the following dependency:
<classpathentry exported="false" kind="lib"
path="web/webroot/WEB-INF/lib/jsoup-1.21.2.jar"/>
7. Clean and rebuild the system by running the following command:
ant clean all
8. Verify that the old javax.servlet.jsp.jstl and jsoup JAR files are removed and that the new jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl version 3.0.1 and jsoup version 1.21.2 JAR files are
successfully downloaded.
9. Review your storefront source code and update all javax.* imports to the corresponding jakarta.* packages as required. For detailed guidance, refer to the official Jakarta migration
documentation:Migrating from javax to jakarta

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

12

3/9/26, 4:28 PM

Results
The storefront extension uses jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl 3.0.1 and jsoup 1.21.2, ensuring compatibility with newer versions.

Related Information
Upgrading jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl from 1.2.6 to 3.0.1 in JDK 21

Implementing a Fixed Issue
There are additional steps to implement some fixed issues.

Adjusting Media#getFileName Method
Implementation of Media#getFileName was aligned with its documented specification and optimized to eliminate file system operations.

Context
The behavior of the Media#getFileName method deviated from the method's specification. The file name depended on the storage strategy used by the media and the java.io.File
representation of it.
The method has been adjusted and optimized to conform to the documented specification. Returned file names now follow a standard format using the data primary key and file extension. Since
custom code may rely on the previous behavior, a legacy mode flag is provided. The legacy behavior is disabled by default and can be restored using this flag.

Procedure
To use the old behavior, set the value of the media.get.file.name.legacy.enabled property to true.

Upgrading to 2211-jdk21.7
There are maintenance changes, such as bug fixes, that may require you to update your custom code.
A new property, task.auxiliaryTables.scheduler.enabled, has been introduced that allows you to control whether a specific aspect, such as backoffice or

backgroundprocessing, can become a task scheduler. This property is configured per aspect type - all pods of that aspect inherit the same scheduler eligibility setting. By default, this

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

15

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
property is set to true. For more information on the property, see Properties.

 Note
At least one aspect in your deployment must have this property set to true to enable task scheduling. It's recommended that you enable the scheduler role for the

backgroundprocessing aspect while disabling it for user-facing aspects like backoffice.
Configuring task scheduler eligibility by aspect type reduces disruptions during maintenance operations. By restricting the scheduler role to back end aspects like

backgroundprocessing, you can troubleshoot and restart those aspects without impacting user-facing aspects. This approach provides greater operational flexibility and system
stability while ensuring reliable task execution across the cluster.
The fallback password policy now includes historical password checking in addition to quality requirements. This means users can receive historical password checking through two routes:
explicitly through password.policy.historical.groups.included, or through the fallback policy when password.policy.fallback.enabled is true.
Additionally, you can now exclude specific user groups from the fallback policy, including both quality and historical checks, using the

password.policy.fallback.excluded.groups property. Enter group names as a comma-separated list or use * to exclude all groups.

 Note
The password.policy.historical.groups.included default value has changed from * to empty, shifting historical password enforcement primarily to the fallback policy
unless you explicitly assign groups.

Administration Console: Orphaned Media Files in Cleanup Tab
We have fixed an issue with the orphaned media files in the Administration Console ( Maintenance

Cleanup

Orphaned Media Files ). Previously, when administrators navigated to this tab to

identify and remove unused media files, the system would fail to load any data, displaying an empty table even when orphaned media files existed in the system. The problem persisted even after
refreshing the page.
The fix replaces inconsistent tab detection methods with a standardized getSelectedTabIndex() function, ensuring the Orphaned Media Files tab properly launches its data loading function.
As a result, the table is now correctly populated with orphaned media files, including file names, paths, and associated data. Administrators can see exactly which media files are orphaned and take
appropriate cleanup actions.

Caching
The following configuration properties have been introduced for monitoring media cache stream statistics (disabled by default).

Property and Value

Description

media.cache.local.stream.stats.enabled=false

Enables or disables stream statistics collection, disabled by default.

media.cache.local.stream.check.interval.seconds=300

Interval in seconds for updating statistics, the default value is 300.

media.cache.local.stream.max.open.seconds=15

Maximum allowed duration in seconds after which a stream is considered as potentially
problematic, the default value is 15.

media.cache.local.stream.debug.stack=false

Enables stack trace logging for streams exceeding the maximum open duration, disabled by
default.

These properties enable monitoring of MediaCacheFileInputStream instances to detect streams that aren't properly closed, which can prevent cached files from being removed from
disk during eviction. Statistics are also available over JMX for monitoring. For more details, see Media Cache Streams Management.

Solr Security and Version Updates
Tika libraries have been upgraded to address a security vulnerability. As part of this security mitigation, you now have access to a dedicated language detection processor. If you have the

langid module and TikaLanguageIdentifierUpdateProcessorFactory enabled in your Solr configuration, For more details, see .
In accordance with our Solr Version Validity Policy, support for Solr 9.7 has been discontinued as of February 10, 2026. For upgrade information, see Upgrading to Solr 9.8.
We've upgraded Solr from version 9.10 to 9.10.1, and this update will be automatically applied during the build phase for all customers who have set the solrversion to 9.10 in their

manifest.json. You can avail the latest improvements and fixes provided in Solr 9.10.1 without any additional configuration on your part.

Upgrading to 2211-jdk21.6
There are maintenance changes, such as bug fixes, that may require you to update your custom code.

Password Handling for Legacy Hashing Algorithms
We have resolved a situation where the password reset functionality failed for users whose passwords were stored using outdated hashing algorithms. These users could not log in when their
passwords used legacy hashing algorithms but this is expected system behavior. The issue was that when they attempted to reset their passwords, the reset process itself did not complete
successfully.
The problem was caused by the UserPasswordEncodingValidator checking password encodings on every user operation, even when the password encoding itself wasn’t being changed.
We have resolved the issue by:
Restoring the password reset flow to properly handle users with deprecated password hashes so that affected users can reset their password and log in after completing the reset. Now the

UserPasswordEncodingValidator always runs, but includes an additional condition that skips validation when the password remains unchanged.
Enabling automatic password rehashing during successful logins – the password.encoding.auto.update.enabled property is now set to true by default. This means that when
users successfully log in, their passwords are automatically upgraded to the current default encodings.

 Note
Automatic update of password encoding only works for passwords hashed with currently supported algorithms (argon2, bcrypt, and scrypt). It is only functional for end users,
understood as storefront customers and not employee users, regardless of the end users’ current password encoding.

For detailed technical information and troubleshooting steps, see KBA 3705251

.

File Attachment Processing in Orbeon Forms Handled by yForms
Some users may have encountered a problem when uploading files through forms with attachments. It happened that the attachment data unexpectedly was consumed from request’s input
stream during the request processing. The attachment was still present but only in parsed form, causing issues when the system tried to handle preview functionality, leaving forms incomplete or
causing upload failures.
This issue occurred specifically with yForms/Orbeon forms using multipart/form-data encoding when processed through the DefaultSimpleProxyEngine.
To address the problem, we've implemented a new multipart data handling system, including a new ParsedMultipartDataSender component that properly preserves file attachments
throughout the entire request lifecycle.
The new implementation now:
Detects multipart requests early – Identifies when a form contains file uploads before processing begins
Preserves attachment data – Safely stores and forwards all parts of multipart requests from the parsed form, including file content and metadata
Maintains proper formatting – Reconstructs multipart data with correct boundaries and headers when forwarding requests
Handles multiple attachments – Supports forms with multiple file upload fields

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

19

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
As a result, users can now confidently upload files through yForms/Orbeon forms without data loss.

Expired Session Cleanup for Clustered Environments
Previously, the out-of-the-box sessionCacheRegion did not invalidate cached Session objects when sessions were invalidated. This caused Session objects to remain in heap memory until
the cache region filled and triggered LRU (Least Recently Used) eviction, leading to unnecessary memory consumption and potential performance degradation. To fix this issue, SAP Commerce
Cloud now allows you to coordinate timeout policies, periodic discovery jobs, and cluster health monitoring to automatically remove expired sessions without manual intervention. Configure five
critical areas:
Expired Session Cleanup– Schedule discovery jobs with batch sizing to prevent performance degradation during large purges
Cluster Health Monitoring – Detect failed nodes through heartbeat intervals and stale node thresholds to trigger recovery
Memory Management – Cap in-memory queues of expired session IDs to prevent heap exhaustion
Session Timeout Policy – Establish predictable validity periods across the cluster
For more information on the new configuration, see Configuring Expired Session Cleanup for Clustered Environments.

Potential Breaking Changes
To fix the issue where multipart/form-data attachments cannot be handled in JDK 21, the protected connect method in the class

de.hybris.platform.xyformsservices.proxy.orbeonservices.impl.DefaultSimpleProxyEngine has been updated.
Previous Method:
protected HttpURLConnection connect(final HttpServletRequest request, final String url, final String method,
final Map<String, String> headers)
throws URISyntaxException, MalformedURLException, IOException, MalformedCookieException
Updated Method:
protected HttpURLConnection connect(final HttpServletRequest request, final String url, final String method,
final Map<String, String> headers)
throws URISyntaxException, IOException, MalformedCookieException, ServletException

Upgrade to Solr 9.10
You can now upgrade to Solr 9.10, which addresses the deprecation of WMIC by Microsoft. This update ensures that your Solr delpoyment continues to operate reliably and remains compatible
with Windows systems.
You can upgrade at your convenience, as no migration steps are required. However, we recommend updating the luceneMatchVersion in your solrconfig.xml to version 9.12. This upgrade
is optional, so you can choose to proceed based on your specific needs and preferences.
Reindexing after the upgrade is not necessary, but you may wish to evaluate your configuration and performance needs to determine if reindexing would benefit your environment.

Google Maps Marker Element Replacement
The google.maps.Marker class is deprecated, and should be replaced with google.maps.marker.AdvancedMarkerElement. For more information, see .

PDF Injection Prevention in Customer Support Backoffice
To prevenet potential PDF injection vulnerabilities when uploading attachments, a PDFValidator has been implemented to block PDFs containing JavaScript. This validation is controlled by
the property: customersupportbackoffice.attachment.pdf.validation.enabled(default: true).

Search and Navigation

Implementing a Fixed Issue
There are additional steps to implement some fixed issues.

Fixing Stuck OPF Order Processes
In some rare cases, such as network issues or extreme race conditions, the OPF order process may fail and remain stuck in an unfinished state. To ensure system reliability, we introduce a
background job that regularly scans such failed processes and retries them automatically.

Fixing Stuck OPF Order Processes
In some rare cases, such as network issues or extreme race conditions, the OPF order process may fail and remain stuck in an unfinished state. To ensure system reliability, we introduce a
background job that regularly scans such failed processes and retries them automatically.

Context
This update includes configuration changes, Spring bean definitions, and new Impex entries.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

22

3/9/26, 4:28 PM

Procedure
1. Configuration Update: Add the following properties to opfservices/project.properties. This background job retrieves business processes from a defined time window.

retryProcessBeforeMinutes defines the end time of the scan window.
retryProcessWithinHours defines the start time of the scan window.

 Example
If the job runs at 10:10, with:

retryProcessBeforeMinutes = 10
retryProcessWithinHours = 6
Then:
End time = 10:10 − 10 minutes = 10:00
Start time = 10:10 − 10 minutes − 6 hours = 04:00
Processes created between 04:00 and 10:00 will be included.

# Which OPF processes can be retried.
opf.process.retry.job.retryDefinitionNames=opf-order-process,opf-return-process
# Which actions can be retried.
opf.process.retry.job.retryActions=opfCheckAuthorization,opfCheckCapture,opfCheckRefundAction
# Which process states can be retried.
opf.process.retry.job.retryProcessStates=WAITING,ERROR,FAILED
# Maximum number of retry attempts allowed per action.
opf.process.retry.job.actionMaxAttempts=4
# Retrieve processes created before X minutes. Default: 10 minutes.
opf.process.retry.job.retryProcessBeforeMinutes=10
# Retrieve processes created within the last X hours. Default: 6 hours.
opf.process.retry.job.retryProcessWithinHours=6
2. Spring XML Update: Add the opfProcessRetryJob bean to opfservices/resources/opfservices-spring.xml
<alias name="opfProcessRetryJob" alias="opfProcessRetryJob"/>
<bean id="opfProcessRetryJob"
class="de.hybris.platform.opfservices.process.job.OpfProcessRetryJobPerformable"
parent="abstractJobPerformable">
<constructor-arg name="configurationService" ref="configurationService"/>
<constructor-arg name="businessProcessService" ref="businessProcessService"/>
</bean>
3. Impex Update: Add the job and cron job in opfservices/resources/impex/essentialdata-cronjobs.impex. By default, no Trigger is assigned, so the job is disabled. You can
either run it manually in Backoffice or configure a Trigger for scheduled execution.
#opfProcessRetryJob JOB
INSERT_UPDATE ServicelayerJob; code[unique = true]; springId[unique = true]
; opfProcessRetryJob
; opfProcessRetryJob
#opfProcessRetry CRON JOB
INSERT_UPDATE CronJob; code[unique = true]; job(code)[unique = true]; sessionLanguage(isoCode)[default = en]
; opfProcessRetryCronJob ; opfProcessRetryJob
;
4. Integration Object Update: In essentialdata-opfservices-integrationObject.impex, update the PaymentTransactionEntry attribute so that PaymentTransaction is
created automatically.
INSERT_UPDATE IntegrationObjectItemAttribute; integrationObjectItem(integrationObject(code), code)[unique = true]; attributeName[unique = true]
# --- Currency --; OpfIntegrationObject:Currency ; isocode ; Currency:isocode ; ; true ;
# --- Order --; OpfIntegrationObject:Order ; code ; Order:code ; ; true ;
; OpfIntegrationObject:Order ; paymentInfo ; Order:paymentInfo ; OpfIntegrationObject:OpfPaymentInfo ; ; true
# --- AbstractOrder (base type for Order/Cart) --; OpfIntegrationObject:AbstractOrder ; code ; AbstractOrder:code ; ; true ;
; OpfIntegrationObject:AbstractOrder ; paymentInfo ; AbstractOrder:paymentInfo ; OpfIntegrationObject:OpfPaymentInfo ; ; true
# --- Cart --; OpfIntegrationObject:Cart ; code ; Cart:code ; ; true ;
; OpfIntegrationObject:Cart ; paymentInfo ; Cart:paymentInfo ; OpfIntegrationObject:OpfPaymentInfo ; ; true
# --- PaymentType --; OpfIntegrationObject:PaymentType ; code ; CheckoutPaymentType:code ; ; true ;
# --- PaymentTransactionEntry --; OpfIntegrationObject:PaymentTransactionEntry ; versionID ; PaymentTransactionEntry:versionID ; ; true ;
; OpfIntegrationObject:PaymentTransactionEntry ; code ; PaymentTransactionEntry:code ; ; true ;
; OpfIntegrationObject:PaymentTransactionEntry ; paymentTransaction ; PaymentTransactionEntry:paymentTransaction ; OpfIntegrationObject:Payment
# --- OrderEntry --; OpfIntegrationObject:OrderEntry ; order ; OrderEntry:order ; OpfIntegrationObject:Order ; true ;
# --- CartEntry --; OpfIntegrationObject:CartEntry ; order ; CartEntry:order ; OpfIntegrationObject:Cart ; true ;
# --- PaymentTransactionType --; OpfIntegrationObject:PaymentTransactionType ; code ; PaymentTransactionType:code ; ; true ;
# --- DeliveryStatus --; OpfIntegrationObject:DeliveryStatus ; code ; DeliveryStatus:code ; ; true ;
# --- Catalog --; OpfIntegrationObject:Catalog ; id ; Catalog:id ; ; true ;

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

23

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
# --- User --; OpfIntegrationObject:User ; uid ; User:uid ; ; true ;
# --- DeliveryMode --; OpfIntegrationObject:DeliveryMode ; code ; DeliveryMode:code ; ; true ;
# --- PaymentTransaction --; OpfIntegrationObject:PaymentTransaction ; code ; PaymentTransaction:code ; ; true ;
; OpfIntegrationObject:PaymentTransaction ; entries ; PaymentTransaction:entries ; OpfIntegrationObject:PaymentTransactionEntry ; true ;
; OpfIntegrationObject:PaymentTransaction ; info ; PaymentTransaction:info ; OpfIntegrationObject:OpfPaymentInfo ; ; true ;
; OpfIntegrationObject:PaymentTransaction ; versionID ; PaymentTransaction:versionID ; ; true ;
# --- Region --; OpfIntegrationObject:Region ; isocode ; Region:isocode ; ; true ;
; OpfIntegrationObject:Region ; country ; Region:country ; OpfIntegrationObject:Country ; true ;

; OpfIntegrationObject:CatalogVersion ; version ; CatalogVersion:version ; ; true ;

; OpfIntegrationObject:OpfPaymentInfo ; user ; SAPGenericPaymentInfo:user ; OpfIntegrationObject:User ; true ;
; OpfIntegrationObject:OpfPaymentInfo ; cartId ; SAPGenericPaymentInfo:sapCartId ; ; true ;

Once you import the updated Impex files, you should see the OPF Process Retry Job available in Backoffice.

Version

Spring

6.2.11

Spring Security

6.5.5

Additional Information

6.5 Migration Guide

.

Search Engines
Major Solr Version

Minor Solr Version

Version Validity

9

9.10

Latest version. Addresses the deprecation of WMIC by Microsoft.
No upgrade steps are required. However, luceneMatchVersion
should be updated to 9.12.
For more information, see Upgrading to 2211-jdk21.6.

9.8

Valid until July 15, 2026.
If you don't specify a Solr version in the manifest.json during
the build process, the system defaults to version 9.8. For
information on configuring your desired Solr version, refer
Selecting Solr Server Version.
For information on the upgrade procedure, see Upgrading to Solr
9.8.

8

9.7

Not valid as of February 10, 2026.

8.11

Not valid as of January 21, 2025.

SAP Commerce Cloud supports the latest version of SAP Commerce and the Solr version that is shipped with it. Although it is possible to build and deploy SAP Commerce Cloud with older
versions of Solr supported by older releases, we recommend you upgrade to the latest Solr version. For more information, see Upgrading Solr Version. You can also refer to the Solr Version Validity
Policy to understand how long the Solr minor versions will be available on the Cloud portal.

 Note
We encourage you to upgrade to Solr 9 at your earliest convenience, see Solr Upgrades.

Upgrading to 2211-jdk21.5
There are upgrade steps. Apply the relevant steps to your custom code.

 Caution
Important Notice: Password Handling Issue
Affected Customers: Customers running Update Release 2211-jdk21.5 who have not migrated from deprecated password hashing algorithms.
Issue: Users with passwords still hashed using removed algorithms cannot login, but the password reset functionality fails due to trying to read the old hash. This affects users whose passwords
have not been re-encoded with supported algorithms (Argon2, bcrypt, or scrypt).
Recommended Actions:
For customers currently on version 2211-jdk21.5:
Wait for Update Release 2211-jdk21.6, which includes a fix for the password reset flow to allow affected users to reset their password and log in after completing the password reset. The
fix also enables automatic password rehashing by default (with the password.encoding.auto.update.enabled property set to true).
Upgrade to 2211-jdk21.6 immediately upon release.
For customers planning to upgrade:
Upgrade to 2211-jdk21.6 immediately upon release.
Consider issuing communication to users with passwords still hashed using deprecated algorithms that password reset will be required.

 Note
An unexpected infinite loop issue may occur if you use two containers that contain identical products or categories to configure your promotion rule for Buy X Get X Discount/Free scenarios.
For more information, see Containers Best Practice for Buy X Get X Discount/Free.
To avoid such infinite loop issues, the constraint PromotionSourceRuleConditionConstraint is implemented as itemType to display a warning message in the Backoffice when two
containers with identical products or categories are detected. This constraint is deactivated by default. For more information, see Configuring Containers with Identical Products or Categories
Detection.

Apache Tomcat has been upgraded to 10.1.48 to ensure improved security. For more information, see Third-Party Compatibility.
The minimum password length has been increased to 8 for password validation when registering customers through the OCC API.
The customer coupon value resolver in the customercouponservices extension has been optimized by implementing query result caching for root categories. This removes redundant
database queries that previously occurred for each product-category combination during indexer jobs, improving indexer performance and reducing database load.
The Flot 0.8.3 and Flot Tooltip 0.9.0 libraries have been removed from the hac extension. The charts in the Administration Console have been updated to utilize Chart.js instead. To maintain
a consistent display with the Administration Console, update any charts in your custom web applications that you've created based on the hac extension to use Chart.js.
Additionally, as part of this change, Chart.js has been upgraded from 2.9.4 to 4.5.0. Analyze the Chart.js migration guide for any changes that could affect your custom code. For more
information, see 4.x Migration Guide

.

The XSSFilter has been deprecated as it's not a reliable or complete defense against XSS attacks and should not be used as the sole protection mechanism. Output encoding and input
validation are the recommended and sustainable methods to defend against XSS attacks. You should always apply these measures in your custom code, ideally through frameworks that
support such practices, such as ZK or Spring. SAP Commerce Cloud also offers tools tailored for this purpose, such as The XSS Encoder. The header injection feature will remain fully
supported until an alternative solution is provided.
We have addressed a security vulnerability in CodeMirror 5.65.18 that affected the mode/markdown/markdown.js component. The vulnerability involves a regular expression denial-ofservice (ReDoS) attack that could cause application freezing or significant performance degradation.
To mitigate this security risk, we have removed multiple language modes from the CodeMirror library in the hac extension, retaining only the following four essential modes:

clike
groovy
javascript
sql
All other language modes (including the vulnerable markdown mode) have been removed from the package.
For a complete list of over 100 removed language modes, expand the section below:

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

If you want to use the hac extension with CodeMirror library modes other than the four retained modes listed above, add them back manually to the extension:
Option 1: Add Full CodeMirror via WebJars
Add the complete CodeMirror library to your extension's external-dependencies.xml:
<dependency>
<groupId>org.webjars.npm</groupId>
<artifactId>codemirror</artifactId>
<version>5.65.20</version>
</dependency>

 Caution
The full CodeMirror 5.65.20 version still contains the vulnerability in markdown mode. Use this option only if you do not use markdown mode or have implemented additional security
measures.

Option 2: Add Specific Modes Manually
For better security, add only the specific modes you need:
1. Place the required mode files in your hac/resources/static context.
2. Update all references in your code to point to the new location of the added modes.

 Example
<!-- Before -->
<script type="text/javascript" src="/webjars/codemirror/mode/yaml/yaml.js"></script>
<!-- After -->
<script type="text/javascript" src="/static/codemirror/mode/yaml/yaml.js"></script>

Updated Properties
The following properties were updated to add more configurations for HTTP pool and connections:

ccAdapter.http.pool.maxTotal=100
The maximum total number of connections that can be created in the connection pool.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

39

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
ccAdapter.http.pool.maxPerRoute=80
The maximum total number of connections allowed per route.

ccAdapter.http.connection.socketTimeout=10000
#Socket timeout in milliseconds. It's the maximum time to wait for data after the connection is established.

ccAdapter.http.connection.requestTimeout=5000
Request timeout in milliseconds. It's the maximum time to wait for a connection from the connection pool.

ccAdapter.http.connection.evictIdleTime=30000
Idle connection eviction time in milliseconds. The connection pool will automatically close idle connections that haven't been used for longer than this time.

ccAdapter.http.connection.timeout=5000
Connection timeout in milliseconds. It's the maximum time to wait when attempting to establish a connection with the server.

Deprecations
The Injector.get method, which accepts a generic any type for the token parameter, has been deprecated. You're encouraged to use ProviderToken<T> instead. If you're using these
tokens, please replace them as the following code shows.
Previously, you could get these tokens with string parameters like these ones:
this.injector.get('SSO_CLIENT_ID');
this.injector.get('SSO_AUTHENTICATION_ENTRY_POINT');
this.injector.get('SSO_LOGOUT_ENTRY_POINT');
this.injector.get('SSO_OAUTH2_AUTHENTICATION_ENTRY_POINT');
Please replace them with the following code:
import {
SSO_CLIENT_ID_TOKEN,
SSO_LOGOUT_ENTRY_POINT_TOKEN,
SSO_AUTHENTICATION_ENTRY_POINT_TOKEN,
SSO_OAUTH2_AUTHENTICATION_ENTRY_POINT_TOKEN
} from 'smarteditcommons';
// some code ....
this.injector.get(SSO_CLIENT_ID_TOKEN)
this.injector.get(SSO_AUTHENTICATION_ENTRY_POINT_TOKEN);
this.injector.get(SSO_LOGOUT_ENTRY_POINT_TOKEN);
this.injector.get(SSO_OAUTH2_AUTHENTICATION_ENTRY_POINT_TOKEN);

APP_INITIALIZER is deprecated in the Angular framework. We use provideAppInitializer to replace APP_INITIALIZER in the moduleUtils.initialize function, which wrapped

provideAppInitializer in SmartEdit.
After the replacement, if you're using APP_INITIALIZER and moduleUtils.initialize at the same time, it might cause an angular dependency injector error. Instead, please use

moduleUtils.initialize in custom SmartEdit applications to replace APP_INITIALIZER. Alternatively, you can use provideAppInitializer directly.

The findIndexTypeId() method that returns the product index type ID as a String is deprecated. Use the findIndexType() method instead. This method returns a

SnIndexTypeModel object. You can then call getId() on the returned object to retrieve the index type ID.
// Old approach (deprecated)
String indexTypeId = findIndexTypeId();
// New approach
SnIndexTypeModel indexType = findIndexType();
String indexTypeId = indexType.getId();
We've enhanced the buildBreadcrumbs() method to support category filter breadcrumbs. The method now accepts an additional SnSearchQuery parameter that provides the
necessary context for building comprehensive breadcrumb navigation. Update your code to use the new three-parameter version buildBreadcrumbs(SolrSearchQueryData,

List, SnSearchQuery) instead.
// Old approach (deprecated)
List<BreadcrumbData<SolrSearchQueryData>> breadcrumbs = buildBreadcrumbs(searchQueryData, facets);
// New approach
List<BreadcrumbData<SolrSearchQueryData>> breadcrumbs = buildBreadcrumbs(searchQueryData, facets, searchQuery);
The getFacetSearchConfig() method that retrieves the FacetSearchConfig for the current context is deprecated. You no longer need to call this method separately. We
incorporated its logic directly into the populate (SearchQueryPageableData, SolrSearchRequest) method to improve code clarity and reduce method call overhead. If you were
using this method, review your implementation and use the populate() method instead.

Updating Custom SmartEdit Extension
Some front-end dependencies have been updated, and they require some library updates if you have a custom SmartEdit extension.

Procedure
Update the libraries with the following command:

ant upgradeCustomSmartEdit -Dscript=dependency -DextPath=$PATH_TO_CUSTOM_SMARTEDIT_EXTENSION

Upgrading to DataTables 2.3.2 and DataTables Buttons 3.2.5
The DataTables and DataTables Buttons libraries have been upgraded to 2.3.2 and 3.2.5 respectively. Carry out the necessary upgrade steps to ensure a smooth upgrade to the new versions of
these libraries.

Context
To improve security, the DataTables library has been upgraded from 1.12.1 to 2.3.2. Additionally, the DataTables Buttons library has been upgraded from 2.2.2 to 3.2.5. Carry out the following steps
to adjust your custom code to the new versions of DataTables and DataTables Buttons.

Procedure
1. To ensure that the web applications created with your custom extensions based on the hac extension have a consistent display with the Administration Console, add the stripe and
cell-border classes to any elements in your JSP and CSS files that you've enhanced with the DataTables library.
<table id="customTable" class="stripe cell-border">
</table>
2. Study the DataTables 2.3.2 and DataTables Buttons 3.2.5 migration guides for any possible changes that could affect your custom code. For more information, see Upgrading to DataTables
2 from 1.10+
and Buttons 3.0.0 .

Replacing Features from the Removed Apache Commons Validator
Apache Commons Validator library has been removed from SAP Commerce Cloud due to incompatibility with other Apache Commons libraries. Carry out the necessary upgrade steps to ensure
that this change doesn't affect your custom implementations.

Context
This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

41

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
The Apache Commons Validator library has been removed from SAP Commerce Cloud. Upgrading to a newer version wasn't feasible because the latest Commons Validator release is incompatible
with other Apache Commons libraries, specifically Commons BeanUtils, that were updated in the 2211-jdk21.1 release.
If your project code uses this library, you need to implement alternative validation methods for strings, e-mails, URLs, and other data types. If your project includes customizations in a copied
template module, inspect your source code for any instances of the Apache Commons Validator library.

Procedure
1. Replace usages of GenericValidator.isBlankOrNull with Apache Commons StringUtils.isBlank, or use standard language features of Java.
/* before */
import org.apache.commons.validator.GenericValidator;
if (GenericValidator.isBlankOrNull(myString))
{
// handle blank or null string
}
/* after */
import org.apache.commons.lang3.StringUtils;
if (StringUtils.isBlank(myString))
{
// handle blank or null string
}
2. You can handle most e-mail address validation scenarios through a regular expression. The Platform provides a basic e-mail validator,
de.hybris.platform.validator.EmailValidator, that is based on the regular expression provided by OWASP. This validator also rejects e-mail addresses using local domains,
such as localhost or localdomain. For more validation options, see Email Validation in Java .
3. You can handle many URL validation scenarios by checking for correctness when creating an URI from a String value, and then verifying that specific elements, such as scheme and ports,
are correct. You may also choose to convert the URI to a URL for additional validation, based on your specific requirements.
import java.net.URI;
final URI uri;
try
{
uri = new URI(value);
}
catch (final URISyntaxException ex)
{
return false;
}
// provide additional validation of URI elements here

Related Information
Commons Validator

Upgrading Custom Data Hub Extensions
Migrate custom Data Hub extensions to support JDK 21 and Spring 6.

Prerequisites
To successfully perform the migration, please have the following:
Access to the source code of custom Data Hub extensions
A development environment configured for working with Maven projects

Procedure
1. Configure the OpenRewrite Maven plugin. For migration, SAP Commerce Cloud provides a special set of code transformation rules (recipes) packaged in a JAR file. Download this file and
connect it locally.
a. Locate and download the JAR file sap-commerce-framework-update-recipes-1.X.X.jar from the attachments section of 3618495

. Save this file in an accessible

location in your project, for example, in the library directory at the project root.
b. Configure the plugin in pom.xml. This configuration activates the plugin and specifies the recipe to use for migrating to JDK 21 and Spring 6. To configure it, open the root pom.xml
of your Data Hub project, and add the rewrite-maven-plugin to the <build> section. For example:

 Note
In the configuration below, replace 1.X.X with the actual version number of the file you downloaded, for example, 1.1.1, and only use the official OpenRewrite Maven plugin with
the artifactId rewrite-maven-plugin. Do not confuse it with the commercial plugin io.moderne:rewrite-maven-plugin, or use the incorrect name openrewrite-

maven-plugin, which does not exist in the Maven Central repository.
Additionally, please use the exact versions specified in the configuration below (rewrite-maven-plugin:6.0.3, rewrite-spring:5.24.1, rewrite-migrate-java:2.30.1). Newer versions of
the OpenRewrite plugin may cause build failures (NullPointerException) when processing Data Hub-specific XML configurations due to missing cache regions that exist in
Commerce but not in Data Hub.

<build>
<plugins>
...
<plugin>
<groupId>org.openrewrite.maven</groupId>
<artifactId>rewrite-maven-plugin</artifactId>
<version>6.0.3</version> <!-- Downgraded version for Datahub compatibility -->
<configuration>

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

42

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
<activeRecipes>
<!-- Main recipe for SAP Commerce migration -->
<recipe>com.sap.cx.rewrite.java.spring.CommerceCloudJdk21AndSpring6Update</recipe>
</activeRecipes>
</configuration>
<dependencies>
<!-- Dependency containing SAP recipes -->
<dependency>
<groupId>com.sap.commerce.platform</groupId>
<artifactId>platform-rewrite-recipes</artifactId>
<version>1.X.X</version> <!-- Replace with the actual downloaded version -->
<scope>system</scope>
<systemPath>${project.basedir}/lib/sap-commerce-framework-update-recipes-1.X.X.jar</systemPath> <!-- Ensure th
</dependency>
<!-- Additional standard OpenRewrite dependencies -->
<dependency>
<groupId>org.openrewrite.recipe</groupId>
<artifactId>rewrite-spring</artifactId>
<version>5.24.1</version> <!-- Specific version required to avoid NPE in Datahub -->
</dependency>
<dependency>
<groupId>org.openrewrite.recipe</groupId>
<artifactId>rewrite-migrate-java</artifactId>
<version>2.30.1</version> <!-- Specific version required to avoid NPE in Datahub -->
</dependency>
</dependencies>
</plugin>
...
</plugins>
</build>
2. Remove the @Required annotation since Spring 6 does not support it. To automate the removal process, do the following:
a. In the <configuration> section of the plugin added in Step 1, specify the recipe org.openrewrite.java.spring.RemoveSpringRequired.
<configuration>
<activeRecipes>
<recipe>org.openrewrite.java.spring.RemoveSpringRequired</recipe>
</activeRecipes>
</configuration>
b. If necessaey, configure access to SAP repositories. Some recipes or their dependencies may be located in an internal SAP repository. Ensure that your Maven is configured for
authentication by adding a server configuration to your ~/.m2/settings.xml file.
c. Run the plugin. Open a terminal in the root directory of your Maven project (where the main pom.xml file is located) and execute the following command: mvn rewrite:run.
3. Manually update dependencies and plugins. Update the versions of key dependencies and Maven plugins in the pom.xml files to ensure compatibility with JDK 21 and Spring 6.
a. Update versions of key libraries.

Library

Update to this Version

Spring Framework (including spring-core, spring-beans, spring-web, etc.)

6.2.2

Spring Security

6.4.2

Spring Integration

6.4.1

Spring Data JPA

3.4.2

hibernate-core

6.6.4

querydsl-jpa

5.1.0

jakarta.servlet-api

6.1.0

jakarta.persistence-api

3.2.0

activemq-*

6.1.5

jersey-bom

3.1.10

b. Update versions of Maven libraries.

Maven Library

Update to this Version

maven-compiler-plugin

3.13.0

maven-surefire-plugin

3.5.2

maven-failsafe-plugin

3.5.2

maven-war-plugin

3.4.0

4. Manually migrate namespaces from Javax to Jakarta. Automated OpenRewrite recipes for this task may perform incorrect import replacements, leading to compilation errors or hidden
runtime errors. To manually migrate namespaces, do the following:
a. Use the Search&Replace function in your IDE to control each modification of import statements.
b. Key packages for migration: javax.servlet.*, javax.persistence.*, javax.persistence.*.
5. Adapt code to API changes. After updating dependencies, you need to adapt the code of custom Data Hub extensions to changes in the APIs of the used frameworks. If you used
RequestHandlerRetryAdvice, you need to replace it with the standard class org.springframework.retry.interceptor.RetryOperationsInterceptor.
a. Adapt Java Code (transferr custom logic). If your old class, for example, MyCustomRetryAdvice, contains additional logic, create a new class to hold it. For example:
Before

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

43

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
// Old class that will no longer compile
public class MyCustomRetryAdvice extends RequestHandlerRetryAdvice {
// ... some custom logic
}
Create a new class that extends RetryTemplate and implements RetryListener. Transfer your logic to the methods of this listener, for example, onRetry, onError, and so
on.
After
// New class for custom logic
public class MyCustomRetryTemplate extends RetryTemplate implements RetryListener {
// ... your custom logic from ...RetryAdvice is now here,
// in the methods of the RetryListener interface, for example:
@Override
public <T, E extends Throwable> void onError(RetryContext context, RetryCallback<T, E> callback, Throwable throwable) {
// Logging or other logic on error
}
}
b. Update the spring XML configuration. Reconfigure your XML file to use the new custom class MyCustomRetryTemplate. For example:
Before
<alias name="defaultConsumerRetryAdvice" alias="consumerRetryAdvice" />
<bean id="defaultConsumerRetryAdvice" class="com.hybris.datahub.jms.ConsumerRetryAdvice">
<property name="retryTemplate" ref="publishBatchRetryTemplate" />
</bean>
<int:service-activator ...>
<int:request-handler-advice-chain>
<ref bean="consumerRetryAdvice" />
</int:request-handler-advice-chain>
</int:service-activator>
After
<!-- 1. The old 'consumerRetryAdvice' bean is completely removed. -->
<!-- 2. A new standard interceptor is created. -->
<bean id="retryInterceptor" class="org.springframework.retry.interceptor.RetryOperationsInterceptor">
<!-- 3. A reference to our RetryTemplate is specified. -->
<property name="retryOperations" ref="publishBatchRetryTemplate" />
</bean>
<!-- 4. The 'publishBatchRetryTemplate' bean now refers to our new class with custom logic. -->
<bean id="publishBatchRetryTemplate" class="com.hybris.datahub.jms.ConsumerRetryTemplate">
<!-- ... your retry policy settings (backOffPolicy, retryPolicy, etc.) remain here ... -->
</bean>
<int:service-activator ...>
<int:request-handler-advice-chain>
<!-- 5. The reference now points to the new 'retryInterceptor'. -->
<ref bean="retryInterceptor" />
</int:request-handler-advice-chain>
</int:service-activator>
c. Verify changes to HTTP response status texts. Due to library updates, status reason phrases might have changed. For example, for status 500, the text changed from "Internal

Server Error" to "Server Error". Verify these strings in your code, especially in tests, and make any necessary updates.
d. Additional API Changes to be aware of.
Changes in Spring integration. The .get() method in IntegrationFlows has been replaced with .getObject().
Before
import org.springframework.integration.dsl.IntegrationFlows;
return IntegrationFlows.from("someChannel").get();
After
import org.springframework.integration.dsl.IntegrationFlow;
return IntegrationFlow.from("someChannel").getObject();
Changes in QueryDSL. The type returned by methods for creating subqueries has changed from JPQLQuery to JPQLSubQuery.
Before
final JPQLQuery<DataHubPoolEntity> pendingActionSubQuery = createPendingActionSubQuery(...);
After
final JPQLSubQuery<DataHubPoolEntity> pendingActionSubQuery = createPendingActionSubQuery(...);
Changes in the Hibernate Statistics API. Methods for accessing statistics have been modified.
Before
import org.hibernate.stat.SecondLevelCacheStatistics;
SecondLevelCacheStatistics stats = statistics.getSecondLevelCacheStatistics(s);
After
import org.hibernate.stat.CacheRegionStatistics;
CacheRegionStatistics stats = statistics.getDomainDataRegionStatistics(s);
6. Adapt your test code. Adapting test code is a significant part of the migration, as Spring Test, Mockito, and JUnit have been updated. You should focus on updating the following key areas:

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

44

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
Spring Security configuration in tests. With the transition to Spring 6, the way security is loaded and configured has changed. XML security configurations (<http> ... </http>)
require significant adaptation. It may be necessary for you to switch to Java-based configuration using SecurityFilterChain for tests to work correctly.

 Note
It is best to review all custom *-security spring.xml files in your project as any changes can also affect the main application configuration.
Transition to JUnit 5. Although not strictly required for compilation, Spring Framework 6 provides native and significantly improved support for JUnit 5. Migrating from JUnit 4 to
JUnit 5 is a best practice to ensure stability and leverage the full benefits of Spring’s new testing infrastructure. This includes replacing annotations (@Before) to (@BeforeEach),
updating the handling of expected exceptions, and using the new Assertions API.
Preserving constructor parameter names. If your XML bean configurations use autowiring by constructor parameter name, add the -parameters flag to the maven-compiler-

plugin configuration. This preserves parameter names in the bytecode allowing Spring to correctly inject dependencies. For example:
<plugin>
<groupId>org.apache.maven.plugins</groupId>
<artifactId>maven-compiler-plugin</artifactId>
<configuration>
<parameters>true</parameters>
</configuration>
</plugin>
This approach is a pragmatic solution for supporting existing legacy code and ensuring backwards compatibility compared to type-based injection or explicit annotations, for
example, (@Qualifier).

 Note
Be prepared to address specific issues, such as changes in constructor argument order that Spring may now resolve incorrectly, or adaptations to new versions of Mockito.

Implementing a Fixed Issue
There are additional steps to implement some fixed issues.

Features in Rollout Phases
There are new features and some previously released features reached a new phase. There are new default API endpoint configurations.
As part of the continuous innovation strategy, some features are delivered in a phased approach.
For more information about the rollout phases and the relevant features, refer to Feature Rollout Phases.

Activating New Features
There are new features that you must activate to use.
Deactivating Features
If you do not want to implement a new feature you recently activated or a previously released feature that is now activated by default, perform the required steps to deactivate it.
Overriding Default API Endpoint Configuration
The deactivated by default endpoints that were released in 2211.32 are now activated by default. If you have previously added API endpoints to a configuration property in your
manifest.json file, the factory default configuration may be overridden by your custom configuration, and you may want to make adjustments.

Activating New Features
There are new features that you must activate to use.
In future releases, these new features will become activated by default but remain configurable, and then in the final phase, they will be delivered as standard features. It is recommended that you
implement the features before they are activated by default so that you can prepare and test them. For more information about the timeline and strategy, refer to Feature Rollout Phases.

Activating Quote Performance Improvement
You can skip the quote validation process during cart operations, which can help improve response times in B2C scenarios. This improvement does not affect B2B scenarios.
Activating Purchase Order Number in Quote Creation
You can add a purchase order number during quote creation in SAP Commerce Cloud system.This feature gives the buyer the flexibility to enter the purchase order number if it is already
known at the time of the quote creation process.
Activating Consent Management and Profile Tracking for B2B
You can now enable the consent management and profile tracking for B2B scenarios.
Activating Concurrency in Add to Cart
You can now prevent concurrency issue when same product is added multiple times resulting in a total price of $0. This also ensures accurate recalculation of the cart for each new entry.

Activating Quote Performance Improvement
You can skip the quote validation process during cart operations, which can help improve response times in B2C scenarios. This improvement does not affect B2B scenarios.

Prerequisites
Ensure that you have not enabled any quote functionality in your B2C workflows.

Procedure
This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

"value": "true"

You can add a purchase order number during quote creation in SAP Commerce Cloud system.This feature gives the buyer the flexibility to enter the purchase order number if it is already known at
the time of the quote creation process.

Procedure
To activate this feature, add the following key and value to the properties list in the manifest.json file:
"properties": [
{
...,
"key": "toggle.sapPurchaseOrderNumber.enabled",
"value": "true"
}
]

Activating Consent Management and Profile Tracking for B2B
You can now enable the consent management and profile tracking for B2B scenarios.

Procedure
To activate this feature, add the following key and value to the properties list in the manifest.json file:

"properties": [
{
"key": "toggle.b2bcustomer.consentManagement.enabled",
"value": "true"
},
{
"key": "toggle.b2bcustomer.produceRegisterEvent.enabled",
"value": "true"
},
{
"key": "toggle.b2bcustomer.produceSubmitOrderEvent.enabled",
"value": "true"
}
]

Activating Concurrency in Add to Cart
You can now prevent concurrency issue when same product is added multiple times resulting in a total price of $0. This also ensures accurate recalculation of the cart for each new entry.

Procedure
To activate this feature, add the following key and value to the properties list in the manifest.json file:

"properties": [
{
...,
"key": "toggle.enhanceConcurrencyCartForMerge.enabled",
"value": "true"
}
]

New Features in this Release
If you activate a new feature from this release and then decide that you don't want to implement it after all, you can deactivate it. Even though you are able to deactivate it now, you still need to plan
and prepare for the next rollout phases.
In future releases, these new features will become activated by default but remain configurable, and then in the final phase, they will be delivered as standard features. It is recommended that you
implement the features before they are activated by default so that you can prepare and test them. For more information about the timeline and strategy, refer to Feature Rollout Phases.

Features now Activated by Default
If you do not want to use a feature that was initially deactivated in 2211.16 and is now activated by default, you can deactivate it. If you deactivate it now, you may have less time to prepare and test
the feature before it is available out-of-the-box in the final rollout phase.

The deactivated by default endpoints that were released in 2211.32 are now activated by default. If you have previously added API endpoints to a configuration property in your manifest.json

Context

your desired setup.

Upgrading to 2211-jdk21.4
There are maintenance changes, such as bug fixes, that may require you to update your custom code.

Potential Breaking Changes
The samlKeystore.jks file that was previously provided with SAP Commerce Cloud for SAML SSO test purposes has been removed. For information on how to create your own

samlKeystore.jks file, see Configuring SAP Commerce Cloud.

 Note
If you don't provide a keystore in your configuration, the system starts as usual. However, a warning is logged indicating that SSO will not function correctly. Any attempt to use the

samlsinglesignon extension will redirect users to a blank page displaying a misconfiguration warning.
SmartEdit has introduced a Rush lockfile that improves determinism and security without impacting current SmartEdit builds. If you need to manually change the Rush version, see
SmartEdit Rush Version Control with Lockfile.

Implementing a Fixed Issue
There are additional steps to implement some fixed issues.

Fixing Issues with Concurrency Issues When Customers Simultaneously Add Products to Cart Bundle
The configurablebundlefacades OCC APIs now include locking mechanisms to prevent concurrency issues when multiple requests are made to add products to the same cart.
Fixing Issue with Promotion Discount Calculation

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

51

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
The promotion discount calculation error which occurs for some scenarios has been fixed.

Fixing Issues with Concurrency Issues When Customers Simultaneously Add Products to Cart
Bundle
The configurablebundlefacades OCC APIs now include locking mechanisms to prevent concurrency issues when multiple requests are made to add products to the same cart.

Context
The configurablebundlefacades API previously faced concurrency issues, generating duplicate entry numbers when multiple requests were made simultaneously to add products to the same cart.
When customers added a new entry without specifying an entry number, the system automatically placed it at the end. It counted the number of available entries in the cart. However, the system
didn't secure this logic when determining the entry number. If two or more actions occurred simultaneously, a concurrency issue occurred.
To resolve this issue, synchronized and optimistic locking mechanisms are added to prevent concurrency problems when adding products to cart bundle.
Synchronized locking processes requests sequentially. When multiple requests hit the API simultaneously, they queue up, allowing each request to be processed one after the other. This approach
ensures that no two requests interfere with each other, maintaining the integrity of cart data.
Optimistic locking works when requests are distributed across multiple instances. It assumes that conflicts are rare and allows multiple requests to proceed without locking resources. However, if a
conflict occurs, such as when the cart is modified by another request on a different instance, a 409 error is triggered. This error informs customers that their cart has been modified elsewhere,
prompting them to retry their action.

Procedure
This feature is deactivated by default. To activate it, set the value to true for property configurablebundlefacades.addToCartInOptimisticLockMode.

Fixing Issue with Promotion Discount Calculation
The promotion discount calculation error which occurs for some scenarios has been fixed.

Context
Based on the currency, for some scenarios, the rounding loss issue in promotion discount calculations can be avoided by enabling internal scale calculation.

Procedure
To enable internal scale calculation, set ordercalculation.calculate.internal.scale.enabled to true.

Update Release 2211-jdk21.1
The September 2025 framework update brings important changes such as an upgrade to JDK 21 and Spring 6. Additionally, some deprecated extensions are removed.
To improve security and performance and provide the latest, future-proof technology, this update release introduces a framework update that includes the following major changes:
Upgrade from Java 17 to Java 21 and Spring 5 to 6
OAuth2 replaced with the Spring Authorization Server framework, which introduces new extensions
Removal of the deprecated cockpit-related extensions
Removal of the deprecated amazoncloud extensions
Upgrade of dependent third-party libraries and components
