Known Issues
In the 2211.42 update release, the Microsoft JDBC Driver for SQL Server has been updated to version 12.10.0, which introduces automatic spacing for prepared SQL parameter names. This could
potentially lead to the regeneration of database query plans. For more details on the issue, see 3679180

.

Framework
In Spring Framework 6, the transition has been made from using the javax.annotation package to the jakarta.annotation package as part of aligning with the Jakarta EE 9+
specifications. The annotations have been updated from javax.annotation:javax.annotation-api:1.3.2 to jakarta.annotation:jakarta.annotation-api:3.0.0
to avoid issues such as @Resource and @PostConstruct not working in javax.annotation-api.
The following deprecated classes have been removed:

org.appformer.maven.support.PomModel
org.drools.compiler.kproject.ReleaseIdImpl
org.drools.core.command.runtime.rule.FireAllRulesCommand
org.drools.core.definitions.rule.impl.RuleImpl
In the cmsocc-beans.xml and cmsoccaddon-beans.xml files, the package name javax.xml.bind.annotation.* has been changed to jakarta.xml.bind.annotation.*.
The de.hybris.platform.previewwebservices.controllers.PreviewController.java file has been modified:
Before:
public PreviewTicketWsDTO updatePreviewTicket
After:
public ResponseEntity<PreviewTicketWsDTO> updatePreviewTicket
The return value of updatePreviewTicket has been wrapped with ResponseEntity.
The *Controller.java file in the de.hybris.platform.personalizationwebservices.controllers package has been modified. The return values of all API functions have
been wrapped with ResponseEntity.

Extensions
Prepare for the removal of the amazoncloud extension from SAP Commerce Cloud.
After the deprecation announcement in December, the amazoncloud extension is now removed with this version of SAP Commerce Cloud and it will no longer be a part of the installer. In
case you still need to use this extension, see 3594005

: Removal of amazoncloud Extension. There you will find the source code and all required information to be used at your own

discretion but without SAP support or guarantees.

 Remember
SAP will no longer provide support for amazoncloud extension in SAP Commerce Cloud.
As part of the Integration API at-least-once-delivery (ALOD) feature, the integrationservices extension imports a series of Azure Spring libraries. One of the transitive dependencies
required for Azure Identity is msal4j, which is used internally during runtime by Azure Identity. Version 1.17.1 of the msal4j library brings in further transitive dependencies, some of which do
not match the versions that SAP Commerce Cloud explicitly includes. For this reason, even though msal4j is present when including the Integration API outboundservices extension, we
recommend not using this library in any custom code to prevent the potential for code incompatibilities.

Security
An unexpected infinite loop issue may occur if you use two containers that contain identical products or categories to configure your promotion rule for Buy X Get X Discount/Free
scenarios. For more information, see Containers Best Practice for Buy X Get X Discount/Free.
To avoid such infinite loop issues, the constraint PromotionSourceRuleConditionConstraint is implemented as itemType to display a warning message in the Backoffice when two
containers with identical products or categories are detected. This constraint is deactivated by default. For more information, see Configuring Containers with Identical Products or
Categories Detection.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

81

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
We've enhanced the DBAudit logging mechanism to correctly handle operation types when generic audit is disabled.
Previously, when generic audit was disabled, DBAudit logging could incorrectly compute the type of operation for certain database transactions. This issue was particularly noticeable in
scenarios where an object was created and deleted within the same transaction. The system would sometimes generate inaccurate or redundant audit entries, potentially leading to
confusion in audit trails related to false positives.
The fix focuses on improving the behavior of the AuditableChange.calculateAuditType method when working with the LazySLDDataContainer. As a result, the system now
correctly identifies and logs the appropriate operation type (create, update, or delete) for database transactions. Audit logs are more reliable as object creation and deletion within the same
transaction are properly handled.

 Note
Duplicate audit log entries may still occur when two transactions try to delete the same item from the database simultaneously. In such cases, even though only one transaction
successfully deletes the item, both transactions might log the deletion.
Some customers faced an issue when users without a password tried to log in to the system through Single Sign-On (SSO). Despite successful SSO authentication, it was not possible for
the affected users to log in through Backoffice or the Administration Console. The system returned “Access Denied” error and failed to proceed without logging any exceptions. The problem
happened when the user did not have an encoded password set, although the existence of a password should have been irrelevant for SSO access.
The SSO login issue has been resolved by removing redundant system attempts to encode plain text passwords and perform checks against them. Token-based authentication has been
refined so that it's possible to determine if a login token is valid based on a password in the user profile.
As a result, users can now log in successfully using their SSO credentials regardless of encoder settings.

 Note
To ensure the fix works as intended, check if the following setting is enabled in your local.properties file: login.token.extended=true.
Some customers might have experienced issues with Single Sign-On (SSO) login. The problem manifested as an infinite redirect loop in Backoffice, SmartEdit, and Administration Console
interfaces as the LoginToken cookie was impossible to store.
The reason behind the issue was the system using the legacy encoder specified for the user account while generating the SSO token. The system returned a corresponding

EJBPasswordEncoderDeprecatedException even when customers had configured a newer encoding method, such as Argon2, in the user.passwordEncoding property, and
kept the legacy.password.encoding.enabled flag set to false.
We've updated the SSO login flow to respect the configured password encoding method for login tokens. The system now only uses the value specified in the dedicated

login.token.encoder property.
The user's password encoding method stored in the user.passwordEncoding property is no longer part of the SSO login process. Ultimately, the change ensures that the SSO process
uses the correct, up-to-date password hashing algorithms, avoiding conflicts with legacy encoders, so customers can benefit from the latest security improvements.
We've enhanced OAuth 2.0 implementation by adding support for Demonstrating Proof-of-Possession (DPoP) tokens through the addition of DPOP("DPOP",

OAuth2AccessToken.TokenType.DPOP). In this way, we have ensured stronger security for OAuth 2.0 flows by requiring clients to prove possession of a private key, helping prevent
token theft and replay attacks.
The value of the xss.filter.rule.eval property has been changed to strengthen the security of the XSS filters.
To address a security vulnerability in Apache Commons FileUpload, the vulnerable commons-fileupload2-jakarta (version 2.0.0-M1) library has been removed from the Platform.
If this change impacts your environment and you require the library, you need to re-add it manually.

Testing
We have removed the EasyMock Class Extension module, which is now part of the core EasyMock library. The system now uses the standard EasyMock imports instead of the class
extension-specific imports.
This change modernizes the code base by removing a deprecated module and using the up-to-date EasyMock library. As a result, you can benefit from improved maintainability in your
testing infrastructure. Additionally, this change reduces the complexity of the project's dependencies, making it easier to manage and update in the future.

Upgrades, Removals, and Deprecations
The deprecated CS cockpit web directory has been removed from the cissubscription extension.

hybris/bin/modules/subscriptions/cissubscription/web
The type of the attribute paymentType in AbstractOrderWsDTO has been refactored from a data type to a WsDTO type.
Before:
<property name="paymentType" type="de.hybris.platform.b2bacceleratorfacades.order.data.B2BPaymentTypeData"/>
After:
<property name="paymentType" type="de.hybris.platform.b2bwebservicescommons.dto.order.B2BPaymentTypeWsDTO"/>
The HttpUnit library is no longer used, as it has reached its end-of-life. Review your SAP Commerce Cloud implementation to see if this removal impacts your code base.

Framework Update - Java JDK 21 and Spring 6.2
SAP Commerce Cloud has been updated to leverage Java JDK 21 and Spring Framework 6.2, bringing the platform in line with modern industry standards but requiring adjustments to project
configurations and custom extensions. To simplify the update, it’s recommended to use the OpenRewrite recipes to automatically handle most common changes. Despite the provided automation,
manual code review and updates are necessary to complete the update process.
With the new version of the SAP Commerce Cloud, the product has been updated to a newer version of Java with long-term support. Spring Framework has also been updated to the next major
version. Both Java and Spring are fundamental components within SAP Commerce Cloud. This change allows us to keep up to date with industry standards, maintain continuous innovation and

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

82

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
stay current with the overall Java-based ecosystem. This major technical update comes with changes that require adjustments to your project configuration and custom extensions, for example,
update from javax.* to jakarta.* namespace, or changes in OAuth that are described in-depth in Moving to the New OAuth Implementation. The scope of the required changes and the number of
applicable upgrade steps may differ depending on your project configuration and custom extensions within it.
You can adapt to these changes in one of the two following ways:
In a partially automated way, leveraging the OSS OpenRewrite recipes.
Fully manually following all update steps and additional changes made by the update recipes within the OpenRewrite recipes.
The suggested approach is to consider using the first option, leveraging the OpenRewrite recipes, to smooth the update and reduce the overall complexity. For more information about
OpenRewrite, visit https://docs.openrewrite.org/

.

Update with the Help of the OpenRewrite Recipes
This approach reduces the efforts related to the update to JDK21 and Spring Framework 6.2, thanks to the usage of the recipes and OpenRewrite tool, partially automating required adjustments.
This is the recommended approach and we suggest using it on your project to make the update experience easier.
To learn how to use and run the OpenRewrite recipes related to the Java and Spring Framework update, see 3618495

: Using OpenRewrite recipes to support SAP Commerce Cloud JDK21

Framework Update adoption.
Keep in mind that automated changes made with the help of OpenRewrite and provided recipes may not be sufficient for your given project and custom code. Recipes target the most common
cases found by SAP developers working on the SAP Commerce Cloud code base, and by the OSS community working on multiple Java projects and performing similar technical updates. Some of
the specific cases may still require manual adjustments and closer review from the developers of the given customer project.
Some of the places where the manual review or adjustment is needed will be marked with a comment starting with the following phrase:
FRAMEWORK_UPDATE - TODO (...)
This, however, isn't exhaustive. There may also be project-specific places unmarked with comments that automation didn't manage to identify and will also need your attention.

Fully Manual Update
This approach assumes that the suggested OpenRewrite recipes and update recipes aren't used for the technical update. This is a fully valid approach, but may come with additional cost and a less
smooth experience for the project developers.
For a fully manual update, we recommend reviewing the described update steps within the documentation. This list doesn't include steps that we found covered by the OpenRewrite update
described in the first approach. Therefore, we recommend reviewing the recipe tree that was part of the automation from the first approach to get a better understanding of all the changes. What
can also be useful are generally available update guides for Spring Framework, for example Upgrading to Spring Framework 6.x. x

and Java 21

.

For OpenRewrite, a recipe can consist of different recipes. The overall recipe list behind the update recipe is extensive and includes recipes created by SAP developers and the open-source
community. When reviewing the recipe tree content, be advised that not all recipes may be applicable or affect the code. Mere presence within the recipe tree doesn't mean that the recipe would
introduce changes to the particular project. This is highly dependent on the preconditions for a given recipe to be met within a project, for instance, presence/usage of a class within the project,
usage of a particular method that needs to be adjusted and so forth.
Based on that, it isn't feasible to present only recipes that modified the SAP Commerce Cloud source code and are part of the provided update recipe. To present the overall set of possible changes
we provide a full set of the recipe update tree that should be reviewed, see SAP Commerce Cloud Framework Update Recipe Tree.

 Note
Due to the extent of the report, it can't be provided directly within the documentation, but is shipped structured HTML file that allows checking the recipe name, description or pre-filled
parameters to provide general knowledge regarding the recipe, and possible changes that it could introduce.

3/9/26, 4:28 PM

Spring Framework 6.2.x
Review all manual steps related to Spring 6 update and adapt your SAP Commerce Cloud implementation accordingly.
1. Adapting to PathPatternParser New Default URL Matcher
Adapt your Spring application to use PathPatternParser, the new default URL matcher introduced in Spring 6.0, which replaces AntPathMatcher.
2. Adapting to Strict URL Matching
As of Spring Framework 6.0, the default behavior for matching trailing slash in URL paths has changed. The trailing slash matching configuration option has been deprecated and its default
value has been set to false.
3. Adjusting to jakarta.servlet.Filter API
With the SAP Commerce Cloud Framework Update, javax.servlet.Filter was updated to jakarta.servlet.Filter.
4. Using StandardServletMultipartResolver for Multipart Data
Prepare for StandardServletMultipartResolver usage in your SAP Commerce Cloud implementation after the removal of CommonsMultipartResolver that was used in Spring
versions prior to 6.1.
5. Updating spring-security-saml2-service-provider to 6.4.x
For compatibility reasons with Spring 6, the version of the spring-security-saml2-service-provider library version has been updated from 5.8.11 to 6.4.1.
6. Updating to SiteMesh 3.2.x
SiteMesh 3.0-alpha is not fully compatible with Jakarta EE 10 and was upgraded to version 3.2.1 with the Spring 6 update.
7. Adding Missing MVC Configuration in Web Application Context
Ensure Spring MVC and Security share the same web application context to avoid missing mvcHandlerMappingIntrospector bean issues introduced in Spring 6.x.
8. Adapting to Removal of the @Required Annotation
With Spring Framework 6 update, the @Required annotation is no longer used. If you decided to utilize the OpenRewrite recipe, all the invocations of @Required annotation were
automatically removed from the code.
9. Adapting codebase after removal of SocketUtils Class with Spring 6.X releases
Spring removed the deprecated org.springframework.util.SocketUtils class with 6.X releases.
10. Resolving BeanPostProcessorChecker Warnings
Adapt to new warning message logic introduced in BeanPostProcessorChecker with Spring Framework 6.
11. Configure Extension Load Order to Support Fixed Spring 6 Alias Overriding Behavior
Spring Framework 6 resolves inconsistencies in bean overriding, specifically involving conflicts between bean names and aliases.
12. Adapting to @TestExecutionListener Annotation Changes
Spring 6.0 changed how test listeners are registered in certain base classes. Some tests may need updates to keep the expected behavior when updating from earlier versions.
13. Replacing HttpPutFormContentFilter with FormContentFilter
If your extensions are generated from ycommercewebservices template, perform the following steps to replace HttpPutFormContentFilter with FormContentFilter.
14. Loading OCC Swagger Properties
If your extensions are generated from the ycommercewebservices template, perform the following steps to load OCC Swagger properties.
15. @ModelAttribute Annotation Changes
Spring provides a @ModelAttribute annotation that allows binding elements for the HTTP request to the model object.
16. Consider Removing Separate DispatcherServlet Context
When configuring a Spring web application, it's worth evaluating how servlet contexts are defined.
17. Integration 6.4.x Update
Spring integration version was updated from 5.5.20 to >= 6.4.1.
18. Parameter Name Retention for Dependency Injection
Spring framework now relies on Java and Groovy compilers to retain parameter names in bytecode for dependency injection, removing the need for bytecode parsing.
19. Resolving Redirection Issues of request-matcher
In Spring Security 6.x, the default policy of the request-matcher has been changed from AntPathRequestMatcher to MvcPathRequestMatcher, causing 302 redirections of
static resources.
20. Fixing "No visible WebSecurityExpressionHandler" Error
This document provides steps to resolve the java.io.IOException: No visible WebSecurityExpressionHandler instance could be found error when starting the
server, which occurs due to missing security expression handler configuration for JSP 'authorize' tags.
21. Updating Spring Security Intercept-URL Configuration for Empty Expression Strings
This document provides guidance on resolving the "expressionString cannot be empty" error during server startup by properly configuring intercept-url rules in Spring Security 6.
22. Optimizing SequenceSizeReleaseStrategy Configuration for Large Groups
This document provides steps to resolve performance warnings related to SequenceSizeReleaseStrategy by switching to the more
efficient SimpleSequenceSizeReleaseStrategy implementation.
23. Resolving DispatcherServlet Exceptions During Server Startup
Update the Spring MVC configuration to ensure compatibility with Spring 6 by explicitly defining the use of AntPathMatcher and setting the patternParser property to null for all
handler mapping beans.
24. Adding xxxMapping Annotation
Add annotation of xxxMapping to chineseaddressaddon, chinesepaymentaddon, chineselogisticaddon, and chineseprofileaddon to fix certain issues in cx_china
recipe.

Adapting to PathPatternParser New Default URL Matcher
Adapt your Spring application to use PathPatternParser, the new default URL matcher introduced in Spring 6.0, which replaces AntPathMatcher.

Prerequisites
Ensure that your application uses a subclass of AbstractHandlerMapping and review the Spring 5.3 announcement along with the Spring 6.0 release notes.
Verify that you have access to the configuration files (such as MVC XML files and Spring Security configurations) that need to be updated.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

84

3/9/26, 4:28 PM

Context
With the release of Spring 5.3, a new alternative URL Matcher, PathPatternParser, was introduced to replace the AntPathMatcher for performance reasons. From Spring 6.0 onwards,

PathPatternParser became the default parser, including in SAP Commerce Cloud. This change affects all beans that are subclasses of AbstractHandlerMapping. PathPatternParser
is not fully compatible with the AntPathMatcher, the incompatible cases are described here: Spring blog: PathPattern

.

Review your current URL mapping patterns for incompatibilities. For instance, check if multi-segment matching isn't specified as endpoint path fragment, except for the end of the path. Here's an
example of an invalid definition.
@RequestMapping(value = "/test/**/subpath")

Adjusting mapping patterns to be compatible with the new parser is the most optimal option going forward. However, if this isn't possible, you can restore the previous AntPathMatcher behavior.
For more information, jump to Restoring AntPathMatcher Usage.

 Note
In general, PathPatternParser is used as the default parser in SAP Commerce Cloud, following Spring 6's default behavior. However, for Accelerator UIs, AntPathMatcher was kept as the
default matcher, to support path formats that aren't supported by PathPatternParser, for example, containing multi-segment matching constructs like '**'. As a result, Accelerator UIs
(including newly provided templates) can still use paths in the old format.

Procedure
Decide on the approach to take:
Adjust the mapping patterns to work with PathPatternParser – by removing multi-segment matching constructs.
Restore the usage of AntPathMatcher for annotation-based configuration through explicit configuration changes.
This decision will determine the changes you need to implement in your configuration files and code. Then continue with appropriate steps described in the following sections.

Results
Your application's URL mappings are now compatible with the new PathPatternParser, ensuring proper functionality with Spring 6.0 and later versions.

Next Steps
Thoroughly test your application after making these changes to ensure all URL mappings work as expected.
Task overview: Spring Framework 6.2.x
Next: Adapting to Strict URL Matching

Adjusting Mapping
Multi-segment matching and AntPathMatcher specific syntax are not supported in static resource mappings.

Context
Spring XML-based configuration doesn't support a return to the AntPathMatcher for static resource mappings. As a result, mappings with syntax that is no longer compatible with the
PathPatternParser may no longer work and will require manual adjustments.

Procedure
Mappings such as the following example are mapped with additional comments and require adaptation:
<mvc:resources mapping="**/some-path/**"

location="classpath:/static/example.jsp/">

Here's an example of a comment:
<!-- FRAMEWORK_UPDATE - TODO - verify if the pattern is valid for the new path matcher. -->

 Remember
These comments will only be added if you're using OpenRewrite recipes.

Adapting patterns within the Spring Security configuration
Context
Spring Security configuration of the HTTP Security using the Spring Security XML element may also be affected by this change. Any mappings with syntax that are no longer compatible with the

PathPatternParser may no longer work if you use the Spring MVC Request Matcher as it no longer uses the AntPathMatcher. Problematic mappings such as the below example are marked
with a comment and may require manual adaptation.
<http access-decision-manager-ref="accessDecisionManager" use-expressions="false" request-matcher="mvc" use-authorization-manager="false">
<intercept-url pattern="/problematic/**/sample" access="PERMIT_ALL" requires-channel="https"/>

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

85

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
</http>

Procedure
Consider two different approaches for this issue:
Adjusting the mappings to be more specific and use the supported syntax.
Change the request-matcher within the <http> tag parameter and switch the request-matcher from the mvc one to ant. With this change, the mappings for this tag will not use
the Spring MVC Matcher but the Ant Path Patterns.

Changes for extensions generated from ycommercewebservicestest template
If your extensions are generated from the ycommercewebservicestest template, perform the following step.

Context
The URL pattern configuration in the springmvc-v2-servlet.xml file is no longer supported.

Procedure
Update the following code:
Previous Configuration:
<mvc:resources mapping="**/swagger-ui.html" location="classpath:/META-INF/resources/"/>

Updated Configuration:
<mvc:resources mapping="/*/swagger-ui.html" location="classpath:/META-INF/resources/"/>

Restoring AntPathMatcher Usage
Context
With the change of the default behaviors, Spring authors provide two ways to restore the old behavior and usage of the old AntPathMatcher:
explicitly setting the PathPatternParser to null.
explicitly using the AntPathMatcher configuration options when PathPatternParser is not set explicitly.
For more information, see this comment

.

On the SAP Commerce Cloud side, this configuration has to be adjusted per web application (extensions). See the suggested approach in the following section.

Procedure
1. Adjust the configuration setting in the spring-mvc-config.xml in a given extension by explicitly defining the usage of AntPathMatcher.
<bean id="pathMatcher" class="org.springframework.util.AntPathMatcher" />
<mvc:annotation-driven>
<mvc:path-matching path-matcher="pathMatcher"/>
</mvc:annotation-driven>
2. If you customize within the web application context of the extension definition of RequestMappingHandlerMapping bean, you need to also explicitly set the patternParser property
to null.
<bean id="requestMappingHandlerMapping"
class="org.springframework.web.servlet.mvc.method.annotation.RequestMappingHandlerMapping">
<property name="order" value="0" />
<!-Some custom property here-->
<property name="patternParser" >
<null/>
</property>
</bean>

 Note
To ensure that your request mapping overrides the default one provided by the servlet HandlerMappings, you must declare the bean using the same ID that Spring uses (in this case,

requestMappingHandlerMapping). Next, define it before configuring <mvc:annotation-driven />. When Spring parses <mvc:annotation-driven />, it registers the
few core beans including requestMappingHandlerMapping, if it isn't already present.
Depending on your configuration you might need to configure patternParser for other HandlerMappings used in your application, such as:

org.springframework.integration.http.inbound.IntegrationRequestMappingHandlerMapping
org.springframework.web.servlet.handler.BeanNameUrlHandlerMapping

3. Set the patternParser property explicitly to null, if your Spring MVC configuration contains or configures beans that are instances of SimpleUrlHandlerMapping, or in general a
subtype of AbstractUrlHandlerMapping class. Find below an example using the bean definition of SimpleUrlHandlerMapping:

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

86

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
<bean class="org.springframework.web.servlet.handler.SimpleUrlHandlerMapping">
<property name="mappings">
<props>
<prop key="/products/details">detailsController</prop>
</props>
</property>
<property name="patternParser">
<null/>
</property>
</bean>

Related Information
Spring 6.0 Release Notes
Spring blog: URL Matching with PathPattern in Spring MVC

Adapting to Strict URL Matching
As of Spring Framework 6.0, the default behavior for matching trailing slash in URL paths has changed. The trailing slash matching configuration option has been deprecated and its default value
has been set to false.
This change means that URLs with trailing slashes no longer automatically match their non-trailing slash counterparts.
For example, before update GET /some/greeting/ would match @GetMapping("/some/greeting") in your controller. With the new default settings in Spring 6.0, this is no longer the
case. The same request will result in an HTTP 404 error, unless it's explicitly handled. This strict mapping will be left enabled by default within the SAP Commerce Cloud.
In SAP Commerce Cloud all endpoints are exposed without trailing slashes. Here are possible solutions:
The advised solution is to adjust URLs in your files to match the endpoint configuration exactly to path without trailing slash. If you had any path defined with trailing slash, after running the
OpenRewrite Framework Update recipe set, the comment like this one should be present:
FRAMEWORK_UPDATE - TODO - according to the new guide paths should not contain a trailing slash.
Handle requests with trailing slashes explicitly:
@GetMapping(value = {"/some/greeting","/some/greeting/"})

Removal of the Trailing Slash in JSP Files
In the JSP files, you need to find all the tags where the paths/url are specified and if the url value contains a trailing slash, remove this slash. For instance, you need to remove the trailing slash from

value="/monitoring/database/logs/download/" in the following example:
<form id="downloadForm" method="GET" action="<c:url value="/monitoring/database/logs/download/"/>">
<input type="text" id="downloadSize" name="downloadSize" value="-1"/>
</form>

<form id="downloadForm" method="GET" action="<c:url value="/monitoring/database/logs/download"/>">
<input type="text" id="downloadSize" name="downloadSize" value="-1"/>
</form>

You should adjust the paths in JSP files only for tags where the path/url is referring to SAP Commerce Cloud API. If you're using custom API and explicitly expose paths with trailing slashes no
change on JSP side is needed.

Changes for Extensions Generated from ycommercewebservicestest Template
If your extensions are generated from the ycommercewebservicestest template, follow the following instructions.
Test cases that build URLs with trailing slashes should be updated to remove the trailing slash.
As an example, the following code is changing:
Previous Configuration:
path: getBasePathWithSite() + '/users/' + customer.customerId + "/addresses/",
Updated Configuration:
path: getBasePathWithSite() + '/users/' + customer.customerId + "/addresses",

Adjusting to jakarta.servlet.Filter API
This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

87

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
With the SAP Commerce Cloud Framework Update, javax.servlet.Filter was updated to jakarta.servlet.Filter.

 Note
Update of packages is covered by the OpenRewrite framework update recipe.

In case logic in your implementation contains custom filters, you might need to adjust to the new API, if some of the deprecated methods were in use. Namespaces also need to be adjusted.
With this change these deprecated methods were removed from the interface:
Deprecated Methods and Replacements
Removed Method

Replacement

public HttpSessionContext getSessionContext()

HTTPSessionContext was removed, use HttpSession directly instead.

public Object getValue(final String arg0)

public void getAttribute(final String arg0)

String[] getValueNames()

public Enumeration<String> getAttributeNames()

public void putValue(final String arg0, final Object arg1)

public void setAttribute(final String arg0)

public void removeValue(final String arg0)

public void removeAttribute(final String arg0)

public String encodeUrl(final String arg0)

public String encodeURL(final String arg0)

public String encodeRedirectUrl(final String arg0)

String encodeRedirectURL(final String arg0)

If any custom logic was provided in one of those methods, consider moving it to the new method version. All direct invocations of the removed methods should be adjusted as well.

Using StandardServletMultipartResolver for Multipart Data
Prepare for StandardServletMultipartResolver usage in your SAP Commerce Cloud implementation after the removal of CommonsMultipartResolver that was used in Spring
versions prior to 6.1.

Context
Starting from Spring 6.1, some of the Servlet-based integrations are removed, including CommonsMultipartResolver. For more information about this class, see Spring Documentation: Class
CommonsMultipartResolver

.

SAP Commerce Cloud provides a recipe for replacing usage of the CommonsMultipartResolver with StandardServletMultipartResolver. The replacement involves updating Java
code, bean definitions, and configuring multipart settings in web.xml. More information about the new class can be found in Spring Documentation: Class StandardServletMultipartResolver

.

Limitations
Not all methods accessible on CommonsMultipartResolver have an equivalent in the StandardServletMultipartResolver. With the StandardServletMultipartResolver,
some parts of the configuration, like the maximum size or storage location, must be done directly in the web.xml of the given servlet configurations. Calls to methods that are not available on the

StandardServletMultipartResolver may cause compilation errors and require manual adjustments.

Procedure
Verify the usage and adapt the following methods/settings if needed:
Methods/Settings Unavailable in StandardServletMultipartResolver
Method

Comment

CommonsMultipartResolver#setSupportedMethods

Checking the HTTP Request Method is not supported by the StandardServletMultipartResolver.
Only content type is taken into consideration.

CommonsMultipartResolver#setServletContext

StandardServletMultipartResolver is not ServletContextAware. Setting the servlet context explicitly is not supported.

CommonsMultipartResolver#getFileItemFactory
CommonsMultipartResolver#getFileUpload
CommonsMultipartResolver#setMaxUploadSize

For StandardServletMultipartResolver this setting should be explicitly set in the web.xml <multipart-config> if needed:
<multipart-config>
<max-request-size>2097152</max-request-size>
<!-- Specified value is just an example. Adjust your configuration depending on the requirements -->
</multipart-config>

CommonsMultipartResolver#setMaxUploadSizePerFile

For StandardServletMultipartResolver this setting should be explicitly set in the web.xml <multipart-config> if needed:
<multipart-config>
<max-file-size>1048576</max-file-size>

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

88

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
Method

Comment
<!-- Specified value is just an example. Adjust your configuration depending on the requirements -->
</multipart-config>

CommonsMultipartResolver#setMaxInMemorySize

For StandardServletMultipartResolver this setting should be explicitly set in the web.xml <multipart-config> if needed:
<multipart-config>
<file-size-threshold>51200</file-size-threshold>
<!-- Specified value is just an example. Adjust your configuration depending on the requirements -->
</multipart-config>

CommonsMultipartResolver#setUploadTempDir

For StandardServletMultipartResolver this setting should be explicitly set in the web.xml <multipart-config> if needed:
<multipart-config>
<location>/tmp/example</location>
<!-- Specified value is just an example. Adjust your configuration depending on the requirements -->
</multipart-config>

CommonsMultipartResolver#setPreserveFilename

This setting is not supported by StandardServletMultipartResolver.

CommonsMultipartResolver#setDefaultEncoding

This setting is not supported by StandardServletMultipartResolver.

Previous Configuration:
@Bean
public MultipartResolver multipartResolver() {

Updated Configuration:
@Bean

final StandardServletMultipartResolver multipartResolver = new StandardServletMultipartResolver();

}

Updating spring-security-saml2-service-provider to 6.4.x
For compatibility reasons with Spring 6, the version of the spring-security-saml2-service-provider library version has been updated from 5.8.11 to 6.4.1.

Context
Imports may require adjustments in some classes since the structure of some packages has changed in the new library version.

Procedure
This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

89

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
1. Replace classes that are no longer available:
With the new version of the library, some classes are removed or replaced with new ones. Here are suggested replacements:

Class in version 5.8.x

Suggested replacement in version 6.4.x

DefaultSaml2AuthenticationRequestContextResolver

OpenSaml5AuthenticationRequestResolver

OpenSaml4LogoutRequestResolver

OpenSaml5LogoutRequestResolver

OpenSaml4LogoutResponseResolver

OpenSaml5LogoutResponseResolver

OpenSaml4AuthenticationProvider

OpenSaml5AuthenticationProvider

OpenSaml4MetadataResolver

OpenSaml5MetadataResolver

2. Verify Saml2AuthenticationTokenConverter class constructor usage in code.
Since version 6.4.1 the Saml2AuthenticationTokenConverter class contains only one constructor:

Saml2AuthenticationTokenConverter(RelyingPartyRegistrationResolver relyingPartyRegistrationResolver). The second deprecated constructor has been
removed. To learn more, see Spring Documentation: Class Saml2AuthenticationTokenConverter

.

3. Initialize the SignatureValidationFilter class object.
Due to the OpenSaml update from version 4 to version 5, the SignatureValidationFilter class object needs to be initialized. This is due to the fact that in the new version the

SignatureValidationFilter class implements the InitializableComponent interface. For more information on SignatureValidationFilter, see Java

and Shibboleth

documentation.
//Before
SignatureValidationFilter signatureValidationFilter = new SignatureValidationFilter(signatureTrustEngine);
/After update
SignatureValidationFilter signatureValidationFilter = new SignatureValidationFilter(signatureTrustEngine);
signatureValidationFilter.initialize();
4. To restore the previous behavior of some classes, Spring Security configuration needs to be updated and an additional parameter: security-context-explicit-save="false",
needs to be added to spring-security-config.xml.
<!--Example before-->
<security:http entry-point-ref="samlEntryPoint"
authentication-manager-ref="samlAuthenticationManager"
use-expressions="false"
use-authorization-manager="false">
<!--Example after-->
<security:http entry-point-ref="samlEntryPoint"
authentication-manager-ref="samlAuthenticationManager"
use-expressions="false"
use-authorization-manager="false"
security-context-explicit-save="false">
Behavior of some classes has changed in Spring Security 6. Currently, SecurityContextHolderFilter only reads SecurityContext from the SecurityContextRepository,
and populates it in the SecurityContextHolder. For more information, see Spring Documentation: Require Explicit Saving of SecurityContextRepository

.

Next task: Updating to SiteMesh 3.2.x

Updating to SiteMesh 3.2.x
SiteMesh 3.0-alpha is not fully compatible with Jakarta EE 10 and was upgraded to version 3.2.1 with the Spring 6 update.

Context
The best choice of SiteMesh version for Spring 6 is 3.1.0 or later. There is a difference between SiteMesh 3.0-alpha and SiteMesh 3.1.0 in the behavior when sitemesh3.xml configFile is not
explicitly defined. In SiteMesh 3.0-alpha, when configFile param is not specified, it searches for sitemesh3.xml in /WEB-INF/ default location, however, in SiteMesh 3.1.0 this works
differently. When configFile param is not specified, it applies default SiteMesh rules but it doesn't search for a sitemesh3.xml configFile in /WEB-INF/. It means that with the upgrade
of SiteMesh, we also need to customize it's configuration. The configFile parameter should be explicitly specified if sitemesh3.xml exists and contains any custom configuration.

 Note
This is only relevant if you created a SiteMesh filter in your custom code, or modified sitemesh3.xml file configuration, provided that you used SiteMesh in your custom extensions.

Procedure
1. Replace the previous SiteMesh filter configuration with an updated one:
Previous Configuration
<filter>
<filter-name>sitemesh</filter-name>
<filter-class>org.sitemesh.config.ConfigurableSiteMeshFilter</filter-class>
</filter>
Updated Configuration

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

90

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
<filter>
<filter-name>sitemesh</filter-name>
<filter-class>org.sitemesh.config.ConfigurableSiteMeshFilter</filter-class>
<init-param>
<param-name>configFile</param-name>
<param-value>/WEB-INF/sitemesh3.xml</param-value>
</init-param>
</filter>
2. Modify the decorator path and configure decorator-prefix parameter in the sitemesh3.xml file. Here's the previous decorator path and the updated version of it:
Previous Configuration
<mapping path="/*" decorator="/WEB-INF/jsp/decorators/main.jsp"/>
Updated Configuration
<decorator-prefix>/WEB-INF/jsp/decorators/</decorator-prefix>
<mapping path="/*" decorator="main.jsp"/>
In this case decorator-prefix is overwritten so the decorator doesn't have to be located in the default /WEB-INF/decorators location.

 Remember
Since 3.2.0 decorators are expected to be in /WEB-INF/decorators/. If they are in another location, you have to overwrite the decorator-prefix parameter. This change is
obligatory. If you want to set a full path in the decorator parameter, you have to set decorator-prefix to empty value. Nevertheless, the most readable and maintainable option is
to split decorator file name and location.

Adding Missing MVC Configuration in Web Application Context
Ensure Spring MVC and Security share the same web application context to avoid missing mvcHandlerMappingIntrospector bean issues introduced in Spring 6.x.

Context
During startup, you may encounter issues connected to a missing mvcHandlerMappingIntrospector bean. This might be related to an incorrectly configured web application context, where
Spring MVC and Spring Security aren't configured within the same web application context and the HandlerMappingIntrospector bean isn't available. The requirement to have Spring MVC
and Security configuration in the same context (when Spring MVC is on the classpath) comes with the Spring 6.X update.

Procedure
Adjust the configuration and ensure that Spring MVC and Spring Security are configured within the same web application context, and the HandlerMappingIntrospector bean is available.

</param-value>
</context-param>

Adapting to Removal of the @Required Annotation
With Spring Framework 6 update, the @Required annotation is no longer used. If you decided to utilize the OpenRewrite recipe, all the invocations of @Required annotation were automatically
removed from the code.
To implement bean injection verification at application startup using standard Spring functionality, consider utilizing a bean initialization callback to carry out the verification. You can do this by
implementing InitializingBean interface.
Here is the previous implementation with the @Required annotation:
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Required;
public class MyBean implements MyBeanInterface
{
@Required
private String myProperty;
...
}
This is an example with the InitializingBean interface:
//import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Required; - LINE REMOVED WITH FRAMEWORK UPDATE
import org.springframework.beans.factory.InitializingBean;
public class MyBean implements InitializingBean, MyBeanInterface
// ADD InitializingBean if not present
{
//@Required - LINE REMOVED WITH FRAMEWORK UPDATE
private String myProperty;
// ADD BEAN EXISTENCE VERIFICATION LOGIC (if required)
@Override
public final void afterPropertiesSet() throws Exception
{
if (this.myProperty == null) {
throw new IllegalArgumentException("Property 'myProperty' must be set");
}
}
...
}
To read more about initialization callbacks, see the related information section.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

94

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
For new functionalities, or in case backward compatibility isn't an issue, it's preferred to use constructor injection and perform the verification logic there, instead of using InitializingBean.
Here's an example solution using the constructor injection:
public class MyBean implements
{
private String myProperty;

MyBeanInterface

public MyBean(final String myProperty)
{
if (myProperty == null) {
throw new IllegalArgumentException("Property 'myProperty' must be set");
}
this.myProperty = myProperty;
}
...
}
Here's a change in the *-spring.xml configuration for switching to constructor injection that is backward incompatible.
<bean id="myBean"
class="org.my.package.MyBean">
<!--<property name="myProperty" value="ExpectedValue"/> // PROPERTY INJECTION REMOVED IN PLACE OF CONSTRUCTOR INJECTION -->
<constructor-arg name="myProperty" value="ExpectedValue"/> <!--// NEW CONSTRUCTOR INJECTION - changing injection type breaks compatibility </bean>

Adapting codebase after removal of SocketUtils Class with Spring 6.X releases
Spring removed the deprecated org.springframework.util.SocketUtils class with 6.X releases.

Context
If you use this class in your project, you need to adapt it. We propose choosing between two actions.

Procedure
Choose one of these options:
Create own utility class using JDK API directly. Here's an example:
public class CustomSocketUtils {
public static int findAvailableTcpPort() throws IOException {
try (ServerSocket socket = new ServerSocket(0)) {
socket.setReuseAddress(true);
return socket.getLocalPort();
}
}
public static int findAvailableUdpPort() throws IOException {
try (DatagramSocket socket = new DatagramSocket(0)) {
socket.setReuseAddress(true);
return socket.getLocalPort();
}
}
}
Migrate to Apache Commons Net.

Resolving BeanPostProcessorChecker Warnings
Adapt to new warning message logic introduced in BeanPostProcessorChecker with Spring Framework 6.

Context
This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

95

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
With Spring Framework 6, the BeanPostProcessorChecker now emits WARN-level log messages when it detects that a Spring bean might not have been fully initialized before being injected
or used by a BeanPostProcessor. For more information, see Spring Framework GitHub: BeanPostProcessorChecker

.

Here is the new warning message:
Bean '%BEAN_THAT_MIGHT_NOT_BE_CORRECTLY_INITIALIZED%' of type [%TYPE_OF_THE_BEAN%] is not eligible for getting processed
by all BeanPostProcessors (for example: not eligible for auto-proxying). Is this bean getting eagerly injected/applied
to a currently created BeanPostProcessor [%POST_PROCESSOR_WHICH_FAILED_THE_CHECK%]? Check the corresponding
BeanPostProcessor declaration and its dependencies/advisors. If this bean does not have to be post-processed,
declare it with ROLE_INFRASTRUCTURE.

BEAN_THAT_MIGHT_NOT_BE_CORRECTLY_INITIALIZED: bean which was referenced during the post processing phase, but was not yet fully processed (for example, AOP proxies were not
created yet).

POST_PROCESSORS_WHICH_FAILED_THE_CHECK: list of post processors which reference the not initialized bean.
Theoretical Background
This bean post processing check existed in older Spring versions as well, but its severity was set to INFO. With the Spring 6 release, the log severity was changed to WARN to increase the issue
visibility.
Spring creates all BeanPostProcessor beans before creating any other beans. Using BeanFactory in postConstruct, or afterPropertiesSet logic in BeanPostProcessor to fetch
or modify other beans could bring unexpected results as those beans may not yet be properly initialized. Such logic should be invoked only in BeanPostProcessor interface methods. For more
information, see Spring Documentation: Interface BeanPostProcessor

.

Task overview: Spring Framework 6.2.x
Previous task: Adapting codebase after removal of SocketUtils Class with Spring 6.X releases
Next task: Configure Extension Load Order to Support Fixed Spring 6 Alias Overriding Behavior

Resolving the Issue
Prerequisites
Before applying any of the below suggestions, verify if the BeanPostProcessor uses the bean factory getBean() in methods which implement the BeanPostProcessor interface, and not
during post processor initialization, for example, in PostConstruct or afterPropertiesSet logic.

Procedure
1. Modify the order in which the post processor beans are created.
This solution requires making the PostProcessor implement the org.springframework.core.PriorityOrdered interface. Another step is implementing getOrder method
which should return a low-priority order (for example, Integer.MAX_VALUE). Here are examples of existing PostProcessors that were already modified::

ListMergeDirectiveBeanPostProcessor
MapMergeDirectiveBeanPostProcessor
ModifyPopulatorListBeanPostProcessor
This allowed finer control over their initialization order, which can resolve the warning in some instances. However, this sometimes led to additional errors connected to processing of some
of the post processors. To fix those new errors, initialization logic was moved into the BeanPostProcessor methods.
2. Define the bean as lazy-loaded. This changes the behavior as the bean is created with the first invocation that requires its usage.

 Caution
This solution was not tested.

Debugging the Problem
Procedure
1. Check the WARN message. It logs PostProcessor name that is affected.
2. Set breakpoints to warnings in PostProcessorRegistrationDelegate$BeanPostProcessorChecker#postProcessAfterInitialization.
3. Run the server in debug mode.
./hybrisserver.sh debug
4. After stopping on a breakpoint, show all frames in your IDE to have a full stacktrace.
5. Find PostProcessor bean creation in the stacktrace and its direct dependency.
6. Apply one of the solutions presented above.

 Remember
Although it's possible to mute the logger for the BeanPostProcessorChecker class, this isn't a valid long-term solution and can lead to unexpected errors.

Configure Extension Load Order to Support Fixed Spring 6 Alias Overriding Behavior
This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

96

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
Spring Framework 6 resolves inconsistencies in bean overriding, specifically involving conflicts between bean names and aliases.

Context
These changes may affect your configuration if all of the following points apply:
You override a bean from another extension.
Alias of your bean is the same as the id of the overridden bean.
There is no dependency configured between these extensions in extensioninfo.xml file which specifies the expected loading order.
See the Spring Framework v6.0.0-M3

release notes and the related issue

for details.

Let's analyze the following example. In the extension BaseExt, there's a bean defined without an alias:
<bean id="myBeanId" class="com.sap.MyBean" />

In the extension AnotherExt, the bean is overridden, and the alias attribute value of the new bean is the same as the bean id in the extension BaseExt. See this example:
<alias name="mySuperBeanId" alias="myBeanId"/>
<bean id="mySuperBeanId" class="com.sap.MySuperBean"/>

As there is no dependency configured in extensioninfo.xml between these extensions, the loading order of extensions, and consequently loading order of beans is non-deterministic.
In Spring Framework 5: the bean myBeanId from extension BaseExt did not override mySuperBeanId because the alias myBeanId from extension AnotherExt was not removed and
remained active. Although the extension and Spring context loading order was incorrect, the underlying issue

masked the problem, resulting in no apparent impact on the

implementation.
In Spring Framework 6: the bean myBeanId from extension BaseExt overrides alias of mySuperBeanId from extension AnotherExt because alias is removed due to the resolved bean
alias overriding issue. To align with this corrected logic in Spring 6, it's necessary to enforce the correct extension loading order.

Task overview: Spring Framework 6.2.x
Previous task: Resolving BeanPostProcessorChecker Warnings
Next task: Adapting to @TestExecutionListener Annotation Changes

Identify and Resolve the Issue
Context
The problem is only visible in an application that's already updated to Spring Framework 6. If your extension loading order is wrong, you will find the following log during the server startup:
Removing alias 'myBeanId' for bean 'mySuperBeanId' due to registration of bean definition for bean 'myBeanId'
The log entry above indicates that a bean definition has overridden an existing alias. This behavior is generally unintended and may lead to the application using a different bean implementation
than expected. You need to identify the extensions for which alias and bean mentioned in the application startup log are defined.

Procedure
1. Add missing requires-extension element in the extensioninfo.xml file of extension AnotherExt to load them in a proper order, if the dependency between extensions is missing
by mistake.
<requires-extension name="BaseExt"/>
2. If the dependency between extensions isn't applicable, you can add load-prior-to metadata in the extensioninfo.xml file of the BaseExt extension (the one which should be
loaded first):
<meta key="load-prior-to" value="AnotherExt" />

Next Steps
If you want to learn more, see the Enforcing Extension Loading Order without Defining Dependencies section in Extension Dependencies.

Adapting to @TestExecutionListener Annotation Changes
Spring 6.0 changed how test listeners are registered in certain base classes. Some tests may need updates to keep the expected behavior when updating from earlier versions.

Context
Spring 6.0 introduced a breaking change related to the @TestExecutionListeners annotation, which was removed from several key base classes. If you have test classes extending from these
specific base classes and also using the @TestExecutionListeners annotation, you need to update it to use the <MERGE_WITH_DEFAULTS> mergeMode. This ensures that the default
listeners are registered, maintaining the same behavior as in Spring 5.x.
The @TestExecutionListeners annotation was removed from the following classes:

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

97

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
org.springframework.test.context.junit4.AbstractJUnit4SpringContextTests
org.springframework.test.context.junit4.AbstractTransactionalJUnit4SpringContextTests
org.springframework.test.context.testng.AbstractTestNGSpringContextTests
org.springframework.test.context.testng.AbstractTransactionalTestNGSpringContextTests
For more information on the annotation removal, see this commit in Spring GitHub repository

.

If you extend any of these classes, follow the below steps to keep backward compatibility.

Procedure
1. Add the @TestExecutionListeners annotation to the definitions of classes it was removed from.
2. Update @TestExecutionListeners annotation usage in your test classes with the <MERGE_WITH_DEFAULTS> mergeMode.
// Switch to default listeners
@TestExecutionListeners(
listeners = { MyCustomListener.class },
inheritListeners = false,
mergeMode = MergeMode.MERGE_WITH_DEFAULTS)
public class MyTest extends AbstractJUnit4SpringContextTests { }

Loading OCC Swagger Properties
If your extensions are generated from the ycommercewebservices template, perform the following steps to load OCC Swagger properties.

Context
After upgrading to Spring 6, the properties defined in v2/swagger.properties, which are used by springdoc-openapi to construct the OpenAPI response URL, are no longer loaded via

@PropertySource.
To fix this issue, create a new class OCCPropertiesFactory to explicitly load these properties, enabling springdoc-openapi to read them.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

98

3/9/26, 4:28 PM

Procedure
1. Add a new class to load extra properties from v2/swagger.properties.
package de.hybris.platform.ycommercewebservices.v2.config;
import de.hybris.platform.servicelayer.config.impl.TenantAwareHybrisPropertiesFactory;
import java.io.InputStream;
import java.util.Properties;
import wiremock.org.slf4j.Logger;
import wiremock.org.slf4j.LoggerFactory;
public class OCCPropertiesFactory extends TenantAwareHybrisPropertiesFactory
{
private static final Logger LOGGER = LoggerFactory.getLogger(OCCPropertiesFactory.class);
public static final String V2_SWAGGER_PROPERTIES = "v2/swagger.properties";
@Override
public Properties getObject() throws Exception
{
Properties properties = super.getObject();
if (properties != null)
{
properties.putAll(loadProperties(V2_SWAGGER_PROPERTIES));
}
return properties;
}
private Properties loadProperties(String propertiesFileName)
{
Properties properties = new Properties();
try (InputStream inputStream = Thread.currentThread().getContextClassLoader().getResourceAsStream(propertiesFileName))
{
if (inputStream != null)
{
properties.load(inputStream);
}
}
catch (Exception e)
{
LOGGER.error("cannot load OCC property file", e);
}
return properties;
}
}
2. Configure the bean in springmvc-v2-servlet.xml.
<alias name="applicationHybrisProperties" alias="occHybrisProperties"/>
<bean id="applicationHybrisProperties" parent="hybrisProperties"
class="de.hybris.platform.ycommercewebservices.v2.config.OCCPropertiesFactory">
</bean>
<alias name="occPropertyPlaceholderConfigurer" alias="platformPropertyPlaceHolder"/>
<bean id="occPropertyPlaceholderConfigurer"
class="org.springframework.beans.factory.config.PropertyPlaceholderConfigurer">
<property name="properties" ref="occHybrisProperties"/>
<property name="ignoreUnresolvablePlaceholders" value="true"/>
<property name="order" value="-10"/>
</bean>
Task overview: Spring Framework 6.2.x

Next: @ModelAttribute Annotation Changes

@ModelAttribute Annotation Changes
Spring provides a @ModelAttribute annotation that allows binding elements for the HTTP request to the model object.
With Spring 6.x two changes have been made that affect how the annotation binding works using the @ModelAttribute annotation:
Support for binding the request headers has been added.

@ModelAttribute annotation no longer allows for binding of the request elements such as parameters, multiparts, path variables, or headers, to the primitive types like for example int,
or long. To compensate for that you can consider the usage of a wrapper object, or switch to @RequestParam annotation, however, keep in mind that the scope of the request elements
that can be bonded to the parameter is more limited here.

Parent topic: Spring Framework 6.2.x

Spring Documentation: @RequestParam
Spring 6.2 Release Notes: Data Binding from Headers

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

3/9/26, 4:28 PM

Consider Removing Separate DispatcherServlet Context
When configuring a Spring web application, it's worth evaluating how servlet contexts are defined.
As a result of combining of the Spring MVC and Spring Security into web application context, there might be no need to create a separate DispatcherServlet context with a similar
configuration. By doing so, some application memory can be saved. For more information, see Adding Missing MVC Configuration in Web Application Context.
Check the sample yempty web.xml configuration changes, as well as the updated processing extension configuration, to see how to reuse web application context for the DispatcherServlet.

Integration 6.4.x Update
Spring integration version was updated from 5.5.20 to >= 6.4.1.
The spring-integration-rmi module has been removed altogether after being deprecated in previous versions. There is no replacement: it's recommended to migrate to more secure network and
application protocols, such as WebSockets, RSockets, gRPC or REST. For more information, see Spring Release Notes: Changes between 5.5 and 6.0

.

Furthermore, after previously being deprecated, the spring-integration-security module is now completely removed in favor of API from spring-security-messaging module. To learn more about this
change, see Security in Spring Integration

as well as Spring Release Notes: Changes between 6.2 and 6.3

.

Parent topic: Spring Framework 6.2.x
Previous: Consider Removing Separate DispatcherServlet Context
Next: Parameter Name Retention for Dependency Injection

Parameter Name Retention for Dependency Injection
Spring framework now relies on Java and Groovy compilers to retain parameter names in bytecode for dependency injection, removing the need for bytecode parsing.
Spring framework no longer uses bytecode parsing to resolve parameter names during dependency injection. This has been addressed by configuring Java and Groovy compilers within the SAP
Commerce Cloud to retain the parameter names within the bytecode. This change should be transparent and doesn't require any additional modifications.
If you have any custom compilation-related logic within your project and encounter issues with dependency injection during framework upgrade, you may need to consider adjusting the
compilation configuration with an additional -parameters compiler flag to retain the parameters names in bytecode.

Parent topic: Spring Framework 6.2.x
Previous: Integration 6.4.x Update
Next: Resolving Redirection Issues of request-matcher

Related Information
Spring Documentation: Parameter Name Retention

Resolving Redirection Issues of request-matcher
In Spring Security 6.x, the default policy of the request-matcher has been changed from AntPathRequestMatcher to MvcPathRequestMatcher, causing 302 redirections of static
resources.
To prevent these redirections, the request-matcher has been updated:
Before:
<http use-expressions="true" security="none" pattern="/zkau/**" disable-url-rewriting="false"/>
<http use-expressions="true" security="none" pattern="/cng/**" disable-url-rewriting="false"/>
<http use-expressions="true" security="none" pattern="/css/**" disable-url-rewriting="false"/>

After:
<http use-expressions="true" security="none" pattern="/zkau/**" disable-url-rewriting="false" request-matcher="ant"/>
<http use-expressions="true" security="none" pattern="/cng/**" disable-url-rewriting="false" request-matcher="ant"/>
<http use-expressions="true" security="none" pattern="/css/**" disable-url-rewriting="false" request-matcher="ant"/>
If you have similar redirection issues in your customized code, update the code accordingly.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

100

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
For more information on previous request-matcher, see Spring Security Web Security

.

Fixing "No visible WebSecurityExpressionHandler" Error
This document provides steps to resolve the java.io.IOException: No visible WebSecurityExpressionHandler instance could be found error when starting the server,
which occurs due to missing security expression handler configuration for JSP 'authorize' tags.

Procedure
1. Locate the configuration file:
a. Navigate to the following directory in your project:
yacceleratorstorefront/web/webroot/WEB-INF/config/
b. Open the spring-security-config.xml file for editing
2. Insert the following bean definition within the <beans> tags of the configuration file:
<bean id="webSecurityExpressionHandler" class="org.springframework.security.web.access.expression.DefaultWebSecurityExpressionHandler"/>
3. Save the modified spring-security-config.xml file.

Next task: Updating Spring Security Intercept-URL Configuration for Empty Expression Strings

Updating Spring Security Intercept-URL Configuration for Empty Expression Strings
This document provides guidance on resolving the "expressionString cannot be empty" error during server startup by properly configuring intercept-url rules in Spring Security 6.

Context
In Spring Security 6, the framework now requires explicit specification of the access attribute for all intercept-url rules, even when setting open access via permitAll(). This change
enforces more explicit security configuration.

Procedure
1. Locate the configuration file:
a. Navigate to the following directory in your project:
yacceleratorstorefront/web/webroot/WEB-INF/config/
b. Open the spring-security-config.xml file for editing.
2. Identify affected Intercept-url Rules:
a. Search for <security:intercept-url> elements that lack an access attribute.
b. Specifically locate any patterns using only requires-channel without access.
3. For each found occurrence (typically the global pattern), add the access="permitAll()" attribute:
<!-- Original -->
<security:intercept-url pattern="/**" requires-channel="https" />
<!-- Updated -->
<security:intercept-url pattern="/**" access="permitAll()" requires-channel="https" />
4. Save the modified spring-security-config.xml file.

Task overview: Spring Framework 6.2.x

Optimizing SequenceSizeReleaseStrategy Configuration for Large Groups
This document provides steps to resolve performance warnings related to SequenceSizeReleaseStrategy by switching to the more
efficient SimpleSequenceSizeReleaseStrategy implementation.

Context

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

101

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
When processing large groups of aggregated messages, the default SequenceSizeReleaseStrategy may issue performance warnings. The SimpleSequenceSizeReleaseStrategy
offers better performance for these scenarios.

Procedure
1. Navigate to your project's Spring configuration file(s) where the aggregator is configured.
2. Search for the existing SequenceSizeReleaseStrategy bean definition:
<bean id="defaultSequenceSizeReleaseStrategy" class="org.springframework.integration.aggregator.SequenceSizeReleaseStrategy"/>
3. Replace the class attribute with the more efficient implementation:
<!-- Original -->
<bean id="defaultSequenceSizeReleaseStrategy" class="org.springframework.integration.aggregator.SequenceSizeReleaseStrategy"/>
<!-- Updated -->
<bean id="defaultSequenceSizeReleaseStrategy" class="org.springframework.integration.aggregator.SimpleSequenceSizeReleaseStrategy"/>
4. Save the modified Spring configuration file.

Resolving DispatcherServlet Exceptions During Server Startup
Update the Spring MVC configuration to ensure compatibility with Spring 6 by explicitly defining the use of AntPathMatcher and setting the patternParser property to null for all handler
mapping beans.

Procedure
1. In the yacceleratorstorefront/web/webroot/WEB-INF/config/spring-mvc-config.xml file, define the usage of the AntPathMatcher by adding the following
configuration:
<bean id="defaultPathMatcher" class="org.springframework.util.AntPathMatcher" />
<bean id="mvcHandlerMappingIntrospector" class="org.springframework.web.servlet.handler.HandlerMappingIntrospector"/>
2. In the yacceleratorstorefront, the bean RequestMappingHandlerMapping is automatically assembled by Spring. To avoid compatibility issues, explicitly define this bean and
configure its pathMatcher and patternParser properties in the yacceleratorstorefront/web/webroot/WEB-INF/config/spring-mvc-config.xml file as follows:
<bean id="requestMappingHandlerMapping"
class="org.springframework.web.servlet.mvc.method.annotation.RequestMappingHandlerMapping">
<property name="pathMatcher" ref="defaultPathMatcher"/>
<property name="patternParser">
<null/>
</property>
</bean>
3. To maintain consistent request mapping behavior, configure the pathMatcher to use AntPathMatcher and set the patternParser property to null for any applicable handler
mapping beans. If your project includes additional custom or automatically detected handler mappings, apply the same configuration to those beans as well. In
yacceleratorstorefront, only the IntegrationRequestMappingHandlerMapping bean requires this update. In the yacceleratorstorefront/web/webroot/WEBINF/config/spring-mvc-config.xml add the following configuration:
<bean id="integrationRequestMappingHandlerMapping"
class="org.springframework.integration.http.inbound.IntegrationRequestMappingHandlerMapping">
<property name="pathMatcher" ref="defaultPathMatcher"/>
<property name="patternParser">
<null/>
</property>
</bean>
4. To customize message converters, declare the RequestMappingHandlerAdapter bean instead of relying on <mvc:annotation-driven>. In yacceleratorstorefront,
ResourceHttpMessageConverter, Jaxb2RootElementHttpMessageConverter, and MappingJackson2HttpMessageConverter are needed. Include only the required
converters in the messageConverters list. Add or update the configuration in yacceleratorstorefront/web/webroot/WEB-INF/config/spring-mvc-config.xml
Previous configuration:
<alias name="jaxb2RootElementHttpMessageConverter" alias="jaxbMessageConverter"/>
<bean id="jaxb2RootElementHttpMessageConverter" class="org.springframework.http.converter.xml.Jaxb2RootElementHttpMessageConverter"/>
<!-- activates annotation driven binding -->
<mvc:annotation-driven ignore-default-model-on-redirect="true" validator="validator">
<mvc:message-converters>
<bean class="org.springframework.http.converter.ResourceHttpMessageConverter"/>
<ref bean="jaxbMessageConverter"/>
<bean class="org.springframework.http.converter.json.MappingJackson2HttpMessageConverter"/>
</mvc:message-converters>
</mvc:annotation-driven>
Current configuration:
<alias name="jaxb2RootElementHttpMessageConverter" alias="jaxbMessageConverter"/>
<bean id="jaxb2RootElementHttpMessageConverter" class="org.springframework.http.converter.xml.Jaxb2RootElementHttpMessageConverter"/>
<bean class="org.springframework.web.servlet.mvc.method.annotation.RequestMappingHandlerAdapter">
<property name="webBindingInitializer">
<bean class="org.springframework.web.bind.support.ConfigurableWebBindingInitializer">
<property name="validator" ref="validator"/>
</bean>
</property>
<property name="messageConverters">
<list>
<bean class="org.springframework.http.converter.ResourceHttpMessageConverter"/>

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

102

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
<ref bean="jaxbMessageConverter"/>
<bean class="org.springframework.http.converter.json.MappingJackson2HttpMessageConverter"/>
</list>
</property>
</bean>
5. Optional: If the server startup still reports a requestPath mismatch error after completing the previous configuration steps, like the following SEVERE: Servlet.service() for

servlet [DispatcherServlet] threw exception java.lang.IllegalArgumentException: Invalid contextPath '/electronics/en': must match the
start of requestPath: '/view/DefaultCMSComponentController', update the DispatcherServlet configuration in
yacceleratorstorefront/web/webroot/WEB-INF/web.xml. Set the detectAllHandlerMappings property to false. This configuration disables Spring MVC’s automatic
detection and registration of HandlerMapping beans.

 Caution
When automatic detection is disabled, you must define and configure all required HandlerMappingimplementations. If any required mappings are missing, certain paths or resources
may not be routed correctly.

Replacing setAttribute() Method for Tomcat Connector
Tomcat was updated from version 9.0.95 to version 10.1.x.

Context
In the previous version, the setAttribute() method was marked as deprecated and it's recommended to use the setProperty() method instead. To learn more, see the related information
section.

 Note
This is only relevant if you created Tomcat connectors in your custom code.

Procedure
Replace the removed setAttribute() method with setProperty() method.
Replace this fragment:
final Connector connector = new Connector();
connector.setAttribute("URIEncoding", "UTF-8");
connector.setAttribute("sslProtocol", "TLS");
with this updated code:

final Connector connector = new Connector();
connector.setProperty("URIEncoding", "UTF-8");
connector.setProperty("sslProtocol", "TLS");

Adjusting to new filter API after Tomcat update
After update to Spring 6 and JDK 21 and some of the libraries have been updated to newer versions. Updates include replacement of javax.servlet with jakarta.servlet and the Tomcat
version.
Because of API changes in these libraries some of the methods had to be removed to compile the code. de.hybris.tomcat.ConfigurableRfc6265CookieProcessor class inherits

org.apache.tomcat.util.http.Rfc6265CookieProcessor, which no longer contains method generateHeader(final Cookie cookie). Now, only method String
generateHeader(final Cookie cookie, final HttpServletRequest request) can be used.
Furthermore, de.hybris.platform.util.RootRequestFilter class contains nested class HybrisResponseWrapper, which inherits

jakarta.servlet.http.HttpServletResponseWrapper. This class no longer contains the following methods:
getSessionContext()
getValue(final String arg0)
getValueNames()
putValue(final String arg0, final Object arg1)
removeValue(final String arg0)
encodeUrl(final String arg0): there is newer method used encodeURL(final String arg0) with same logic inside.
encodeRedirectUrl(final String arg0): there is newer method used encodeRedirectURL(final String arg0) with same logic inside.

Adapting security headers configuration in Tomcat 10.1.X
Tomcat was upgraded to 10.1.x. As per Tomcat's documentation, X-XSS-Protection header was deprecated and it has been removed starting with Tomcat 11.0.x.

Context
Tomcat xssProtectionEnabled property with default value of false, has been deprecated and has been removed starting with Tomcat 11.0.x. This property is not enabled in SAP Commerce
Cloud and therefore X-XSS-Protection header is no longer added to responses by Tomcat. The check previously available to integration tests for X-XSS-Protection header assertions
through WebservicesAssert class has been removed.
Mozilla recommends using Content-Security-Policy header instead of XSS filtering. Content-Security-Policy header is available in SAP Commerce Cloud but it's only set for some of
the web services extensions. For more details about X-XSS-Protection, Mozilla recommendations, see related information section.

Content-Security-Policy header needs to be set for all custom web services extensions. For more information, see Content Security Policy Response Headers.

Procedure
Enable the Content-Security-Policy header. One option to do that is in the local.properties file of your custom SAP Commerce Cloud installation.
Here's a template for applying such a change:
<extension_name>.xss.filter.header.Content-Security-Policy=<header_value>

And here is an example of properties for yempty extension:
yempty.xss.filter.header.Content-Security-Policy=default-src 'self'; style-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline'; img-src 'self'; script-src 'self' 'unsafe-inli

Next Steps

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

105

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
The value of the Content-Security-Policy header is determined on extension basis; different web services extension might have different requirements. Once set, proper testing needs to be done
for the extension to ensure that the header is added to REST API responses, everything works as expected, and that nothing is broken. If in doubt, reach out to security experts.

Update of Ant Version to >= 1.10.14
Update to Java 21 version requires Ant update from 1.10.5 to 1.10.14 or higher.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

106

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
Ant 1.10.14 contains an important change wherein it no longer uses or sets Java SecurityManager when running on Java versions 18 and higher. This should allow projects to build on Java 21. Using
an older version may lead to issues or unrecognized features when building or running Java 21 code.
Ant will no longer use Java SecurityManager because it has been deprecated for removal and by default it's disallowed to be set at runtime since Java 18. This means that the <permissions> type is
no longer functional. Furthermore, if the build executes tasks that call java.lang.System.exit() and if those tasks aren't running in a forked VM of their own, then such tasks will now
terminate the entire Ant build process. It's recommended that such tasks be updated to launch in a forked JVM so that the System.exit() call doesn't impact the JVM in which the Ant process
runs.

The default value of the property that controls behavior of SAP Commerce Cloud during an unsuccessful create data phase has been changed to true, making update or initialization processes fail

accurate and that all project data has been correctly processed.

Activation of JUnit 5 Engines
The default value of the tests.runner.legacy property has been updated to false, activating default support for JUnit 5. This change allows for comprehensive test execution using JUnit 5
engines while maintaining compatibility with JUnit 4.
The default value of the tests.runner.legacy property has been changed to false, activating support for JUnit 5 in the default configuration. As a result, JUnit 4, JUnit 5, and Spock tests,
and JUnit 5 suites are now run by the ant yunitlauncher task that uses the JUnit 5 engines. Previously, the default value of the property was set to true. This meant that only JUnit 4 and
Spock tests were run by the ant yunitint task, which didn't utilize the JUnit 5 engines.

Removing Fest Libraries
Switch from deprecated Fest-Util and Fest-Assert libraries to AssertJ and standard Java utilities.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.
