3/9/26, 4:28 PM

Prerequisites
This step is only relevant if you used Fest libraries in your extensions.

Context
The Fest-Util and Fest-Assert libraries have been long deprecated and are no longer supported or shipped with the codebase. Their usages must be replaced, primarily with AssertJ.

Automated Replacement Using OpenRewrite Recipes
If you decided to use OpenRewrite recipes, it automatically replaced methods and classes that were found to be most commonly used across the source code of the product. The recipes cover the
following updates:
Assertions (assertThat): replaces calls to org.fest.assertions.Assertions.assertThat with org.assertj.core.api.Assertions.assertThat
Map Assertions:
Type Replacement:
All occurrences of org.fest.assertions.MapAssert are replaced with org.assertj.core.api.MapAssert
Static Method Replacement:
When the static method entry(...) is used on Fest’s MapAssert, it's replaced by a call to org.assertj.core.data.MapEntry.entry(...)
Failure handling: The recipe replaces calls to org.fest.assertions.Fail.fail(...) with org.assertj.core.api.Assertions.fail(...)
Collection and Array Utilities:
Type org.fest.util.Arrays is replaced with org.assertj.core.util.Arrays
Type org.fest.util.Strings is replaced with org.assertj.core.util.Strings
Recipes replace Collections.set(...)/list(...) with standard Java collection utilities (new HashSet<>(Arrays.asList(...)) or new ArrayList<>

(Arrays.asList...))).
Imports of org.fest.util.Collections are removed automatically
Condition Implementations:
Replaces org.fest.assertions.Condition with org.assertj.core.api.Condition
Assertion Chain Methods:
The recipes also convert Fest assertion chain methods as follows:
Replace onProperty(...) with extracting(...)
Replace includes(...) with contains(...)
Replace excludes(...) with doesNotContain(...)

 Remember
Our recipes cover only methods that we found to be most commonly used. Other Fest library use cases may require manual adjustments.

Review Fest libraries usage and manually update any areas they're used in to plain Java or AssertJ equivalents. Below are examples of such manual changes that are required.

Procedure
1. Update the incompatible throw org.fest.assertions.Fail.failure(...) method call with throw org.assertj.core.api.Assertions.fail(...).
2. Adjust manually three FEST array methods that have no direct AssertJ equivalent.

Old Method

Replacement

copyOf

java.util.Arrays.copyOf(...)

isEmpty

org.assertj.core.util.Arrays.isNullOrEmpty(...)

format

java.util.Arrays.toString(...)

3. Handle Groovy files manually.

 Note
Even if you used the OpenRewrite automation, it doesn't support Groovy files and they must be handled manually.

Next Steps
After removing Fest-Util and Fest-Assert, thoroughly test your codebase to ensure the replacement to AssertJ works as expected. While most changes are straightforward, be sure to check that all
assertions, exception handling, and utility methods behave correctly after the update.

Upgrading AssertJ 3.5.2 to 3.27.3
Adjust your AssertJ configuration to a new version of the library to ensure that the upgrade remains compatible with your custom implementations.

Context
AssertJ 3.5.2 has been upgraded to 3.27.3. Carry out the following steps to ensure that the new version of the library remains compatible with your custom implementations.

Procedure
1. Since Assertions.assertThat(java.lang.Iterator) in AssertJ 3.12.0 and later now returns org.assertj.core.api.IteratorAssert instead of
org.assertj.core.api.IterableAssert, it's now impossible to directly check the elements of the iterator. If your implementation expects an IterableAssert object, simply
chain the toIterable() method after your assertion:
assertThat(myIterator).toIterable().contains("expected");
This modification converts the returned IteratorAssert back to an IterableAssert, restoring access to collection-specific assertion methods.
2. The upgrade changes the AssertJ extraction syntax from using string property names to using lambda expressions for map property access. If you've found instances of the following
pattern in your custom code:
assertThat(records).extracting(AuditTestHelper::getAuditRecordsAttributes)
.extracting("uid", "name", "defaultpaymentaddress", "defaultshipmentaddress")
Replace them with lambda expressions:
assertThat(records).extracting(AuditTestHelper::getAuditRecordsAttributes)
.extracting(m -> m.get("uid"), m -> m.get("name"), m -> m.get("defaultpaymentaddress"),
m -> m.get("defaultshipmentaddress"))
...

Task overview: Testing
Previous: Testing Cloud Hot Folders Locally
Next: Mockito Upgrade Issues

Mockito Upgrade Issues
Key Mockito upgrade issues include ambiguous method calls after updating argument matchers, unsupported spying on certain core classes like Thread, and injection failures with @InjectMocks
when generic type parameters are missing.

Verified Method Ambiguity
Following argument matchers no longer accept a class parameter and it will be removed by org.openrewrite.java.testing.mockito.Mockito1to3Migration recipe:

org.mockito.ArgumentMatchers isNull(java.lang.Class)
org.mockito.ArgumentMatchers notNull(java.lang.Class)
For example:
verify(myService).updateEntity(notNull(MyEntity.class)) ->
verify(myService).updateEntity(notNull())
In case the verified method is overloaded, it won't compile due to ambiguous method call and has to be cast to the appropriate type, for example:
verify(myService).updateEntity((MyEntity) notNull())
To learn more, see the related information section.

Spying the Thread Class
Spying the Thread class is not supported. What's more mocking a type you don't own is considered a bad practice. In case you encounter some problems with this topic, you can follow the solution
from Mockito guidelines on creating a wrapper. For more details on this topic, see the related information section at the end.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

110

3/9/26, 4:28 PM

Using @InjectMocks with Generic Types
Starting from Mockito 5.2, there are incompatible changes that affect the use of @InjectMocks when working with mocks of generic types. In particular, Mockito fails to inject mocks correctly
when either the class under test contains a generic field without an explicit item type or when the mock in the test is defined without an explicit item type. This change doesn't generate any
warnings or errors in the logs making it difficult to identify and troubleshoot the issue, as the test will encounter a NullPointerException at runtime when class under the test tries to use the
uninitialized field.
Here is an example of problematic usage:
// generic class
class MyGenericType<T extends ItemType> { }
// class with a generic type field with an explicit type parameter
class MyClass {
private MyGenericType<ItemType> myGenericType;
}
// test class attempting to inject the mock without an explicit type parameter
class Test {
@InjectMocks
private MyClass myClass;
@Mock
private MyGenericType myGenericType; // missing type parameter
}
Alternatively, if the class contains a generic field without a specified type parameter, even if the mock is properly defined, injection will still fail:
class MyClass {
private MyGenericType myGenericType; // missing type parameter
}
class Test {
@InjectMocks
private MyClass myClass;
@Mock
private MyGenericType<ItemType> myGenericType;
}
To resolve this issue, ensure that the generic type parameter is explicitly defined both in the class under test and in the mock declaration. This resolves the ambiguity and guarantees the correct
injection of mocks.
Here's the correct implementation:
class ReferenceType {}
class MyGenericType<T extends ItemType> { }
class MyClass {
private MyGenericType<ReferenceType> myGenericType;
}
class Test {
@InjectMocks
private MyClass myClass;
@Mock
private MyGenericType<ReferenceType> myGenericType;
}
By making sure the generic type parameter is defined in both places, you avoid injection problems and runtime issues during testing.

Adding Mocking Name for Mockito @InjectMocks
If your extensions are generated from the ycommercewebservicestest template, follow the following instructions.
Mockito 5.2 introduces changes that can cause issues with @InjectMocks. If you have multiple mock objects of the same type and do not specify a mock name, Mockito will report an error and fail
to inject the objects using @InjectMocks. To fix this issue, you need to declare all the properties of the target bean that uses the @InjectMocks annotation. Additionally, ensure that all Mock
objects of the same type have unique names.
Example Scenario:
The target class to inject contains two members of the same type Validator:
@Resource(name = "validator1")
private Validator validator1;
@Resource(name = "validator2")
private Validator validator2;
If only one of these members is defined as a mock object, the injection will fail. This issue persists regardless of whether the name parameter is specified. For example:
@Mock(name = "validator1")
private Validator validator1;
To fix this issue, ensure that all members of the same type are mocked. Each mock object should be declared with the name of the corresponding class member.
@Mock(name = "validator1")
private Validator validator1;
@Mock(name = "validator2")
private Validator validator2;

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

111

3/9/26, 4:28 PM

Migrating MockedStatic#when
If your extensions are generated from the ycommercewebservicestest template, perform the following step.
Because of changes in the Mockito API, the org.mockito.MockedStatic#when method now only accepts arguments of the type org.mockito.MockedStatic.Verification.
Update the following code:
Previous Configuration:
mockBoolean.when(Boolean.valueOf(userFacade.isAnonymousUser())).thenReturn(Boolean.TRUE);
Updated Configuration:
mockBoolean.when(() -> Boolean.valueOf(userFacade.isAnonymousUser())).thenReturn(Boolean.TRUE);

Declaring Target Bean Properties Where @InjectMocks Annotation Applied
With Mockito 5.2, changes have been introduced such that errors are now reported when attempting to inject objects using @InjectMocks if multiple Mock objects of the same type are present
without a mock name specified. To avoid the errors, ensure that all properties of the target bean on which the @InjectMocks annotation is applied are declared, and make sure that all Mock objects
of the same type have unique names assigned, for example:
@Mock(name="themeStyleService")
private BackofficeThemeStyleService themeStyleService;
@Mock(name="widgetInstanceManager")
private WidgetInstanceManager widgetInstanceManager;
@Mock(name="configurationService")
private ConfigurationService configurationService;

Parent topic: Testing

OAuth
Review all manual steps related to the OAuth update and adapt your SAP Commerce Cloud implementation accordingly.

Moving to the New OAuth Implementation
Adjust your OAuth configuration to the new implementation that has been introduced as a result of moving the OAuth functionality from the Spring Security OAuth library, which has reached its
EOL, to Spring Security.
In this release, the oauth2 extension has been removed and replaced with a new OAuth implementation that comes with the new authorizationserver, resourceserver, and

oauth2commons extensions. The changes are a result of moving the OAuth functionality from the Spring Security OAuth 2.5.x library that reached its EOL in May 2022 to Spring Security 6.x. As
Spring Security isn't fully compatible with Spring Security OAuth, a few changes have been made to the OAuth implementation that required creating new extensions and adjusting their
configuration to what is supported in Spring Security.
The supported OAuth version depends on the currently supported version of the Spring Authorization Server. For more information on currently supported libraries, see Update Releases.
Study the following migration guide and carry out any necessary steps to ensure that you've fully migrated to the new OAuth implementation.

 Note
Some steps might have already been covered by a configuration of an extension that you have already included in your build, for example, the webservicescommons or apiframework
extensions.

How the New OAuth Implementation Works
The new OAuth implementation now supports JWTs (JSON Web Tokens) only. All information is now located within a token. Opaque tokens aren't supported anymore.
Here's a high-level summary of the new OAuth flow:
1. A client requests an access token.
2. The authorization server returns a signed JWT access token.
3. A client requests a resource with the signed JWT access token.
4. The resource server verifies the JWT access token signature with public keys accessible under a JWK endpoint and verifies user permissions.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

112

3/9/26, 4:28 PM

Enabling the New OAuth Implementation
SAP Commerce Cloud is now shipped with the following new extensions:
the authorizationserver extension that holds the authorization server configuration
the resourceserver extension that holds the resource server configuration
the oauth2commons extension that holds the common configuration for the deprecated and the new implementation, and contains common parts of the authorizationserver and

resourceserver configuration
The new extensions are part of the default configuration.

Configuring the New OAuth Implementation
To adjust the new OAuth implementation to the needs of your module, use the properties provided with the new extensions.

Configuring OAuth Clients
The new implementation supports two types of clients:
confidential clients
public clients
Creating OAuth clients is similar to the deprecated OAuth implementation. However, there are some new attributes in OAuthClientDetailsModel that you can configure:

PKCE
Setting the requireProofKey attribute to true means that the PKCE flow is required for all authorization code requests, while setting it to false means that PKCE is optional for a client.
Using PKCE is obligatory for public clients and optional for confidential clients. However, if not explicitly specified, it's activated by default.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

113

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
Relative Redirect URI for OAuth Clients
According to the OAuth specification, the redirection endpoint URI that is used in the authorization code flow must be an absolute URI. Because of that, the new implementation doesn't allow for
using relative redirect URIs. Adapt your configuration of OAuth clients to contain absolute redirect URIs only. If using absolute URIs isn't possible in your configuration, change the behavior by
setting the following property to false:
authserver.authorizationCode.absolute.redirect.uri.check=false
By default, the property is set to true.

Confidential Clients
The value of the public attribute of the OAuthClientDetails model defines whether a client is public or confidential. By default, the value of this attribute is set to false.

Public Clients
Set the value of the public attribute to true for specific public clients.

Client Validation
Each created and updated OAuthClientDetails object is validated against certain preconditions by DefaultOAuthClientDetailsValidator. The preconditions ensure the following:
1. The list of authorized grant types isn't empty.
2. A client has at least one assigned authority.
3. For a client using the authorization code grant type, at least one redirect URI is registered.
4. A public client has no assigned secrets.
5. PKCE has been activated for a public client.
6. A public client has no client credentials grant type activated.
7. A confidential client has a client secret.
8. A client model can be successfully converted to a RegisteredClient object, which is used by Spring when managing OAuth clients. Essentially, OAuthClientDetailsModel is a
database representation of this Spring object.
When any of the preconditions aren't met, InterceptorException is thrown.
To streamline the migration process, the following property has been introduced to enable a “dry run” mode for the validator:
authserver.client.validation.dry.run=true

When activated, this mode logs validation issues as warnings instead of throwing exceptions. By default, this property is set to false, which means that if any of the listed preconditions fail during
the creation or update of OAuthClientDetails, an exception is thrown.

Issuer “iss” Claim of JWT Configuration
You can configure the “iss” issuer claim of a JWT using the following property:
authserver.jwt.claims.iss
The property defines the JWT issuer. If not specified, the issuer is automatically set to the authorization server's endpoint.
The value of this property isn't specified in the default configuration.

Supported Endpoints
SAP Commerce Cloud now exposes the following endpoints:
Issuer endpoint: https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/
Authorization endpoint: https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/authorize
Token endpoint: https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/token
Supported authentication methods: client_secret_basic, client_secret_post
JWKS URI endpoint: https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/jwks
Userinfo endpoint: https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/userinfo
Revocation endpoint: https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/revoke
Supported authentication methods: client_secret_basic, client_secret_post
Introspection endpoint: https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/introspect
Supported authentication methods: client_secret_basic, client_secret_post

Supported Flows
The following flows are supported in the new OAuth implementation:
for confidential clients:
authorization code flow
authorization code flow + PKCE
refresh token flow
client credentials flow
custom SAML token flow
for public clients:
authorization code flow + PKCE
refresh token flow
custom SAML token flow
The password flow and implicit flows are not available in the new implementation.

 Caution
Retrieving a token for a public client using the client credentials flow is no longer supported. Consequently, APIs that are secured with any client role will not be accessible to public clients.
To ensure uninterrupted service, configure public APIs to permit consumption without requiring an access token.

Authorization Code Flow
To get an authorization code, use the following request:
https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/authorize?client_id=<client_id>&response_type=code
You can add the following additional parameters to an authorization code request:

state: Specifies the parameter that’s responsible for cross-site request forgery prevention
scope: Specifies the scope of an access request
redirect_uri: Specifies the URI to which the authorization server redirects requests after successful authorization

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

115

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
When PKCE is activated, you can include the following parameters:

code_challenge
code_challenge_method=S256

 Note
The authorization server currently supports the S256 code challenge method only.

Requesting Access and Refresh Tokens
Use the following to get access or access and refresh tokens:
curl -X POST --location "https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/token" \
-H "Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded" \
-d 'grant_type=authorization_code&code=<authorization-code>' \
--basic --user <client_id>:<secret>
If PKCE is activated, the code_verifier parameter is also required.

 Note
In Spring 6, parameters can only be transmitted in request-body and must not be included in request URIs. For more information, see Client Password

.

OAuthClientDetailsModel now includes a new attribute: requireAuthorizationConsent. This Boolean flag determines whether to display a consent screen to users during the
authorization request flow. It defaults to false, meaning no consent screen is shown unless explicitly activated.

Authorization Code Flow + PKCE
The authorization server supports the PKCE flow. In the authorization code flow, using PKCE is obligatory for public clients. It's optional for confidential clients. By default, PKCE is activated for all
client, but it can be configured separately for each client using the requireProofKey attribute in OAuthClientDetailsModel. Setting this attribute to true results in making the PKCE flow
required for all authorization code requests. Setting it to false means that PKCE is optional for a client.

Code Verifier and Code Challenge
To use PKCE, you need to generate a code verifier and a code challenge. In the default configuration, the code verifier must be between 43 and 128 characters long. The length of the code verifier
can be controlled through the following properties:
Code Verifier Properties
Property

Description

Default Value

authserver.authorizationCode.pkce.codeVerifier.length.min

The minimum length of the code verifier.

43

authserver.authorizationCode.pkce.codeVerifier.length.max

The maximum length of the code verifier.

128

The code challenge is generated based on the code verifier through the following algorithm:
code_challenge = BASE64URL-ENCODE(SHA256(ASCII(code_verifier)))

Example of Authorization Request to Get Authorization Code
See an example of an authorization request to obtain an authorization code:
https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/authorize?client_id=<client_id>&response_type=code&code_challenge=<code_challenge>&code_challenge_meth
In the request, specify the following parameters:

code_challenge
code_challenge_method=S256

 Note
The authorization server currently supports the S256 code challenge method only.

Example of Token Request
See an example of a token request:
curl -X POST --location "https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/token" \
-H "Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded" \
-d 'grant_type=authorization_code&code=<authorization-code>&code_verifier=<verifier>' \
--basic --user <client_id>:<secret>
In the request, specify the code_verifier parameter. The request returns a token if the CODE_CHALLENGE that is used in the authorization request has been created based on the VERIFIER.

 Note
In Spring 6, parameters can only be transmitted in request-body and must not be included in request URIs. For more information, see
https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc6749#section-2.3.1

.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

Refresh Token Flow
To get an access or refresh token in a refresh token flow, use the following request:
curl -X POST --location "https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/token" \
-H "Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded" \
-d 'grant_type=refresh_token&refresh_token=<refresh-token>' \
--basic --user <client_id>:<secret>

Refresh Token Flow for Public Clients
The support for public clients in the refresh token flow can be activated and deactivated in the same way as for confidential clients - by configuring it for selected clients through the

authorizedGrantTypes attribute in the OAuthClientDetails model.
With public clients, the risk of leaked refresh tokens is greater than with confidential clients. If a refresh token is stolen, an attacker can use it to continuously obtain new access tokens without
being detected by the authorization server. To mitigate the risks of using the refresh token flow with public clients, the following properties have been introduced:
Public Client Properties
Property

Description

Default Value

authserver.publicClients.refreshToken.timeToLive.seconds

Sets the maximum lifetime (in seconds) of refresh tokens that are

3600

obtained by public clients.
To set a lifetime of refresh tokens for a specific client, use the

refreshTokenValiditySeconds attribute in the
OAuthClientDetails model.
authserver.publicClients.refreshToken.reuse

Specifies whether refresh tokens are reused on every use of the

false

refresh token flow. If set to false, new refresh tokens are issued for
public clients. Reusing refresh tokens on every flow reuse is part of
the default behavior in OAuth.

authserver.publicClients.rotated.refreshToken.limit.timeToLive

Sets the TTL (time-to-live) for refresh tokens.

true

If reusing refresh tokens for public clients is deactivated through the

authserver.publicClients.refreshToken.reuse=false
property, the default lifetime of new refresh tokens is limited to the
lifetime of the initial refresh tokens that are initially obtained through
the authorization code flow. For example, the refresh token lifetime
is one hour and the access token lifetime is 15 minutes:
1. An access and refresh tokens are issued for a public client.
2. After 15 minutes, the refresh token is used to get a new
access token.
3. The refresh token that is returned is now valid for 45
minutes.
4. This continues until an hour passes from the moment the
initial refresh token was issued.
5. At this point, the refresh token is no longer valid and the user
has to authenticate again through the authorization code
flow.

Client Credentials Flow
To get an access token in a client credentials flow, use the following request:
curl -X POST --location "https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/token" \
-H "Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded" \
-d 'grant_type=client_credentials' \
--basic --user <client_id>:<secret>
You can add the following additional parameter to the authorization code request:

scope: Specifies the parameter that’s responsible for cross-site request forgery prevention

 Note
In Spring 6, parameters can only be transmitted in request-body and must not be included in request URIs. For more information, see
https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc6749#section-2.3.1

.

Custom SAML Token Flow
SAML token flow is a custom grant flow that allows you to obtain access token using the login token issued by the samlsinglesignon extension during the SSO (Single Sign-On) authentication.
The flow can be configured for both public and confidential clients.
To enable the custom SAML token flow, ensure the following:
You have included the samlsinglesignon extension in your configuration.
Your OAuth clients must have the SAML token flow listed as a supported flow in the authorizedGrantTypes attribute
The custom SAML token flow supports the following tokens:

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
access tokens
refresh tokens - only when the relevant client has the refresh_token listed as a supported flow
To request tokens in this flow, use the following endpoint:
https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/token
The following parameters are required in requests:

grant_type=saml_token
client_id=<client_id>
client_secret=<client_secret> - required only for confidential clients
The following parameters are optional:

scope - with space-separated values
The token requests must include the SAML login token with the name matching the sso.cookie.name property.

Custom Token Granter
Previously, implementing a custom token granter was achieved by implementing a TokenGranter interface. In the new authorization server, you can configuring it by following the steps:
1. Implement the CustomAuthenticationConverter interface by creating a new class. This implementation must return an instance of AbstractCustomAuthenticationToken.
Use CustomUserAuthenticationToken for flows that require both users and clients, such as the authorization code flow. For flows that require clients only, such as the client
credentials flow, use CustomClientAuthenticationToken. Authentication providers then use these authentication tokens to generate the necessary OAuth tokens.
To ensure that access tokens include the desired scopes, use the constructor of the AbstractCustomAuthenticationToken implementation that accepts the scopes
parameter. The authorization server later issues a JWT access token that contains the specified scopes in the scope claim.
For flows that require both users and client: To enable refresh tokens, set the generateRefreshToken property to true when creating the

CustomUserAuthenticationToken object. Note that to receive refresh tokens, your OAuth clients must have the refresh token flow listed as a supported flow.
public class ExampleUserAuthenticationConverter implements CustomAuthenticationConverter
{
private static final AuthorizationGrantType EXAMPLE_AUTHORIZATION_GRANT_TYPE = new AuthorizationGrantType("example");
private final UserDetailsService userDetailsService;
public ExampleUserAuthenticationConverter(final UserDetailsService userDetailsService)
{
this.userDetailsService = userDetailsService;
}
@Override
public CustomUserAuthenticationToken convert(final HttpServletRequest request)
{
final String grantType = request.getParameter(OAuth2ParameterNames.GRANT_TYPE);
if (!EXAMPLE_AUTHORIZATION_GRANT_TYPE.getValue().equals(grantType))
{
return null;
}
final String userId = request.getParameter("userId");
final OAuth2ClientAuthenticationToken oAuth2ClientAuthenticationToken = (OAuth2ClientAuthenticationToken) SecurityContextHolder.getCont
.getAuth
final UserDetails loadedUser = userDetailsService.loadUserByUsername(userId);
final Authentication userAuth = new UsernamePasswordAuthenticationToken(userId, null, loadedUser.getAuthorities());
if (someCondition())
{
return new CustomUserAuthenticationToken(userAuth, oAuth2ClientAuthenticationToken, EXAMPLE_AUTHORIZATION_GRANT_TYPE);
}
else
{
throw new OAuth2AuthenticationException(OAuth2ErrorCodes.INVALID_REQUEST);
}
}
private boolean someCondition()
{
return true;
}
}
2. Register your authentication converter as a Spring bean to ensure that it's recognized by the authorization server:
<bean id="exampleUserAuthenticationConverter" class="com.sap.cx.commerce.platform.oauth2.authorizationserver.spring.ExampleUserAuthenticationCo
3. Ensure that the OAuthClientDetails object includes your new grant type in the authorizedGrantTypes attribute.
4. After registering your bean, create requests using it:
curl --request POST \
--url https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/token \
--header 'Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded' \
--data client_id=mobile_android \
--data client_secret=<client_secret> \
--data grant_type=<grant_type> \
--data userId=admin

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

118

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
5. Optionally, if your custom grant flow requires customizations of client authentication, you can create your own AuthenticationConverter and AuthenticationProvider by
implementing CustomAuthenticationPurposeConverter and CustomAuthenticationPurposeProvider and declaring the necessary beans in your Spring configuration file.
The class that implements CustomAuthenticationPurposeConverter is used to validate token requests and the relevant authentication method. The class that implements

CustomAuthenticationPurposeProvider is used to authenticate OAuth clients.
public class ExampleAuthenticationConverter implements CustomAuthenticationPurposeConverter
{
private static final AuthorizationGrantType EXAMPLE_AUTHORIZATION_GRANT_TYPE = new AuthorizationGrantType("example");
@Override
public Authentication convert(final HttpServletRequest request)
{
final String clientId = request.getParameter(OAuth2ParameterNames.CLIENT_ID);
if (!isExampleGrantType(request) || !someCondition(request))
{
return null;
}
final ClientAuthenticationMethod exampleAuthenticationMethod = new ClientAuthenticationMethod("example");
final String credential = request.getParameter(OAuth2ParameterNames.CLIENT_SECRET);
return new OAuth2ClientAuthenticationToken(clientId, exampleAuthenticationMethod, credential, null);
}
private boolean isExampleGrantType(final HttpServletRequest request)
{
final String grantType = request.getParameter(OAuth2ParameterNames.GRANT_TYPE);
return EXAMPLE_AUTHORIZATION_GRANT_TYPE.getValue().equals(grantType);
}
private boolean someCondition(final HttpServletRequest request)
{
return true;
}
}
public class ExampleAuthenticationProvider implements CustomAuthenticationPurposeProvider
{
private static final ClientAuthenticationMethod EXAMPLE_AUTHENTICATION_METHOD = new ClientAuthenticationMethod("example");
private final RegisteredClientRepository registeredClientRepository;
public ExampleAuthenticationProvider(final RegisteredClientRepository registeredClientRepository)
{
this.registeredClientRepository = registeredClientRepository;
}
@Override
public Authentication authenticate(final Authentication authentication) throws AuthenticationException
{
final OAuth2ClientAuthenticationToken clientAuthentication = (OAuth2ClientAuthenticationToken) authentication;
if (!EXAMPLE_AUTHENTICATION_METHOD.equals(clientAuthentication.getClientAuthenticationMethod() || !someCondition(authentication))
{
return null;
}
final String clientId = clientAuthentication.getPrincipal().toString();
final RegisteredClient registeredClient = this.registeredClientRepository.findByClientId(clientId);
validateRegisteredClient(registeredClient);
return new OAuth2ClientAuthenticationToken(registeredClient,clientAuthentication.getClientAuthenticationMethod(), clientAuthentication.
}
@Override
public boolean supports(final Class<?> authentication)
{
return OAuth2ClientAuthenticationToken.class.isAssignableFrom(authentication);
}
private boolean someCondition(final Authentication authentication)
{
return true;
}
private void validateRegisteredClient(final RegisteredClient registeredClient)
{
// method implementation
}
}
<bean id="exampleAuthenticationConverter" class="com.sap.cx.commerce.foo.bar.ExampleAuthenticationConverter"/>
<bean id="exampleAuthenticationProvider" class="com.sap.cx.commerce.foo.bar.ExampleAuthenticationProvider"/>

Token Introspection
To introspect access tokens, use the following request:
curl -X POST --location "https://<server_url>/authorizationserver/oauth/introspect" \
-H "Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded" \
-d 'token=<token>' \
--basic --user <client_id>:<secret>

 Note
In Spring 6, parameters can only be transmitted in request-body and must not be included in request URIs. For more information, see Client Password

.

Accessing Resources with Access Tokens
This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

119

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
To access secured resources, use requests with an HTTP Authorization header containing an access token:
Authorization: Bearer <access-token>

User Roles
For authorization code flow, the authorization server does not include information about user roles in the JWT access tokens. Instead, roles are retrieved from the database when the token is
presented to the resource server, based on the currently signed-in user's assigned groups.

Token Revocation
In the new authorization server, a custom revocation system has been created for access token revocation. Since access tokens aren't meant to be persisted, an in-memory revocation list has been
introduced that is designed to work quickly and be safe for short-lived tokens. Each time an access token is revoked, it's added to the revocation list that is checked against by the system during
each request to the resource server.
The revocation list is applied in the following cases:
Password change
Creation of a new access token with a refresh token with the old access token being revoked when authserver.refreshToken.reuse and

authserver.publicClients.refreshToken.reuse are set to false
Revocation by the /revoke endpoint
Removal of authorization from the database
Deserialization failure when fetching authorization from the database

OpenID
SAP Commerce Cloud supports the OpenID Connect (OIDC) protocol as an OIDC provider. It can now only be used with the authorization code flow since the implicit flow is deprecated.
For more information on how to create OIDC clients, see Platform as an OpenId Connect Identity Provider.
When configuring OIDC, there's no need to create OpenIDClientDetails instances as creating OAuthClientDetails is sufficient. You only need to add the openid scope to

OAuthClientDetails.
The use of ExternalScopes is no longer supported.
Defining separate keystores for each client is no longer supported.

Keystore Configuration
Keys accessible through a JWK endpoint, used for signing JWTs and verifying signatures, are stored in an external keystore file.
Keys used for signing JWTs and verifying signatures are stored in an external keystore and accessible through a JWK endpoint. The generation and rotation of these private keys is fully automatic,
with keys being rotated every sixty days to maintain compliance with SAP security policy.

 Note
The TTL of the JWTs you generate must not exceed sixty days. If a token is older than sixty days, the server refuses to validate it. According to security best practices, the TTL of a JWT should
not exceed a few minutes.

Preventing Brute-Force Attacks
To prevent brute-force attacks, use the following property to set the maximum number of failed client authentication attempts:
oauth2.maxAuthenticationAttempts

Revoking OAuth Tokens on User Disabling
When a user account becomes disabled by the brute force attack protection mechanism or deleted from the system, all the OAuth tokens previously issued to that user are revoked and deleted
from the database. Previous access tokens and refresh tokens become invalid and can't be used anymore. Before getting access tokens for disabled user accounts, re-enable the accounts first.
Any attempt to use a revoked refresh token of a disabled user results in the following error response:
{"error":"invalid_grant"}
When introspecting access and refresh tokens of disabled users, the OAuth authorization server notifies the client that these tokens are inactive.

Changes in Scope Handling
In the new OAuth implementation, scopes are handled differently in requests. The authorization server no longer automatically applies predefined scopes when the scope parameter is omitted
from requests. Consequently, access tokens issued as a response don't include any scope-related claims.
If necessary, update your authorization requests in the authorization code flow and token requests in the client credentials flow to explicitly include any necessary scopes.

Customizing JWT Access Token
To customize JWT access tokens to ensure that they contain custom claims, implement a customizer:

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

120

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
1. Create a new class that implements the ExtensibleOAuth2TokenCustomizer interface:
com.sap.cx.commerce.platform.oauth2.authorizationserver.custom.ExtensibleOAuth2TokenCustomizer
2. Optionally, you can override the Set<AuthorizationGrantType> getSupportedAuthGrantTypes() method and return the set of supported authorization grant types. This
ensures that the customizer is only used for the specified grant types. For example, if you have created a new custom grant type, you can return a set containing only that new grant type in
the getSupportedAuthGrantTypes() method. This way, the customizer is used only when the authorization server is processing the custom grant type, and not for other standard
grant types. If you don't override this method and leave it returning an empty set, the customizer is used for every authorization grant type processed by the authorization server.
3. Create your custom claims by inserting your custom logic in to the customize method:
@Override
public void customize(final JwtEncodingContext context) {
context.getClaims().claims((claims) -> {
claims.put("claim-1", "value-1");
});
}
4. Register your customizer as a bean in your application context:
<bean id="firstCustomizer" class="package.YourJWTCustomizer"/>

Custom Login Pages in Authorization Code Flow
You can implement a custom login page for your storefront in the authorization code flow. For more information, see Custom Login Page.

Verification Process for Existing Clients
After upgrading to the new OAuth implementation, use Backoffice to review your existing clients. There have been changes to the prerequisites for adding and saving clients, as described in the
“Client Validation” section, that could affect your configuration.
After the upgrade, new OAuthClientDetails attributes are available in client configuration in Backoffice. Some of these attributes may not be explicitly set and now have default values:
Require PKCE Proof Key: If this attribute isn't explicitly set, it's activated by default. This means you need to adjust authorization code flow requests for the authorization code flow to
include PKCE. If you don't make this adjustment, you may encounter errors during the authorization code flow requests similar to the following:
error=invalid_request&error_description=OAuth 2.0 Parameter: code_challenge
You can also consider deactivating this attribute for confidential clients if you don't want to include PKCE in your flow.
OAuth require authorization consent: If this attribute isn't explicitly set, it's deactivated by default.
Public client: This attribute is automatically set after the upgrade based on whether a client secret is present. If no secret is present during the upgrade process, this attribute is set to

true.
For more information on the new attributes, see the “Configuring OAuth Clients” section.
The following attributes that were previously optional are now required:
OAuth authorities: At least once authority is required.
OAuth authorized grant types: At least one authorized grant type is required.
Additionally, review and adjust token validity settings as default values have been changed. If you don't modify them, the default values are used.

Orphaned Types Cleanup
After the upgrade, you can clean up outdated or orphaned types that are related to the deprecated oauth2 extension by navigating to

Maintenance

Cleanup

Type System

in SAP

Commerce Cloud Administration Console and performing the cleanup procedure for the following types:

OAuthAccessToken
OAuthAuthorizationCode
OAuthRefreshToken
User2TokenRelation

Punchout Token for Punchout Flow
To generate an oauth token for the punchout flow, we've added a new grant type: punchout_token. This grant type retrieves the token needed to call commerce. It is a non-public client, so the
clientSecret field is now required.
You can customize the clientId and clientSecret by setting value for these properties:
b2bpunchout.oauthclient.clientId=punchout_client
b2bpunchout.oauthclient.clientSecret=secret
Here is a sample impex to add the new grant type:
INSERT_UPDATE OAuthClientDetails;clientId[unique=true]
;punchout_client

;resourceIds

;scope

;authorizedGrantTypes

;authorities

;hybris

;basic

;punchout_token

;ROLE_CLIENT

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

121

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
By default, punchout calls the commerce OAuth token URL to obtain a new token. If you have your own OAuth token URL, update these properties:
b2bpunchout.oauth.host=https://localhost:9002
b2bpunchout.oauth.tokenUrl=/authorizationserver/oauth/token
To securely call the OAuth token URL, use a keystore file to generate the secure client.
You can also ignore host SSL verification by updating this property to true. By default, it is false: b2bpunchout.oauth2.keyselector.http.ssl.ignoreHostnameVerification=false
Additionally, configure the keystore information:
b2bpunchout.keystore.path=your.keystore.path
b2bpunchout.keystore.password=your.keystore.password
b2bpunchout.keystore.type=your.keystore.type

Moving to the New Resource Server
Adjust your resource server configuration to the new OAuth implementation.

Context
To fully move to the new OAuth implementation, adjust your resource server configuration to the new version of the Spring Security library. Unless stated otherwise, all changes should be
introduced in your Spring configuration file.

 Note
There are no changes to the configuration of the Swagger UI.

When migrating your resource server to the new implementation, check your extensions' dependency tree as some steps might have already been covered by an extension configuration that you
have already included in your configuration, for example, in the webservicescommons and apiframework extensions.

Procedure
Import resourceserver-commons-spring.xml
1. Remove the import of the old resource server definition and replace it with the import with a common Spring configuration.
Previous Configuration
<beans:import resource="classpath*:oauth2-resource-spring.xml"/>
Updated Configuration:
<import resource="classpath*:resourceserver-commons-spring.xml"/>

 Note
There's no need to specify a dependency to the resource server extension as it's one of the core extensions that are part of each build.

Remove the resource-server Tag
2. Remove the resource-server tag.
<resource-server id="resourceServerFilter"
token-services-ref="oauthTokenServices"
entry-point-ref="oauthAuthenticationEntryPoint"/>
3. Remove the use of the resource-server filter bean from the security filter chain in the HTTP security configuration.
<custom-filter ref="resourceServerFilter" before="PRE_AUTH_FILTER"/>
Remove oauthAuthenticationEntryPoint Bean
4. Remove the oauthAuthenticationEntryPoint bean for the deprecated OAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint class.
<alias name="defaultOauthAuthenticationEntryPoint" alias="oauthAuthenticationEntryPoint"/>
<bean id="defaultOauthAuthenticationEntryPoint"
class="org.springframework.security.oauth2.provider.error.OAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint"
p:realmName="hybris" p:typeName="Bearer" p:exceptionRenderer-ref="oauth2ExceptionRender"/>
5. Remove the entry-point-ref attribute with OAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint.
<http pattern="/**" entry-point-ref="oauthAuthenticationEntryPoint">
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access=.../>
...
</http>
Configure Authentication Using oauth2-resource-server Tag
6. Use <oauth2-resource-server> instead of <resource-server> to configure authentication.
<http pattern="/**">
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access=.../>
<access-denied-handler ref="enrichingAccessDeniedHandler" />
<oauth2-resource-server entry-point-ref="enrichingAuthenticationEntryPoint">
<jwt decoder-ref="jwtDecoder" jwt-authentication-converter-ref="jwtAuthenticationRoleConverter" />
</oauth2-resource-server>
</http>
a. Decide if you want to configure the entry-point-ref attribute inside the oauth2-resource-server tag. If you don't specify it, the default
BearerTokenAuthenticationEntryPoint is used. You can add a reference to the enrichingAuthenticationEntryPoint bean that is defined in
bin/platform/ext/resourceserver/resources/resourceserver-commons-spring.xml.
<oauth2-resource-server entry-point-ref="enrichingAuthenticationEntryPoint">
...
</oauth2-resource-server>
The enrichingAuthenticationEntryPoint bean ensures that error descriptions are added to the response body in authentication exceptions (HTTP 401 status code Unauthorized access).
{
"error_code": "invalid_token",
"error_description": "An error occurred while attempting to decode the Jwt: Jwt expired at 2024-03-05T12:46:08Z"
}

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

124

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
{
"error_code": "invalid_token",
"error_description": "An error occurred while attempting to decode the Jwt: Malformed token"
}
If you don't use it, the response body is always empty. For more information on BearerTokenAuthenticationEntryPoint being added to the default configuration, see
<oauth2-resource-server> .
b. Remove the oauthAccessDeniedHandler bean and the oauth2ExceptionRender exception renderer for the deprecated OAuth2AccessDeniedHandler and
DefaultOAuth2ExceptionRenderer classes.
<bean id="oauthAccessDeniedHandler" class="org.springframework.security.oauth2.provider.error.OAuth2AccessDeniedHandler"
p:exceptionRenderer-ref="oauth2ExceptionRender" />
<bean id="oauth2ExceptionRender"
class="org.springframework.security.oauth2.provider.error.DefaultOAuth2ExceptionRenderer">
<property name="messageConverters">
<list>
<bean class="org.springframework.http.converter.json.MappingJackson2HttpMessageConverter" />
<bean class="org.springframework.security.oauth2.http.converter.jaxb.JaxbOAuth2ExceptionMessageConverter" />
<bean class="org.springframework.http.converter.StringHttpMessageConverter"
p:writeAcceptCharset="false" />
<bean class="org.springframework.http.converter.ByteArrayHttpMessageConverter" />
</list>
</property>
</bean>
c. Decide if you want to configure access-denied-handler as a replacement for oauthAccessDeniedHandler. If you don't specify it, the default
BearerTokenAccessDeniedHandler is used.
You can add a reference to the enrichingAccessDeniedHandler bean that is defined in bin/platform/ext/resourceserver/resources/resourceserver-

commons-spring.xml.
<http pattern="/**">
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access=.../>
<access-denied-handler ref="enrichingAccessDeniedHandler" />
</http>
The enrichingAccessDeniedHandler bean ensures that error descriptions are added to the response body in access exceptions (HTTP 403 status code - access to the
requested resource is forbidden).
{
"error_code": "insufficient_scope",
"error_description": "The request requires higher privileges than provided by the access token."
}
If you don't use it, the response body will always be empty.
As an alternative, you can define your own custom logic by creating a class that implements the AccessDeniedHandler interface and overrides the handle() method. For more
information on BearerTokenAccessDeniedHandler being added to the default configuration, see <oauth2-resource-server> .
d. Configure the JWT authentication through the <jwt> tag. Use the decoder-ref attribute with a reference to the jwtDecoder bean to use JwtDecoder that’s responsible for
decoding and validating JWTs. Use the jwt-authentication-converter-ref attribute with a reference to the jwtAuthenticationRoleConverter bean to use
JwtAuthenticationConverter that’s responsible for converting JWTs (JSON Web Tokens) into a Collection of granted authorities.
<oauth2-resource-server>
<jwt decoder-ref="jwtDecoder" jwt-authentication-converter-ref="jwtAuthenticationRoleConverter" />
</oauth2-resource-server>
Replace AccessDecisionManager and AccessDecisionVoter with AuthorizationManager
7. Replace the deprecated AccessDecisionManager and AccessDecisionVoter with AuthorizationManager that supersede these two classes.
a. Remove the accessDecisionManager bean along with a list if voters.
<bean id="accessDecisionManager" class="org.springframework.security.access.vote.UnanimousBased"
xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/beans">
<constructor-arg>
<list>
<bean class="org.springframework.security.oauth2.provider.vote.ScopeVoter"/>
<bean class="org.springframework.security.access.vote.RoleVoter"/>
<bean class="org.springframework.security.access.vote.AuthenticatedVoter"/>
<bean class="org.springframework.security.web.access.expression.WebExpressionVoter" />
</list>
</constructor-arg>
</bean>
If you use custom voters, you can replace their functionality by either:
as a probably most simple approach, creating a custom @Bean, which is used in the access expression or the @PreAuthorize annotation. Create your custom class, for
example, a SystemInitializedSecurityChecker class.
public class SystemInitializedSecurityChecker
{
public boolean isNotInitialized()
{ //code }
}
Create a bean.
<bean id="systemInitializedChecker" class="de.hybris.platform.spring.security.expression.SystemInitializedSecurityChecker"/>
This can be used in:
your XML configuration in the access element.
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access="@systemInitializedChecker.isInitialized()"/>
in your Java configuration in the @PreAuthorize annotation.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
@PreAuthorize("@systemInitializedChecker.isInitialized()")
public void someMethod()
{
// some code }
You need to add an explicit reference to org.springframework.security.access.expression.method.DefaultMethodSecurityExpressionHandler.
<bean id="expressionHandler" class="org.springframework.security.access.expression.method.DefaultMethodSecurityExpressionHandler"/>
<method-security pre-post-enabled="true" proxy-target-class="true" secured-enabled="true">
<expression-handler ref="expressionHandler" />
</method-security>
If you don't reference DefaultMethodSecurityExpressionHandler in your configuration, you encounter the following issue:
org.springframework.expression.spel.SpelEvaluationException: EL1057E: No bean resolver registered in the context to resolve access t
For more information on this solution, see Use a Custom @Bean instead of subclassing DefaultMethodSecurityExpressionHandler
Expressions

and Referring to Beans in Web Security

.

adding a new custom expression by sub-classing expression handlers. To use a new expression in your Java configuration, for example, the @PreAuthorize annotation, subclass DefaultMethodSecurityExpressionHandler and SecurityExpressionRoot. This approach requires adding a custom expression handler to your XML
configuration, for example:
<bean id="myMethodSecurityExpressionHandler" class="some.package.CustomMethodSecurityExpressionHandler"> </bean>
<method-security pre-post-enabled="true" proxy-target-class="true" secured-enabled="true">
<expression-handler ref="myMethodSecurityExpressionHandler"/>
</method-security>
To use new expressions in your XML configuration in the access tag, sub-class DefaultHttpSecurityExpressionHandler and WebSecurityExpressionRoot.
This requires adding a custom expression handler to your XML configuration, for example:
<bean id="myHttpSecurityExpressionHandler" class="some.package.CustomHttpSecurityExpressionHandler"> </bean>
<http pattern="/**" use-authorization-manager="true" use-expressions="true" ...>
<expression-handler ref="myHttpSecurityExpressionHandler"/>
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access="customExpression()"/>
...
</http>
For more information, see Use a Custom @Bean instead of subclassing DefaultMethodSecurityExpressionHandler

and Customizing Authorization

.

adding a custom AuthorizationManager. This approach could be problematic as, in a such scenario, the default AuthorizationManager, which handles the access
attribute from the intercept-url element, isn't created by Spring. For more information, see Replace any custom filter-security AccessDecisionManagers

.

For example, in your XML configuration files, you can construct your custom AuthorizationManager as follows:
Create a MyAuthorizationManager class with your custom logic that implements the AuthorizationManager interface.
Define a bean of the org.springframework.security.authorization.AuthorizationManagers class and pass the MyAuthorizationManager class
in the constructor.
Define the factory-method element:
Using the anyOf value, which creates an AuthorizationManager that grants access if at least one AuthorizationManager is granted or abstained. If
managers are empty, then a denied decision is returned.
Using the allOf value, which creates an AuthorizationManager that grants access if all AuthorizationManagers are granted or abstained.
For more information on the anyOf and allOf values, see Class AuthorizationManagers

.

<bean id="myRequestAuthorization" class="org.springframework.security.authorization.AuthorizationManagers" factory-method="anyO
<constructor-arg>
<list>
<bean class="some.package.MyAuthorizationManager"/>
</list>
</constructor-arg>
</bean>
Inside the <http> tag, add a reference to the myRequestAuthorization class through the authorization-manager-ref element.
<http pattern="/**" use-authorization-manager="true" authorization-manager-ref="myRequestAuthorization">
...
</http>
In the myRequestAuthorization bean definition, define just your custom AuthorizationManagers in the constructor list since there's no need to pass the
Spring AuthorizationManagers. This means that if you use the @PreAuthorize() annotation, the corresponding PreAuthorizeAuthorizationManager
is called out automatically.
However, expressions defined inside the access element aren't validated in the custom AuthorizationManager approach.
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access="isFullyAuthenticated()"/>
It's caused by the fact that when you explicitly set authorization-manager-ref to your custom AuthorizationManager, Spring doesn't create the default

org.springframework.security.web.access.intercept.RequestMatcherDelegatingAuthorizationManager manager.
RequestMatcherDelegatingAuthorizationManager matches requests with the most appropriate delegate AuthorizationManager by calling
WebExpressionAuthorizationManager.check() and, as a result, evaluating expressions from the access element. For more information, see Delegate-based
AuthorizationManager Implementations

.

b. Remove the access-decision-manager-ref attribute and replace it with use-authorization-manager="true".
Previous Configuration:
<http pattern="/**" access-decision-manager-ref="accessDecisionManager">
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access=.../>

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
...
</http>

<http pattern="/**" use-authorization-manager="true">
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access=.../>
...
</http>
For more information on the AuthorizationManager replacing AccessDecisionManager and AccessDecisionVoter, see Architecture

.

Implement Spring EL Expressions
8. To secure individual URLs, use Spring EL expressions.
a. Add use-expressions="true" to the <http> tag to enable Spring EL expressions. Spring Security will now expect the access attributes of the <intercept-url> elements
to contain Spring EL expressions. These expressions should evaluate to a Boolean, defining whether access should be allowed or not.
<http pattern="/**" use-authorization-manager="true" use-expressions="true">
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access="isFullyAuthenticated() and hasAuthority('SCOPE_READ') and hasRole('ROLE_BUSINESSADMINGROUP')"/>
...
</http>
If you didn't use Spring EL expressions so far, your access attributes looked like the following:
access="IS_AUTHENTICATED_FULLY, ROLE_BUSINESSADMINGROUP, SCOPE_READ"
Access rules were previously evaluated by voters, which are deprecated and recommended not to be used. For example, IS_AUTHENTICATED_FULLY was evaluated by
AuthenticatedVoter, which should now be replaced with the access="isFullyAuthenticated() expression. Similarly, SCOPE_READ should be replaced with
hasAuthority('SCOPE_READ') and ROLE_BUSINESSADMINGROUP with hasRole('ROLE_BUSINESSADMINGROUP').
For a list of common built-in expressions, such as isFullyAuthenticated(), hasAuthority(String authority), hasRole(String role), see Common Built-In
Expressions .
For more information on Spring EL expressions, see Expression-Based Access Control

.

b. Check if you use the @oauthSecurityChecker.hasScope() method in the intercept-url tag in the access attribute for scope checking. The
de.hybris.platform.oauth2.util.OAuth2SecurityChecker class is provided with the removed oauth2 extension. Replace it with a usage of the hasAuthority()
method that is provided with Spring Security.
Previous Configuration:
<intercept-url pattern="/**" method="GET" access="@oauthSecurityChecker.hasScope(authentication,'basic')"/>
Updated Configuration:
<intercept-url pattern="/**" method="GET" access="hasAuthority('SCOPE_basic')"/>
For more information on the Spring Security built-in methods, see Common Built-In Expressions

.

Replace enable global method security with enable security
9. Replace “enable global method security” with “method security”. You can use annotation-based configuration using the EnableMethodSecurity annotation on any @Configuration
instance. @EnableGlobalMethodSecurity and <global-method-security> are deprecated in favor of @EnableMethodSecurity and <method-security>, respectively. The
new annotation and XML elements activate Spring’s pre-post annotations by default and use AuthorizationManager internally.
a. In your XML configuration files, replace <global-method-security> with the <method-security> tag.
<global-method-security pre-post-annotations="enabled" proxy-target-class="true" secured-annotations="enabled"/>

 Note
The <method security> attribute names have been changed in the new implementation. For example, the secured-annotations attribute is now secured-enabled.
For more information on the <method security> attributes, see <method-security> attributes

.

The @Secured and @PreAuthorize annotations should work as before.
b. If you use the @EnableGlobalMethodSecurity annotation in your Java configuration, replace it with @EnableMethodSecurity.
c. Remove the usage of the oauthExpressionHandler Spring bean and the expression-handler tag.
<method-security pre-post-enabled="true" proxy-target-class="true" secured-enabled="true">
<expression-handler ref="oauthExpressionHandler"/>
</method-security>
<expression-handler id="oauthExpressionHandler"/>
<web-expression-handler id="oauthWebExpressionHandler"/>
The org.springframework.security.oauth2.provider.expression.OAuth2MethodSecurityExpressionHandler comes with the removed Spring Security
OAuth library. As described in Class OAuth2MethodSecurityExpressionHandler , OAuth2MethodSecurityExpressionHandler is a security expression handler that can
handle default method security expressions plus the set provided by OAuth2SecurityExpressionMethods using the variable oauth2 to access the methods. For example, the
expression #oauth2.clientHasRole('ROLE_ADMIN') would invoke OAuth2SecurityExpressionMethods.clientHasRole(java.lang.String).
This means that methods provided by OAuth2MethodSecurityExpressionHandler could be replaced by one of the Spring Security built-in methods listed in Common Built-In
Expressions

.

d. You might have used the @PreAuthorize annotation with a custom bean in your controller.
@PreAuthorize("@authz.isAdmin(#root)")
To be able to reference your custom bean, you need to define a SecurityExpressionHandler instance through the expression-handler tag inside the method-security
tag with a reference to DefaultMethodSecurityExpressionHandler.
<method-security pre-post-enabled="true" proxy-target-class="true" secured-enabled="true">
<expression-handler ref="expressionHandler" />
</method-security>
<bean id="expressionHandler" class="org.springframework.security.access.expression.method.DefaultMethodSecurityExpressionHandler"/>

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
For more information, see EnableMethodSecurity

and Replace global method security with method security

.

Reference Authentication Manager

file.
<authentication-manager id="authenticationManager" xmlns="http://www.springframework.org/schema/security">
<authentication-provider ref="wsAuthenticationProvider"/>
</authentication-manager>
Replace hybrisUserFilter
11. Remove the hybrisUserFilter bean since hybrisUserFilter uses the deprecated OAuth2Authentication class. Replace it with
com.sap.cx.commerce.platform.oauth2.resourceserver.filter.JwtAuthenticationUserFilter that is already defined in
resourceserver/resources/resourceserver-spring.xml.
Previous Configuration:
<bean id="hybrisUserFilter" class="de.hybris.platform.webservicescommons.oauth2.HybrisOauth2UserFilter" />
<http pattern="/**">
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access=.../>
<custom-filter ref="hybrisUserFilter" after="LAST" />
</http>
Updated Configuration:
<http pattern="/**">
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access=.../>
<custom-filter ref="jwtAuthenticationUserFilter" after="LAST" />
</http>
a. If you use other custom UserFilter or UserMatchingFilter, make sure that they work properly as it might be necessary to adjust their implementation to use
org.springframework.security.oauth2.server.resource.authentication.JwtAuthenticationToken and avoid casting errors.
INFO

[hybrisHTTP38] [AbstractRestHandlerExceptionResolver] Translating exception [java.lang.ClassCastException]: class org.springframewo

ERROR [hybrisHTTP38] [AbstractRestHandlerExceptionResolver] java.lang.ClassCastException: class org.springframework.security.oauth2.jwt.Jw
As in JwtAuthenticationUserFilter.java

, the configuration needs to be adjusted since Authentication.getPrincipal() used to return a String object, and now it returns an

org.springframework.security.oauth2.jwt.Jwt object.
Session Fixation Protection
12. You might have the following configuration of session fixation protection.
<bean id="fixation" class="de.hybris.platform.servicelayer.security.spring.HybrisSessionFixationProtectionStrategy"/>
<http pattern="/**">
<session-management session-authentication-strategy-ref="fixation" />
<intercept-url pattern="/**" access=.../>
...
</http>

HybrisSessionFixationProtectionStrategy extends Spring Security's SessionFixationProtectionStrategy that is used to protect against session fixation attacks.
SessionFixationProtectionStrategy is added to the default configuration by Spring Security, but it always gets replaced with
HybrisSessionFixationProtectionStrategy by RemoveDefaultSessionFixationStrategyBeanPostProcessor for each web application. If there's no instance of
HybrisSessionFixationProtectionStrategy, RemoveDefaultSessionFixationStrategyBeanPostProcessor creates one. This means that you don't need to specify
the HybrisSessionFixationProtectionStrategy bean explicitly in your configuration or inject it as an instance of SessionAuthenticationStrategy that is used by
SessionManagementFilter in the session-authentication-strategy-ref tag. You can remove the HybrisSessionFixationProtectionStrategy bean and the
session-management tag if you've used it in your configuration.
Replace Deprecated Message Converters
13. Check if you use any deprecated message converters in the annotation-driven configuration, such as JaxbOAuth2AccessTokenMessageConverter or
JaxbOAuth2ExceptionMessageConverter. Consider replacing them with OAuth2AccessTokenResponseHttpMessageConverter and
OAuth2ErrorHttpMessageConverter.
Previous Configuration:
<mvc:annotation-driven>
<mvc:message-converters register-defaults="false">
...
<bean class="org.springframework.security.oauth2.http.converter.jaxb.JaxbOAuth2AccessTokenMessageConverter"/>
<bean class="org.springframework.security.oauth2.http.converter.jaxb.JaxbOAuth2ExceptionMessageConverter"/>
</mvc:message-converters>
</mvc:annotation-driven>
Updated Configuration:
org.springframework.security.oauth2.core.http.converter.OAuth2AccessTokenResponseHttpMessageConverter
org.springframework.security.oauth2.core.http.converter.
Remove oauth2 Extension Dependency
14. In the extensioninfo.xml file of your extension, remove the oauth2 dependency.
<requires-extension name="oauth2"/>
Test Update Steps
15. Update tests that use OAuth with an embedded server. Instead of manually retrieving tokens, the SignedJWTTokenFactory is now used in the Spring test context. The
SignedJWTTokenFactory class generates RSA keys and creates customizable tokens. To ensure that the resource server can decode these tokens, WireMock is used to stub endpoints
that the JWTDecoder requests for JWKS. To streamline the setup, use the @ResourceServerTest annotation alongside @NeedsEmbeddedServer. Remember that
@ResourceServerTest is recognized by ResourceServerRunListener for resource server tests. See an example of a test with @ResourceServerTest.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

import javax.ws.rs.core.MediaType;
import javax.ws.rs.core.Response;
import org.junit.Test;
import com.nimbusds.jwt.SignedJWT;
import com.sap.cx.commerce.api.framework.testsupport.client.WsSecuredRequestBuilder;
import com.sap.cx.commerce.api.framework.testsupport.server.NeedsEmbeddedServer;
import com.sap.cx.commerce.platform.oauth2.resourceserver.constants.ResourceserverConstants;
import com.sap.cx.commerce.platform.oauth2.resourceserver.testframework.tokenfactory.SignedJWTTokenFactory;
import com.sap.cx.commerce.platform.oauth2.resourceserver.testframework.runlistener.ResourceServerTest;
@ResourceServerTest
@NeedsEmbeddedServer(webExtensions =
{ ResourceserverConstants.EXTENSIONNAME })
@IntegrationTest
public class SignedJWTTokenFactoryTest extends ServicelayerBaseTest
{
private final static String OAUTH_WHO_AM_I_PATH = "oauth/whoami";
protected static final Set<String> AUTHORITIES = Set.of("ROLE_USER", "ROLE_CLIENT", "ROLE_CUSTOM");
private final static String USER_UID = "testuser";
@Resource
private SignedJWTTokenFactory signedJWTTokenFactory;
@Resource
private ModelService modelService;
@Test
public void shouldAllowAccessToWhoAmIEndpointWithValidJWTSignature()
{
final Set<PrincipalGroupModel> groups = setupPrincipalGroups();
final CustomerModel customer = setupCustomer(groups);
final SignedJWT jwt = signedJWTTokenFactory.builder()
.roles(AUTHORITIES)
.subject(USER_UID)
.build();
final WsSecuredRequestBuilder wsSecuredRequestBuilder = new WsSecuredRequestBuilder().extensionName(
ResourceserverConstants.EXTENSIONNAME)
.path(OAUTH_WHO_AM_I_PATH)
.jwtAuthorization(jwt.serialize());
final Response response = wsSecuredRequestBuilder.build().accept(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON_TYPE).get();
assertEquals(" HTTP status at response: " + response.getStatus(), Response.Status.OK.getStatusCode(),
response.getStatus());
assertThat(response.readEntity(String.class)).contains(customer.getUid());
}
@Test
public void shouldDenyAccessToWhoAmIEndpointWithInvalidJWTSignature()
{
final SignedJWTTokenFactory tokenFactoryWithDifferentRsaKey = new SignedJWTTokenFactory();
final Set<PrincipalGroupModel> groups = setupPrincipalGroups();
setupCustomer(groups);
final SignedJWT jwt = tokenFactoryWithDifferentRsaKey.builder()
.roles(AUTHORITIES)
.subject(USER_UID)
.build();
final WsSecuredRequestBuilder wsSecuredRequestBuilder = new WsSecuredRequestBuilder().extensionName(
ResourceserverConstants.EXTENSIONNAME)
.path(OAUTH_WHO_AM_I_PATH)
.jwtAuthorization(jwt.serialize());
final Response response = wsSecuredRequestBuilder.build().accept(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON_TYPE).get();
assertEquals(" HTTP status at response: " + response.getStatus(), Response.Status.UNAUTHORIZED.getStatusCode(),
response.getStatus());
}
@Test
public void shouldAllowAccessToWhoAmIEndpointWithDifferentRoles()
{
final Set<PrincipalGroupModel> groups = setupPrincipalGroups();
final CustomerModel customer = setupCustomer(groups);
final Set<String> roles = Set.of("ROLE_ADMIN", "ROLE_USER");
final SignedJWT jwt = signedJWTTokenFactory.builder()
.roles(roles)
.subject(USER_UID)
.build();
final WsSecuredRequestBuilder wsSecuredRequestBuilder = new WsSecuredRequestBuilder().extensionName(
ResourceserverConstants.EXTENSIONNAME)
.path(OAUTH_WHO_AM_I_PATH)
.jwtAuthorization(jwt.serialize());
final Response response = wsSecuredRequestBuilder.build().accept(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON_TYPE).get();
assertEquals(" HTTP status at response: " + response.getStatus(), Response.Status.OK.getStatusCode(),
response.getStatus());
assertThat(response.readEntity(String.class)).contains(customer.getUid());
}

@Test
public void shouldDenyAccessToWhoAmIEndpointWithExpiredJWT()
{
final Set<PrincipalGroupModel> groups = setupPrincipalGroups();
setupCustomer(groups);
final SignedJWT jwt = signedJWTTokenFactory.builder()
.roles(AUTHORITIES)
.subject(USER_UID)
.issuedAt(Instant.now().minus(Duration.ofDays(1)))
.duration(Duration.ofHours(1))
.build();
final WsSecuredRequestBuilder wsSecuredRequestBuilder = new WsSecuredRequestBuilder().extensionName(
ResourceserverConstants.EXTENSIONNAME)
.path(OAUTH_WHO_AM_I_PATH)
.jwtAuthorization(jwt.serialize());
final Response response = wsSecuredRequestBuilder.build().accept(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON_TYPE).get();
assertEquals(" HTTP status at response: " + response.getStatus(), Response.Status.UNAUTHORIZED.getStatusCode(),
response.getStatus());
}
@Test
public void shouldAllowAccessToWhoAmIEndpointWithCustomClaims()
{
final Set<PrincipalGroupModel> groups = setupPrincipalGroups();
final CustomerModel customer = setupCustomer(groups);
final SignedJWT jwt = signedJWTTokenFactory.builder()
.roles(AUTHORITIES)
.subject(USER_UID)
.jwtClaims(claims -> claims.claim("customClaim", "customValue"))
.build();
final WsSecuredRequestBuilder wsSecuredRequestBuilder = new WsSecuredRequestBuilder().extensionName(
ResourceserverConstants.EXTENSIONNAME)
.path(OAUTH_WHO_AM_I_PATH)
.jwtAuthorization(jwt.serialize());
final Response response = wsSecuredRequestBuilder.build().accept(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON_TYPE).get();
assertEquals(" HTTP status at response: " + response.getStatus(), Response.Status.OK.getStatusCode(),
response.getStatus());
assertThat(response.readEntity(String.class)).contains(customer.getUid());
}
private Set<PrincipalGroupModel> setupPrincipalGroups()
{
final PrincipalGroupModel testGroup1 = modelService.create(UserGroupModel.class);
testGroup1.setUid("TEST_GROUP1");
final PrincipalGroupModel testGroup2 = modelService.create(UserGroupModel.class);
testGroup2.setUid("TEST_GROUP2");
modelService.saveAll(testGroup1, testGroup2);
return Set.of(testGroup1, testGroup2);
}
private CustomerModel setupCustomer(final Set<PrincipalGroupModel> principalGroups)
{
final CustomerModel user = modelService.create(CustomerModel.class);
user.setUid(USER_UID);
user.setName(USER_UID);
user.setGroups(principalGroups);
modelService.save(user);
return user;
}
}
Since @ResourceServerTest starts the WireMock server and replaces the JWKS URI configuration, you can't use both @ResourceServerTest and the real authorization server in one
class. For example, you can't use @ResourceServerTest with @NeedsEmbeddedServer(extensions = "authorizationserver").
When creating a token using SignedJWTTokenFactory, it's crucial to set an appropriate expiration time for tokens. Use the duration method to specify the token's lifespan, for example,

duration(Duration.ofMinutes(4). Avoid setting excessively long expiration times. Tokens with extended lifespans undergo additional verification, which fails for tokens generated
by SignedJWTTokenFactory. This verification process activates for tokens exceeding the threshold defined by the

resourceserver.revoked.access.tokens.store.longttl.threshold=300 property. Ensure that the token's expiration time remains below this threshold to prevent
verification failures.
Configuration of Read and Connection Timeout for JwtDecoder
16. You might want to customize the process of decoding access tokens to include additional validations or conversions to modify the way JWT access tokens are validated and converted. To
implement custom validations or conversions:
a. Extend the DefaultJwtConfigProvider class.
com.sap.cx.commerce.platform.oauth2.resourceserver.config.impl.DefaultJwtConfigProvider
b. Customize token validators by overriding the getOAuth2TokenValidators() method.
The following validators are provided in the default configuration:

JwtTimestampValidator - an implementation of OAuth2TokenValidator for verifying expiration time for JWTs.
JWTRevocationTokenValidator - a validator for JWT access tokens which checks the tokens against a disallow list that is stored in the
RevokedAccessTokensStore.
The validators are run during the decode process. They ensure that JWT access tokens meet specific requirements and are valid for further processing. Because of that, make sure
that these validators are also returned in the overridden method.
@Override
Collection<OAuth2TokenValidator<Jwt>> getOAuth2TokenValidators(){
Collection<OAuth2TokenValidator<Jwt>> extendedValidatorList = new LinkedList<>(super.getOAuth2TokenValidators());
extendedValidatorList.add(new YourOAuth2TokenValiator());

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
return extendedValidatorList;
}
c. Customize authority converters by overriding getGrantedAuthorityConverters(). Overriding this method allows you to add your custom granted authority converters that
translate JWTs into a collection of GrantedAuthority. Make sure that the converters provided in the default configuration in DefaultJwtConfigProvider are returned in the
overridden method.
@Override
Collection<Converter<Jwt, Collection<GrantedAuthority>>> getGrantedAuthorityConverters(){
final Collection<Converter<Jwt, Collection<GrantedAuthority>>> extendedConveterList = new LinkedList<>(super.getGrantedAuthorityConve
extendedConveterList.add(new YourOAuth2GrantedAuthorityConverter());
return extendedConveterList;
}
d. Register your custom implementation bean.
<bean id="jwtConfigProvider" class="package.YourJwtConfigProviderCustomization"/>

Troubleshooting
Procedure
To resolve the issue with users not being able to log in as agent in ASM mode on the B2B storefront with the punchoutaddon enabled, follow these steps:
In the b2bacceleratoraddon/resources/b2bacceleratoraddon/web/spring/b2bacceleratoraddon-spring-security-config.xm and the
b2bpunchoutaddon/resources/b2bpunchoutaddon/web/spring/b2bpunchoutaddon-spring-security-config.xml files, remove the definition of the
csrfTokenRequestAttributeHandler:
<bean id="csrfTokenRequestAttributeHandler" class="org.springframework.security.web.csrf.XorCsrfTokenRequestAttributeHandler" />
This issue arises because the spring security configurations in the b2bpunchoutaddon and the b2bacceleratoraddon override the csrfTokenRequestAttributeHandler configuration in the
B2B storefront web. This results in an empty CSRF token.
To ensure individual URLs use Spring EL expressions, use the AuthorizationManager with use-expressions="true". Update the configuration in the
b2bpunchoutaddon/resources/b2bpunchoutaddon/web/spring/b2bpunchoutaddon-spring-security-config.xml file. Change the following from:
<security:http pattern="${b2bpunchoutaddon.mapping.cxml.pattern}"
...
<security:intercept-url pattern="/**" requires-channel="https" />

disable-url-rewriting="true" use-expressions="false">

to
<security:http pattern="${b2bpunchoutaddon.mapping.cxml.pattern}" disable-url-rewriting="true" use-expressions="true">
...
<security:intercept-url pattern="/**" access="permitAll()" requires-channel="https" />
To resolve the login requirement issue, update the Spring Security configuration. Add the parameter security-context-explicit-save="false" to the spring-securityconfig.xml file. In the b2bpunchoutaddon/resources/b2bpunchoutaddon/web/spring/b2bpunchoutaddon-spring-security-config.xml file, modify the
configuration by including security-context-explicit-save="false" as shown:
<security:http pattern="${b2bpunchoutaddon.mapping.cxml.pattern}" disable-url-rewriting="true" use-expressions="true" security-context-explicit
This issue arises because the behavior of some classes has changed in Spring Security 6. Currently, the SecurityContextHolderFilter only reads the SecurityContext from the
SecurityContextRepository and populates it in the SecurityContextHolder.

Context
If your extensions are generated from the ycommercewebservicestest template, perform the following steps to adopt them for the new resource server.

Procedure

/*

package de.hybris.platform.ycommercewebservicestest.setup;

public void start()
{
if (this.wireMockManager == null)
{
final var rsaKey = signedJWTTokenFactory.getRsaKey();
this.wireMockManager = new ResourceServerWireMockManager(rsaKey);
}
wireMockManager.start();
}
public void stop()
{
if (this.wireMockManager != null)
{
wireMockManager.stop();
}
}
