Note

In the Spock test setup for a class annotated with org.junit.platform.suite.api.Suite, the ResourceServerTestManager#start method should be called before all
other embedded servers start. In the teardown process, the ResourceServerTestManager#stop method should be called after all other hooks have completed.
Update the following code for all suite classes: AbstractSpockTest.groovy, AllSpockTests.groovy, AllSpockTestsJUnit5MigratedSuite.groovy,
AllAccSpockTests.groovy, and AllAccSpockTestsJUnit5MigratedSuite.groovy.

protected refreshOAuth2Token(RESTClient client, refreshToken, clientId, clientSecret, redirectUri) {
def bodyParams = [
'grant_type'
: 'refresh_token',
'refresh_token': refreshToken
]
if (clientId) {
bodyParams['client_id'] = clientId
}
if (clientSecret) {
bodyParams['client_secret'] = clientSecret
}
if (redirectUri) {
bodyParams['redirect_uri'] = URLEncoder.encode(redirectUri, 'UTF-8')
}
HttpResponseDecorator response = client.post(
uri: getOAuth2TokenUri(),
path: getOAuth2TokenPath(),
body: bodyParams,
contentType: JSON,
requestContentType: URLENC)
with(response) {
if (isNotEmpty(data) && isNotEmpty(data.errors)) println(data)
assert status == SC_OK
assert data.token_type == 'bearer'
assert data.access_token
assert data.expires_in
assert data.refresh_token
}
return response.data
}
Updated Configuration:
protected void addAuthorization(RESTClient client, token) {
client.addHeader("Authorization", " Bearer " + (token as String))
}
protected SignedJWT getSignedJWT(final String username, final String clientId)
{
final var authorities = new HashSet<>(AUTHORITIES);
if (clientId.equals("trusted_client"))
{
authorities.add("ROLE_TRUSTED_CLIENT")
}
final var builder = getSignedJWTTokenFactory().builder()
.roles(authorities)
.duration(Duration.ofSeconds(180));
if (username != null)
{
builder.subject(username)
}
return builder.build();
}
protected SignedJWTTokenFactory getSignedJWTTokenFactory()
{
if (signedJWTTokenFactory == null)
{
signedJWTTokenFactory = Registry.getApplicationContext()
.getBean("signedJWTTokenFactory", SignedJWTTokenFactory.class);
}
return signedJWTTokenFactory
}

Model and Spring Bean Changes
Analyze changes in models and Spring beans to fully migrate to the new OAuth implementation.
In the new OAuth implementation, authorization-related data is stored differently than previously. All data is now stored in the SAPOAuth2Authorization model and the old models have been
removed.

Removed Models
The following models have been removed:
Removed Models
Removed Model

Description

Related Database Table

OAuthAccessTokenModel

Object for storing access tokens.

OAUTHACCESSTOKEN
OAUTHACCESSTOKE6228SN

OAuthRefreshTokenModel

Object for storing refresh tokens.

OAUTHREFRESHTOKEN
OAUTHREFRESHTOK6229SN

OAuthAuthorizationCodeModel

Object for storing authorization codes.

OAUTHAUTHORIZATIONCODE
OAUTHAUTHORIZAT6231SN

 Note
In newer versions of Spring Security, several classes that have been removed and replaced with appropriate equivalents. Review your compilation logs to ensure that all new classes have been
adjusted to fit your custom implementations.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

134

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
For example, the OAuth2Authentication class has been replaced with specific authentication token types. For OAuth2 resource server authentication, replace all instances of

OAuth2Authentication with JwtAuthenticationToken, which extends AbstractOAuth2TokenAuthenticationToken. Modify your token access logic to use
getToken().getTokenValue() instead of the previous token retrieval methods.

Modified Models
The model that is used for storing OAuth client data remains the same but has been adapted to the new OAuth server implementation:
Modified Models
Model

New Attributes

Deprecated Attributes

OAuthClientDetailsModel

authenticationMethods - contains a set of authentication

auto-approve - defines a set of auto-approved scopes. This

methods that clients can use to authenticate themselves.

attribute is not used anymore as it's no longer possible to define
specific scopes that are approved automatically. In the new
implementation, all scopes are approved automatically or a
consent page is displayed. This behavior can be configured through

requireAuthorizationConsent.
authorizationCodeValiditySeconds - configures the

resourceIds

validity of authorization codes (in seconds).

requireProofKey - determines whether the PKCE flow is
required for all authorization code requests.

public - determines whether a client is public or confidential.
requireAuthorizationConsent - defines if a consent screen
should be displayed to a user during the authorization request flow.

loginPageUri - defines an URI of an external login page.
authorizations - defines a collection of
SAPOAuth2Authorization objects related to a client.
oidcTokenValiditySeconds - defines the validity of OIDC
tokens (in seconds).

Deprecated Models
The following models have been deprecated:
Deprecated Models
Model

Description

OpenIDClientDetailsModel

OAuth client that is used for OpenID connect. It contains additional parameters required to support
OpenID Connect. The parameters are not used in the new OAuth implementation.
Features such as external scopes and client-specific keystore definitions are not supported anymore.
OpenID clients should be redefined as standard OAuthClientDetailsModel.
For more information on configuring OpenID Connect, see Moving to the New OAuth Implementation.

OpenIDExternalScopesModel

Model that is used to define external scopes that can be added to a token in OpenID Connect.
External scopes are not supported in the new implementation.
For more information on configuring OpenID Connect, see Moving to the New OAuth Implementation.

Updating oAuthClient for SmartEdit

Procedure

INSERT_UPDATE OAuthClientDetails;clientId[unique=true];resourceIds;scope[mode=append];authorizedGrantTypes;accessTokenValiditySeconds;authorities;reg
;smartedit;hybris;basic,permissionswebservices;authorization_code,saml_token;3600;ROLE_ADMINGROUP,ROLE_BASECMSMANAGERGROUP,ROLE_PREVIEWMANAGERGROUP;

 Note

Updating Exception and Error Handling for Webservices
Implement new exception and error handling beans and handlers for your webservices extensions.

Introduction of New Error Handling Beans for Webservices
To be consistent with the error-handling process of SAP Commerce Webservices, the oAuth2AccessDeniedHandler and oAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint beans were defined in the

webservicescommons/resources/webservicescommons/commons-security-spring.xml file:
<bean id="oAuth2AccessDeniedHandler" class="de.hybris.platform.webservicescommons.oauth2.OAuth2AccessDeniedHandler">
<constructor-arg name="restHandlerExceptionResolver" ref="restHandlerExceptionResolver"/>
</bean>
<bean id="oAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint"
class="de.hybris.platform.webservicescommons.oauth2.OAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint">
<constructor-arg name="restHandlerExceptionResolver" ref="restHandlerExceptionResolver"/>
</bean>
The oAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint bean extends the EnrichingAccessDeniedHandler and the oAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint extends the

EnrichingAuthenticationEntryPoint defined in platform's resourceserver extension. The beans were introduced because the enrichingAuthenticationEntryPoint and the
enrichingAccessDeniedHandler beans defined in the resourceserver extension use the error-handling process provided in the Spring framework instead of the process used in the SAP
Commerce Webservices.

Making the Error Handling Beans Availabe in the Web Application Context
To make the oAuth2AccessDeniedHandler and the oAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint beans available in the web application context, you must configure a

restHandlerExceptionResolver bean that implements the org.springframework.web.servlet.HandlerExceptionResolver interface. A
restHandlerExceptionResolver bean should already be defined in the error-config-spring.xml file of your webservices extensions.
The following code shows how to configure a restHandlerExceptionResolver bean that implements the org.springframework.web.servlet.HandlerExceptionResolver
interface in the error-config-spring.xml file. In the example, the bean is configured in the ywebservices extension:

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

138

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
<bean id="restHandlerExceptionResolver" class="de.hybris.platform.webservicescommons.resolver.RestExceptionResolver"
parent="wsBaseRestExceptionResolver">
<property name="webserviceErrorFactory" ref="webserviceErrorFactory" />
<property name="messageConverters" ref="jaxbMessageConverters" />
<property name="extensionName" value="ywebservices" />
</bean>

Adopting the Error-Handling Process Used in the SAP Commerce Webservices
To adopt the error-handling process used in the SAP Commerce Webservices, configure the entry-point-ref for the oauth2-resource-server and the ref for the access-denied-

handler in the Spring Security configuration file of your web extension, for example, myWebservice-security-spring.xml. The following code shows an example:
<security:access-denied-handler ref="oAuth2AccessDeniedHandler" />
<security:oauth2-resource-server entry-point-ref="oAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint">

Configuring Exception Handling
You can configure exception mappings, such as exception messages and logging, to be used by the oAuth2AccessDeniedHandler and the oAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint security
handlers. You configure the exception mapping in the project.properties file of your webservices extension. The following code excerpt shows the configuration for the

AuthorizationDeniedException, AuthenticationCredentialsNotFoundException, AuthenticationCredentialsNotFoundException, and the
InvalidBearerTokenException exceptions:
webservicescommons.resthandlerexceptionresolver.<yourextensionname>.AuthorizationDeniedException.logstack=false
webservicescommons.resthandlerexceptionresolver.<yourextensionname>.AuthorizationDeniedException.status=401
webservicescommons.resthandlerexceptionresolver.<yourextensionname>.AuthenticationCredentialsNotFoundException.logstack=false
webservicescommons.resthandlerexceptionresolver.<yourextensionname>.AuthenticationCredentialsNotFoundException.status=401
webservicescommons.resthandlerexceptionresolver.<yourextensionname>.InsufficientAuthenticationException.logstack=false
webservicescommons.resthandlerexceptionresolver.<yourextensionname>.InsufficientAuthenticationException.status=401
webservicescommons.resthandlerexceptionresolver.<yourextensionname>.InvalidBearerTokenException.logstack=false
webservicescommons.resthandlerexceptionresolver.<yourextensionname>.InvalidBearerTokenException.status=401

 Note
You can configure exception mapping, but you can't fully configure the response statuses to be used by the oAuth2AccessDeniedHandler and oAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint
security handlers. These handlers preserve the response status set by the EnrichingAccessDeniedHandler and EnrichingAuthenticationEntryPoint base classes respectively,
if they are set. If they are not set, the response status set uses the response status set through the mapping. The response status codes are configured as in the previous version of the SAP
Commerce, with the exception of the oAuth2AccessDeniedHandler and the oAuth2AuthenticationEntryPoint security handlers.

Preparing for the Removal of All RestTemplate and OAuth2RestTemplate Classes and Methods for
the kymaintegration Extension
To ensure that this change is compatible with your custom implementations, prepare for the removal of RestTemplate and OAuth2RestTemplate classes and methods for the kymaintegration
extension.

Context
RestClient is replacing RestTemplate for the kymaintegration extension. Follow the procedure below if you have custom implementations that contain any RestTemplate code.

<property name="restTemplate" ref="kymaDestinationRestTemplateWrapper"/>
<property name="restTemplate" ref="kymaCertificateRestTemplate"/>
Change to:
<property name="restClientWrapper" ref="kymaDestinationRestClientWrapper"/>

b. Previous Configuration
<property name="kymaDestinationRestTemplateWrapper" ref="kymaDestinationRestTemplateWrapper"/>
<property name="kymaEventRestTemplateWrapper" ref="kymaEventRestTemplateWrapper"/>

Change to:
<property name="kymaDestinationRestClientWrapper" ref="kymaDestinationRestClientWrapper"/>
<property name="kymaEventRestClientWrapper" ref="kymaEventRestClientWrapper"/>
2. Update any customized Java code that uses {{de.hybris.platform.kymaintegrationservices.utils.RestTemplateWrapper}} with
{{de.hybris.platform.kymaintegrationservices.utils.RestClientWrapper}}.

Review all manual steps related to Apache libraries update and adapt your SAP Commerce Cloud implementation accordingly.
1. Updating to Commons Configuration 2.x usage
Adjust your implementation after Apache Commons Configuration 1.x was replaced with Apache Commons Configuration 2.
2. Updating to Commons Lang 3.x
Adapt to Apache Commons Lang 3. Apache Commons Lang 2 library is now in the end of life state and it was replaced by Apache Commons Lang 3.
3. Adapting to Apache HttpComponents 5
If your extensions are generated from ycommercewebservicestest template, perform the following steps to adapt to Apache HttpComponents 5.
4. Preparing for the Removal of Apache Commons Pool 1.6
Prepare for the removal of Apache Commons Pool 1.6 to ensure that this change remains compatible with your custom implementations.
5. Removal of Apache Commons Math 3.6
Adjust your configuration after the removal of the Apache Commons Math 3.6 library to ensure that this change doesn't break your custom code.
6. Apache Commons Collections and Apache Commons BeanUtils Upgrades
The Apache Commons Collections 3.2.2 and BeanUtils 1.9.4 libraries have been upgraded to newer versions, with most migration steps automated by the OpenRewrite recipe. It's
recommended that you review all changes to ensure a successful upgrade.

Updating to Commons Configuration 2.x usage
Adjust your implementation after Apache Commons Configuration 1.x was replaced with Apache Commons Configuration 2.

Context
SAP Commerce Cloud is exposing its configuration capabilities through HybrisConfiguration abstraction class. The class allows retrieval of the configuration object from the Apache
Commons Configuration. With the update of the Apache Commons Configuration to version 2.x, all Apache configuration classes have changed their packages. For most common configuration
usage use cases (reading and modifying the configuration) the OpenRewrite framework update procedure should help you with the required migration. To learn more, see Apache Commons
Configuration

.

The Apache Commons configuration eventing mechanism was changed with version 2. In case you were using this functionality, refer to the official Apache migration guide

and adjust your

implementation accordingly.

Task overview: Apache Libraries
Next task: Updating to Commons Lang 3.x

Updating to Commons Lang 3.x
Adapt to Apache Commons Lang 3. Apache Commons Lang 2 library is now in the end of life state and it was replaced by Apache Commons Lang 3.

Context
Apache Commons Lang 3 was already used in the project, but now version 2 has been completely removed. Most of the changes are automated by the Open Rewrite framework update recipes, but
some methods don't have a direct replacement, or the new methods differ from the old ones. You need to handle each case manually. For example:
StringEscapeUtils.escapeXml() -> StringEscapeUtils.escapeXml10() or StringEscapeUtils.escapeXml11()

Task overview: Apache Libraries
Previous task: Updating to Commons Configuration 2.x usage
Next task: Adapting to Apache HttpComponents 5

Related Information
What's new in Commons Lang 3.0?

Adapting to Apache HttpComponents 5
If your extensions are generated from ycommercewebservicestest template, perform the following steps to adapt to Apache HttpComponents 5.

Context
Apache HttpComponents has been upgraded from version 4 to 5, and there are Java API changes that you need to adapt.

Procedure
1. Introduce new httpClient bean.
The httpClient bean of type org.apache.http.impl.client.CloseableHttpClient is replaced with
org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.classic.CloseableHttpClient. And the configuration of defaultHttpClientBuilder is replaced with a new Factory Bean class
de.hybris.platform.commercewebservicescommons.strategies.impl.DefaultHttpClientBuilderFactory.
a. Create new builder factory class.
package de.hybris.platform.commercewebservicescommons.strategies.impl;

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
import java.util.concurrent.TimeUnit;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.config.ConnectionConfig;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.config.RequestConfig;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.DefaultHttpRequestRetryStrategy;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.classic.HttpClientBuilder;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.io.PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.io.PoolingHttpClientConnectionManagerBuilder;
import org.apache.hc.core5.util.TimeValue;
public class DefaultHttpClientBuilderFactory
{
public static HttpClientBuilder createBuilder()
{
HttpClientBuilder builder = HttpClientBuilder.create();
PoolingHttpClientConnectionManager connectionManager = PoolingHttpClientConnectionManagerBuilder.create()
.setDefaultConnectionConfig(ConnectionConfig.custom().setConnectTimeout(5000L, TimeUnit.MILLISECONDS).build())
.build();
return builder.setDefaultRequestConfig(RequestConfig.custom().build())
.setConnectionManager(connectionManager)
.setRetryStrategy(new DefaultHttpRequestRetryStrategy(3, TimeValue.ofSeconds(1L)));
}
}
b. Update the following bean configuration in commercewebservicescommons-spring.xml:
Previous Configuration:

<constructor-arg name="requestSentRetryEnabled" value="false"/>
</bean>
<bean id="requestConfigBuilder" class="org.apache.http.client.config.RequestConfig.Builder">
<property name="connectTimeout" value="5000"/>
</bean>

factory-bean="requestConfigBuilder" factory-method="build"/>

The BasicHttpEntity’s setContentType and setContent methods are removed in Apache HttpComponents 5 API. Migrate to use the

httpEntity = new BasicHttpEntity();
httpEntity.setContentType("application/json");
httpEntity.setContent(inputStreamRoute);

httpEntity = new BasicHttpEntity(inputStreamRoute, APPLICATION_JSON);

package de.hybris.platform.ycommercewebservicestest.test.groovy.webservicetests;
import java.security.KeyManagementException;

public class SSLIssuesIgnoringHttpClientFactory
{
public static HttpClient createHttpClient()
{
try
{
final TrustManager[] trustAllCerts = { new DummyTrustManager() };
final SSLContext sslContext = SSLContext.getDefault();
sslContext.init(null, trustAllCerts, new java.security.SecureRandom());
final HttpClientBuilder httpClientBuilder = HttpClientBuilder.create();
httpClientBuilder.setSSLHostnameVerifier(new DummyHostnameVerifier());
httpClientBuilder.setSSLSocketFactory(new SSLConnectionSocketFactory(sslContext, new DummyHostnameVerifier()));
return httpClientBuilder.build();
}
catch (KeyManagementException | NoSuchAlgorithmException e)
{
throw new RuntimeException(e);
}
}
}

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
public static HttpClient createHttpClient()
{
try
{
return HttpClients.custom()
.setConnectionManager(PoolingHttpClientConnectionManagerBuilder.create()
.setSSLSocketFactory(SSLConnectionSocketFactoryBuilder.create()
.setSslContext(SSLContextBuilder.create()
.loadTrustMaterial(TrustAllStrategy.INSTANCE)
.build())
.setHostnameVerifier(NoopHostnameVerifier.INSTANCE)
.build())
.build())
.build();
}
catch (KeyManagementException | NoSuchAlgorithmException | KeyStoreException e)
{
throw new RuntimeException(e);
}
}
}
8. Migrate UrlEncodedFormEntity.
In Apache HttpComponents 5, the UrlEncodedFormEntity class no longer includes the constructor UrlEncodedFormEntity (Iterable<? extends NameValuePair>

parameters, Charset charset).
a. Update the following code:
Previous Configuration:
UrlEncodedFormEntity e = new UrlEncodedFormEntity(paramList, Charset.defaultCharset().toString());
if (contentType != null) {
e.setContentType(contentType.toString())
}
return e
Updated Configuration:
return new UrlEncodedFormEntity(paramList);
b. Set the content type in the ClassicRequestBuilder#setHeader method.
requestBuilder.setHeader(HttpHeaders.CONTENT_TYPE, requestContentType);
9. Migrate parsing of ClassicHttpResponse.
a. Since Apache HttpComponent 5 introduces its own HTTP request builder class, the HttpRequestBuilder.groovy file is removed. The logic for building HTTP requests is now
incorporated into the SimpleHttpClient.groovy class using org.apache.hc.core5.http.ClassicHttpRequest.
b. As ClassicHttpResponse in Apache HttpComponent 5 can't be parsed anymore, HttpResponseParser.groovy is removed. A new interface,
HttpEntityParser.groovy, is added instead.
package de.hybris.platform.ycommercewebservicestest.test.groovy.webservicetests.http

/**

interface HttpEntityParser {

}
c. The implementation class TypeAwareResponseParser.groovy is removed, and a new class, TypeAwareHttpEntityParser.groovy, is added.

package de.hybris.platform.ycommercewebservicestest.test.groovy.webservicetests.http
import groovy.json.JsonSlurper
import groovy.xml.XmlSlurper
import groovy.xml.slurpersupport.GPathResult
import org.apache.commons.logging.Log
import org.apache.commons.logging.LogFactory
import org.apache.hc.core5.http.HttpEntity
import org.codehaus.groovy.runtime.MethodClosure
import org.xml.sax.SAXException
import javax.xml.parsers.ParserConfigurationException
/**
* Type aware http entity parser implementation.
* Customize by composition and delegates to this class, instead of subclass.
*/
class TypeAwareHttpEntityParser implements HttpEntityParser {
protected static final Log log = LogFactory.getLog(TypeAwareHttpEntityParser.class)
public static final String DEFAULT_CHARSET = "UTF-8";
private String defaultCharset = DEFAULT_CHARSET;
private Map<String, Closure> registeredParsers
TypeAwareHttpEntityParser() {
registeredParsers = buildDefaultParserMap()

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

143

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
}
@Override
Object parse(final HttpEntity resp) {
def data = null
if (resp != null && resp.getContentLength() != 0) {
data = this.parseData(resp)
}
data
}
Object parseData(final HttpEntity resp) {
String contentType = getContentType(resp)
Closure parser = this.getByType(contentType);
if (parser == null) {
log.warn("No parser found for " + contentType)
return null
} else {
return parser.call(resp)
}
}
void setDefaultCharset(String charset) {
defaultCharset = charset == null ? DEFAULT_CHARSET : charset;
}
String getCharset(HttpEntity resp) {
return resp.getContentEncoding() ?: this.defaultCharset
}
String getContentType(HttpEntity resp) {
return resp.getContentType() ?: org.apache.hc.core5.http.ContentType.DEFAULT_TEXT.getMimeType()
}
String parseTextToString(HttpEntity resp) throws IOException {
def buffer = new StringWriter()
def reader = parseTextToReader(resp)
buffer << reader
return buffer.toString()
}
StringReader parseTextToReader(HttpEntity resp) {
def reader = new InputStreamReader(resp.getContent(),
this.getCharset(resp))
def buffer = new StringWriter()
buffer << reader
return new StringReader(buffer.toString())
}
InputStream parseStream(HttpEntity resp) throws IOException {
def data = resp.getContent()
def buffer = new ByteArrayOutputStream()
buffer << (InputStream) data
return new ByteArrayInputStream(buffer.toByteArray())
}
GPathResult parseXML(HttpEntity resp) throws IOException, SAXException, ParserConfigurationException {
def parsedXml = new XmlSlurper().parseText(parseTextToString(resp))
return parsedXml
}
Object parseJSON(HttpEntity resp) throws IOException {
return new JsonSlurper().parseText(parseTextToString(resp));
}
protected Map<String, Closure> buildDefaultParserMap() {
Map<String, Closure> parsers = new HashMap<String, Closure>();
parsers.put(ContentType.TEXT, new MethodClosure(this, "parseTextToReader"));
parsers.put(ContentType.HTML, new MethodClosure(this, "parseTextToReader"));
parsers.put(ContentType.XML, new MethodClosure(this, "parseXML"));
parsers.put(ContentType.JSON, new MethodClosure(this, "parseJSON"));
parsers.put(ContentType.BINARY, new MethodClosure(this, "parseStream"));
return parsers;
}
Closure getByType(String contentType) {
String ct = contentType
int idx = ct.indexOf(';');
if (idx > 0) ct = ct.substring(0, idx);
Closure parser = registeredParsers.get(ct);
if (parser != null) return parser;
log.warn("Cannot find parser for content-type: " + ct)
return null;
}
void putAt(Object contentType, Closure value) {
this.registeredParsers.put(contentType.toString(), value);
}
void propertyMissing(String key, Closure value) {
this.registeredParsers.put(key, value);
}
Iterator<Map.Entry<String, Closure>> iterator() {
return this.registeredParsers.entrySet().iterator();
}
}

Object doRequest(Map<String, ?> args, Method method) {

//handle response: 1) get entity 2) parse entity to object 3) call postProcessor if any
def res = this.client.execute(request, (response) -> {
def data = null
if (this.parser != null) {
data = this.parser.parse(response.getEntity())
}

resp

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

146

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
res = this.postProcessor.call(res)
}
return res
}
private ClassicHttpRequest buildRequest(Map<String, ?> args, Method method) {
ClassicRequestBuilder requestBuilder = ClassicRequestBuilder.create(method as String)
this.headers.each {
requestBuilder.addHeader(it.key, it.value)
}
requestBuilder.setUri(this.defaultURI)
if (args == null) {
return requestBuilder.build()
}
adjustURI(args, requestBuilder)
Map extraHeaders = (Map) args.remove("headers");
if (extraHeaders != null) {
extraHeaders.each {
requestBuilder.addHeader(it.key as String, it.value as String)
}
}
String acceptContentType = args.remove("contentType");
if (acceptContentType != null) {
requestBuilder.setHeader(HttpHeaders.ACCEPT, acceptContentType);
}
String requestContentType = args.remove("requestContentType")
if (requestContentType == null) {
requestContentType = acceptContentType
}
Object body = args.remove("body")
def encodedBody = this.encoder.encodeBody(body, requestContentType)
if (encodedBody != null) {
requestBuilder.setEntity(encodedBody)
}
// for multipart/form-data, if we don't set httpclient will auto add content-type,
// and the value will contain boundary which is important for multipart request,
// however, if set content-type manually, the value won't contain boundary
if (requestContentType != null && MediaType.MULTIPART_FORM_DATA != requestContentType) {
requestBuilder.setHeader(HttpHeaders.CONTENT_TYPE, requestContentType);
}
if (args.size() > 0) {
String invalidArgs = "";
for (String k : args.keySet()) invalidArgs += k + ",";
throw new IllegalArgumentException("Unexpected keyword args: " + invalidArgs);
}
return requestBuilder.build()
}
private void adjustURI(Map<String, ?> args, ClassicRequestBuilder requestBuilder) {
String baseURI = this.defaultURI
Object uri = args.remove("uri")
if (uri != null) {
baseURI = uri
}
def uriBuilder = new URIBuilder(baseURI)
Map query = (Map) args.remove("params");
if (query != null) {
log.warn("'params' argument is deprecated; use 'query' instead.");
query.each {
uriBuilder.addParameter(it.key as String, it.value as String)
}
}
query = (Map) args.remove("query");
if (query != null) {
query.each {
uriBuilder.addParameter(it.key as String, it.value as String)
}
}
Object path = args.remove("path");
if (path != null) {
uriBuilder.setPath(path.toString())
}
requestBuilder.setUri(uriBuilder.build())
}
}

Preparing for the Removal of Apache Commons Pool 1.6
Prepare for the removal of Apache Commons Pool 1.6 to ensure that this change remains compatible with your custom implementations.

Context
Carry out the following steps to prepare for the full removal of Apache Commons Pool 1.6 that is still shipped with the product alongside the 2.x version.

Procedure
1. Replace removed methods.
a. In the de.hybris.platform.jdbcwrapper.DataSourceImpl class, replace the removed createPoolConfig() method with createNewPoolConfig().
Previous Configuration:

b. In the de.hybris.platform.jdbcwrapper.JDBCConnectionPool class, replace the removed JDBCConnectionPool constructor and the
convertOldPoolConfigToV2() private method with a new constructor.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

148

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
Updated Configuration:
public JDBCConnectionPool(final JDBCConnectionFactory factory, final GenericObjectPoolConfig cfg)
2. Analyze changes in the de.hybris.platform.util.threadpool.PoolableThreadFactory class.

de.hybris.platform.util.threadpool.PoolableThreadFactory has been updated to use Apache Commons Pool 2.x, which introduces structural changes. The class
now extends org.apache.commons.pool2.BasePooledObjectFactory instead of its previous parent class. The

de.hybris.platform.util.threadpool.PoolableThreadFactor class no longer overrides the makeObject() method. Instead, it now implements two separate
methods:

create() - Instantiates new PoolableThread objects
wrap(final PoolableThread poolableThread) - Handles packaging the created thread into a pooled object container
The makeObject() method is now inherited from the parent org.apache.commons.pool2.BasePooledObjectFactory class and serves as a template method that
orchestrates the object creation process. The makeObject() method is no longer abstract. It internally invokes the create() method to instantiate a new object. Subsequently,
the method calls the wrap() method to prepare the newly created object for pool management.

Apache Commons Collections and Apache Commons BeanUtils Upgrades
The Apache Commons Collections 3.2.2 and BeanUtils 1.9.4 libraries have been upgraded to newer versions, with most migration steps automated by the OpenRewrite recipe. It's recommended
that you review all changes to ensure a successful upgrade.

Prerequisites
Aside from import updates, the upgrades to Apache Commons Collections 4.x and Apache Commons BeanUtils 2.x require a number of changes for Collections:
The Collections 3.2.2 library provided Predicate and Closure classes, which have been deprecated, but many methods still refer to these classes.
Some types have been removed from the Collections library.
Some methods in the Collections library have been deprecated.
To ensure that the upgrades, mostly automated by the OpenRewrite recipe, don't disrupt your custom code, analyze the changes introduced by the recipe.

Caching Libraries
Review all manual steps related to caching libraries and adapt your SAP Commerce Cloud implementation accordingly.
1. Upgrading to Ehcache 3.x
As part of the upgrade to JDK21.0, we have upgraded SAP Commerce Cloud from Ehcache 2.x to Ehcache 3.x.
2. Replacing EhCacheRegion with DefaultCacheRegion
Ehcache2 is out of maintenance and the de.hybris.platform.regioncache.EhCacheRegion class which was based on Ehcache2 has been removed.

Upgrading to Ehcache 3.x
This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

151

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
As part of the upgrade to JDK21.0, we have upgraded SAP Commerce Cloud from Ehcache 2.x to Ehcache 3.x.
For Ehcache 3.x, you should be aware of the following points:
The Ehcache 3.x configuration is not backwards compatible with the Ehcache 2.x configuration.
Ehcache 3.x doesn't support the org.springframework.cache.ehcache package. Spring 6 dropped support for the org.springframework.cache.ehcache package as it only
provided support for Ehcache 2.x. For Ehcache 3.x, JCache-support provided by Spring (JSR-107) is used, that is, you must use the org.ehcache:ehcache dependency with the Jakarta
classifier. Spring recommends using Ehcache through the JCache API.
The JCacheManagerFactoryBean doesn't support the naming of cache managers, therefore TenantAwareEhCacheManagerFactoryBean was removed because it's no longer
needed.
For multi-tenant support, the separation of cache managers for tenants is now achieved by configuring different cache-configuration XML files. The cache managers are scoped and
uniquely identified by a URI. This means that a unique ehcache.xml file is required for each tenant, for example, junit_ehcache.xml, and a reference to the file must be added to the
tenant's .properties file, for example, tenant_<tenant_identifier>.properties.
The cache configurations for Ehcache 2.x and Ehcache 3.x are different from one another. The following code samples provide a side-by-side comparison of XML-based cache configuration in
Ehcache 2.x and Ehcache 3.x.
Ehcache 2.x ehcache.xml
<ehcache xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
xsi:noNamespaceSchemaLocation="../config/ehcache.xsd" updateCheck="false" monitoring="autodetect"
dynamicConfig="true">
<diskStore path="java.io.tmpdir/ywebservices_cache"/>
<defaultCache
maxElementsInMemory="100000"
eternal="false"
timeToIdleSeconds="360"
timeToLiveSeconds="360"
overflowToDisk="true"
diskPersistent="false"
maxElementsOnDisk="10"
diskExpiryThreadIntervalSeconds="360"
memoryStoreEvictionPolicy="FIFO"
/>
<!-- sample cache configuration -->
<cache name="sampleCache"
maxElementsInMemory="1000"
eternal="false"
overflowToDisk="true"
timeToLiveSeconds="150"
diskPersistent="false"
maxElementsOnDisk="2000"
memoryStoreEvictionPolicy="LRU"/>
</ehcache>
Ehcache 3.x ehcache.xml
<config xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
xmlns="http://www.ehcache.org/v3"
xsi:schemaLocation="http://www.ehcache.org/v3 http://www.ehcache.org/schema/ehcache-core-3.0.xsd">
<cache-template name="default">
<key-type>java.lang.Object</key-type>
<value-type>java.lang.Object</value-type>
</cache-template>
<cache alias="defaultCache" uses-template="default">
<expiry>
<ttl unit="seconds">360</ttl>
</expiry>
<resources>
<heap unit="entries">100000</heap>
</resources>
</cache>
<cache alias="sampleCache" uses-template="default">
<expiry>
<ttl unit="seconds">150</ttl>
</expiry>
<resources>
<heap unit="entries">1000</heap>
</resources>
</cache>
</config>

Parent topic: Caching Libraries
Next task: Replacing EhCacheRegion with DefaultCacheRegion

Upgrading from Ehcache 2.x to Ehcache 3.x
If you have a customized webservices extension, you must upgrade it from Ehcache 2.x to Ehcache 3.x.

Context
Before upgrading your webservices extension, you should be aware of the following elements provided in Ehcache 3.x:

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

152

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
<cache>: The <cache> element represents a cache instance. Each <cache> element requires an alias attribute. It is used at runtime to retrieve the corresponding Cache<K, V>
instance. The <cache> element can have an optional uses-template attribute, which makes it possible for you to reference a <cache-template> element’s name attribute.

<cache-template>: The <cache-template> element represents a uniquely-named template that <cache> elements inherit from. A <cache> element that uses the usestemplate attribute to reference a <cache-template> by its name inherits all properties of the <cache-template> element. You can use a <cache> element to override these
properties as required.
The following nested elements are supported for a cache configuration:

<key-type>: Fully-qualified class name (FQCN) of the keys held in the cache.
<value-type>: FQCN of the values held in the cache.
<expiry>: Expiry type and its parameters.
<ttl>: Time to live in the units provided. It replaces the timeToLiveSeconds element provided in Ehcache 2.x.
<tti>: Time to idle in the units provided. It is mutually exclusive with ttl . It replaces the timeToIdleSeconds element provided in Ehcache 2.x.
<resources>: Configures the tiers and their capacity.
<heap>: Maximum number of elements to be held in the cache before the eviction starts. It replaces the maxElementsInMemory element provided in Ehcache 2.x.
<disk>: Mandatory element when storing cache data on disk. It replaces the maxElementsOnDisk element provided in Ehcache 2.x.
If you use disk storage, you should use the <disk> element in combination with the <persistence> element to provide a location where data should be stored. It requires
the directory location where data needs to be stored on disk.
The <disk> element has a boolean attribute called <persistence>. When the <persistence> attribute is set to true, the cache will survive a JVM restart. The <disk>
element replaces the diskPersistence provided in Ehcache 2.x.
The webservicescommons extension has been updated from Ehcache 2.x to Ehcache 3.x. To upgrade Ehcache for your webservices extension, follow the instructions in this procedure.

Procedure
Edit the cache-config-spring.xml file of your webservices extension so that your extension can leverage caching using JCache.

 Tip
In Ehcache 3.x, all cache configuration XML files are stored at resources/<extension-name>/cache.

The following code excerpt shows the updated beans configuration in the cache-config-spring.xml file of the ywebservices template extension. Make the same changes in the cache-

config-spring.xml file of your webservices extension.
<!-- instantiates a JCacheManagerFactoryBean instance using the cache configuration provided at the mentioned location -->
<alias name="defaultWSEhcache" alias="wsEhcache"/>
<bean id="defaultWSEhcache" class="org.springframework.cache.jcache.JCacheManagerFactoryBean">
<property name="cacheManagerUri" value="classpath:${ywebservices.ehcache.location:ywebservices/cache/ehcache.xml}" />
</bean>
<!-- instantiates a JCacheCacheManager instance using above created factory bean -->
<alias name="defaultWSCacheManager" alias="wsCacheManager"/>
<bean id="defaultWSCacheManager" class="org.springframework.cache.jcache.JCacheCacheManager">
<property name="cacheManager" ref="wsEhcache"/>
</bean>

Replacing EhCacheRegion with DefaultCacheRegion
Ehcache2 is out of maintenance and the de.hybris.platform.regioncache.EhCacheRegion class which was based on Ehcache2 has been removed.

Context
As Ehcache3 the natural successor is a new library which isn't backward compatible, we decided to investigate other available options and selected Caffeine as a replacement. From this point on,
the de.hybris.platform.regioncache.DefaultCacheRegion class which has been re-implemented to base on Caffeine is used as a default implementation for cache regions.
The main difference compared to de.hybris.platform.regioncache.EhCacheRegion class is the lack of the evictionPolicy constructor parameter because Caffeine uses the

Window TinyLfu eviction policy only. Because of this change, all properties used for configuring eviction policy have been removed (regioncache.<region_name>.evictionpolicy).

Procedure
1. Switch to the de.hybris.platform.regioncache.DefaultCacheRegion class, if you have de.hybris.platform.regioncache.EhCacheRegion bean defined in your code
or in the XML configuration.
2. Adjust the bean configuration to the new constructor if needed.
public DefaultCacheRegion(final String name, final int maxEntries)
public DefaultCacheRegion(final String name, final int maxEntries, final boolean exclusiveComputation)
public DefaultCacheRegion(final String name, final int maxEntries, final boolean exclusiveComputation, final boolean statsEnabled)
public DefaultCacheRegion(final String name, final int maxEntries, final boolean exclusiveComputation, final boolean statsEnabled, final Long t
public DefaultCacheRegion(final String name, final int maxEntries, final boolean exclusiveComputation, final boolean statsEnabled, final Long t
If you use the EhCacheRegion class directly in your code, keep in mind that:

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

153

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
The following methods of EhCacheRegion aren't present in the DefaultCacheRegion class:

protected CacheStatistics createCacheStatistics() - CacheStatistics instance can be provided through the constructor.
protected CacheConfiguration createCacheConfiguration() - if you override this method you can override the DefaultCacheRegion.init() method to
adjust cache configuration.

protected CacheEventListener createCacheEventListener() - if you override this method you can override the DefaultCacheRegion.init() method to
adjust event listeners configuration.
The following method of EhCacheRegion has a different signature:

protected void compareAndSetMaxReachedSize(final long currentMaxReachedSize) - in DefaultCacheRegion it has an additional parameter:
protected void compareAndSetMaxReachedSize(final long currentCacheMapSize, final long currentMaxReachedSize)
The following methods were removed.

public CacheMap getCacheMap();
public void setCacheMap(CacheMap cacheMap);

Upgrading Validation Engine to Jakarta EE 10
One component of the SAP Commerce Cloud framework update is upgrading Jakarta EE. The main change behind this is the namespaces update from 'javax' to 'jakarta'. This change has a visible
impact on some SAP Commerce Cloud functionalities, including the Validation Engine built on top of the Bean Validation Specification.

Context
Jakarta upgrade in the context of Validation Engine
With the adoption of the Jakarta EE 10, the main change affecting the validation mechanism of the SAP Commerce Cloud platform is a change of package names from javax.validation to
jakarta.validation.

Updating the SAP Commerce Cloud Code
Context
The updated version of SAP Commerce Cloud already contains a codebase compatible with the new Jakarta namespace. The following things have been updated:
Code references to old package naming convention
ImpEx files shipped with the product
Default values of AbstractConstraint subtypes specifying annotation class
Database update procedure triggered once during the system update - subtypes of AbstractConstraint type with references to the Annotation Class using javax.validation
package
The system setup procedure has been added to the update process. It relies on the Patching Framework and StartsWithStringAttributeValueMapper class.
During the system update, the Annotation attribute of the AbstractConstraint type is changed if required. It automatically updates values of the Annotation attribute from

javax.validation.* to jakarta.validation.*.
The mapping of annotation values in the database occurs only during the system update. During the system's initialization, new records with valid packages are created, so no update is needed. To
prevent an inconsistent cache state in the running pods, the update procedure needs to be run with downtime.

Updating the Customer-owned Code
This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

154

3/9/26, 4:28 PM

Context
With the adaptation to this change, the following actions may be required:

Procedure
1. Modify javax.validation references in your custom code.
Any import or usage of classes from package javax.validation should be changed to jakarta.validation.

 Note
This step is covered by the OpenRewrite framework update recipe.
2. Adapt *-beans.xml files in your custom code.
References within the POJO class definitions or imports of the classes from the javax.validation package must be replaced with the Jakarta namespace equivalents.

 Note
This step is covered by the OpenRewrite framework update recipe.
3. Update javax.validation references in customer-owned ImpEx files.
You should verify if any of your ImpEx files have the reference to the classes within the package and replace them with equivalents from the Jakarta package.
One of the examples where we can find such references is ImpEx files creating subtypes of AbstractConstraint type with explicit references to the Annotation Class.
4. Verify that your custom extensions no longer reference the legacy javax.validation.constraints.* classes that are no longer supported in SAP Commerce Cloud, unless there is a
specific reason to retain them. In particular, review your external-dependencies and consider removing javax.validation:validation-api, if it is no longer required.
5. Adapt of item type attributes of type java.lang.Class stored in the database.
For the item type attributes of type java.lang.Class a canonical name of the class reference is stored in the database. In some cases, values stored in such attributes may require
manual update. For more information, see Validation Update Helpers.

Runtime Fallback Mapping
Context
With the framework update, we ship a functionality of runtime-based mapping of unresolved canonical names of classes for attributes with java.lang.Class type. This can help you smooth out
the update process and define fallback rules for classes no longer available within the classpath.
This feature is enabled by default and defines the runtime fallback rule for the javax.validation package, which tries to find and return an equivalent class instance within the

jakarta.validation package, if applicable.
Default fallback rule is the following:
jdbc.mapping.runtimeClassTypeFallbackMapping.1.regex=(javax)(\\.)(validation)(\\..*)
jdbc.mapping.runtimeClassTypeFallbackMapping.1.replace.regex.group.1=jakarta
For more information, see Fallback Mapping Details.

Fallback Mapping Details
Fallback mapping details for item types attributes with a java.lang.Class type.

Overview
This feature applies to the item type attributes defined with the type java.lang.Class.
Values of that type are stored in the Database as literals. When package names or library versions are changed, the class's literal value may become invalid and no longer available on the classpath.
The runtime Class type fallback mapping helps you address that and configure a fallback for specified classes that can be leveraged in such a situation.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

156

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
Feature Details
Works lazily, fallback will be applied only when a matching Class cannot be found for the literal.
Changes in the configuration will be applied only after system restart.
Invalid mapping configurations are ignored.
Fallback is applied only in the runtime. The underlying value in the database won't be changed.
Fallback mappings are applied in ascending order based on the mapping number specified in the configuration. If more than one mapping matches the invalid literal, only the first one will be
applied (according to the order).
For each detected invalid literal that cannot be mapped to the Class value, information about it and usage of the fallback mapping (successful or not) will be logged.
Fallback Class Mapping should instead be used as a safe net to secure business functionality. It's usually preferred to update/migrate the class names to the new values on the database as
it's a solution with better performance. To learn more, see the related information section.

Configuration
Here are details of the general settings:

Setting
jdbc.mapping.runtimeClassTypeFallbackMapping.enabled

jdbc.mapping.runtimeClassTypeFallbackMapping.replace.regex.group.limit

Applicable Values

Default Value

Description

true/false

true

Allows for enabling or disabling the
fallback mapping feature.

positive integer

3

Limited the maximum number of
pattern-capturing group
replacements per single fallback
mapping configuration. Fallback
mappings with configured group
replacements that exceed the limit
are ignored.

Single Mapping Configuration
Besides the general settings, each mapping configuration consists of at least two properties.
A single definition of the regex pattern (one per mapping)
This pattern will be used while matching invalid literals with defined fallback mappings. It allows us to determine whether the following mapping configuration applies to the analyzed literal. Pattern
property should match the following scheme:
jdbc.mapping.runtimeClassTypeFallbackMapping.<fallback_mapping_number>.regex=<regex_value>
In this scheme, <fallback_mapping_number> is common and unique within all project properties. The number of mapping configurations shared with the rest of the properties that create a single
mapping definition.

<regex_value> is a String-based value that can be parsed as java.regex.Pattern. Special characters need to be escaped for this value.
Here's what needs to be considered for the regex:
Defined regex should match the whole expression/literal.
It should also define pattern-capturing groups that can be replaced later while applying fallback mapping.
Invalid regex pattern value will cause the mapping configuration to be ignored.
The complexity of regex should be considered, as very complex regex patterns can contribute to reducing system performance.
One or more definitions of pattern-capturing group replacements
Replacement definitions should follow this pattern:
jdbc.mapping.runtimeClassTypeFallbackMapping.<fallback_mapping_number>.replace.regex.group.<regex_group_number>=<replacement_value>
As it was in the previous case, <fallback_mapping_number> is common and unique within all project properties. The number of mapping configurations shared with the rest of the properties that
create a single mapping definition. This number must match the pattern definition schema.

<regex_group_number> is the number corresponding to the number of the capturing group that should be replaced within the literal. Groups are numbered from left to right, starting from 1. For
more details, see the related information section.

<replacement_value> is the value that should be placed instead of the literal part matched by the specified capturing group.

 Note
The number of capturing group replacements is limited. Please take a look at the general settings in the Configuration section.
The group with the number 0 has a special meaning. Defining the configuration for that group will replace the whole literal with the value specified in that group configuration. This replacement
has precedence. If there are other group replacements for this fallback, they are ignored.

Persisting value resolved from the fallback value in the database

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

157

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
By design, the fallback functionality operates only in runtime and doesn't persist the resolved value in the database. An update of the value must be done independently from the fallback
functionality. The fallback functionality is transparent to the persistence layer. This means the SAP Commerce Cloud persistence layer doesn't distinguish between values originating from fallback
and those originating directly from the underlying database. If you want to use the model layer to persist the fallback value in the database, take it into consideration.
To better understand the trade-offs, have a look at these examples:
//Assume you fetched a model that in DB has annotation field value javax.validation.constraints.NotNull
//and fallback was applied to it, so the value in the model is jakarta.validation.constraints.NotNull
TypeConstraintModel nullConstraint = getConstraintById() //Assume valid value has been returned
//Example 1: DB value won't be changed - as the database layer will not identify this as a changed value (the same value was read after the fallback
modelService.save(nullConstraint);
//Example 2: DB value won't be changed - as the database layer will not identify this as a changed value (the same value was read after the fallback
nullConstraint.setAnnotation(jakarta.validation.constraints.NotNull.class)
modelService.save(nullConstraint);
//Example 3: Will change the value if there are no validators/restrictions against null value for the fields (in case of TypeConstraint, it won't wo
final Class<?> correctedValue = nullConstraint.getAnnotation()
nullConstraint.setAnnotation(null)
modelService.save(nullConstraint) // first persist removing annotation value
nullConstraint.setAnnotation(correctedValue)
modelService.save(nullConstraint) // second bring back the corrected annotation value (the one that was mapped with Fallback Class Mapping mechanism
//Example 4:
var clone = modelService.clone(nullConstraint)
modelService.remove(nullConstraint)
modelService.save(clone)

Updating Dependencies in .classpath Files
Context
Synchronize .classpath files with library versions defined in external-dependencies.xml files. In SAP Commerce Cloud .classpath files are in every extension. Only Eclipse IDE uses

.classpath files. If you use Eclipse as your development environment and you updated some library version then you should update .classpath files for your extensions as well. Updating the
.classpath files is recommended as one of the final steps, after upgrading and testing updates in external-dependencies.xml files. Instead of manually adjusting .classpath files for
your extensions, use this procedure:

Procedure
Run ant classpathgen command from the extension directory you would like to regenerate .classpath entries for.
It adjusts .classpath files according to external-dependencies.xml files.

Updating JDK Version Settings in Eclipse
Context
With the update to Java in version 21, you can also adjust the language level for the compiler settings in your Eclipse project settings, see the .settings/org.eclipse.jdt.core.prefs file
in the extension directory. Instead of manual adjustments you can use this procedure:

Procedure
Run the ant updateJdkEclipse setting from the hybris/bin/platform directory level and specify the path to the extension for which you want to update the configuration.
ant updateJdkEclipseSettings -Ddestdir=path/to/extension

Results
This command updates the following compiler-related properties for your Eclipse project based on the target Java version used to compile SAP Commerce Cloud:
org.eclipse.jdt.core.compiler.compliance
org.eclipse.jdt.core.compiler.source
org.eclipse.jdt.core.compiler.codegen.targetPlatform
This ensures that the settings are correctly applied for the specified extension.

Removing Deprecated Thread Class Method Usage
Refactor your code to prevent usage of deprecated and unsafe methods from the Thread class.

Context
The following methods are not supported since Java 20:

Thread.stop()
Thread.suspend()
Thread.resume()
When these methods are used, UnsupportedOperationException is thrown.

Procedure
1. Review your code to identify if you use any of the methods mentioned above.
2. Remove usage of these deprecated and unsafe methods. Code should be refactored, for example by using the Thread.interrupt() method.
The existing recipe identifies usage of methods, adds comments to the code, and adds throwing of any additional UnsupportedOperationException.

Task overview: Other Topics

Upgrade of Groovy to 4.0.x
With the update to Java 21 version, Groovy was also updated from 3.0.13 to 4.0.26.
Groovy and dependent libraries should be updated along with other dependencies, but developers should verify if they use any groovy syntax that has been deprecated. Some syntax or features
supported in Groovy 3.x might be removed or altered in Groovy 5.x. Groovy 5.x is expected to improve static compilation and type-checking, which might make some dynamically typed codes
incompatible. Introduction of new reserved keywords could conflict with existing variable names or methods. It's recommended to get familiar with Groovy's official documentation, check their
release notes and verify if any groovy files require adjustment. For more details, see the related information section.

Removal of Legacy Groovy Servlet Integration due to Jakarta EE Incompatibility
The org.apache.groovy.groovy-servlet library has been removed due to its incompatibility with Jakarta EE 9 and later officially released versions.
As a result of this change, the de.hybris.platform.spring.SpringAwareGroovyServlet class, which extended groovy.servlet.GroovyServlet, has also been removed.

Changes for Extensions Generated from ycommercewebservicestest Template

groovy.xml are added to the relevant files.

import groovy.xml.XmlSlurper

import groovy.xml.XmlParser

Migrating from javax to jakarta
If your extensions are generated from the yacceleratorstorefront template, perform the following steps to upgrade from javax to jakarta.

Procedure
1. Update taglib URIs for all JSP, TLD, and tag files, change the taglib URIs from javax to jakarta:

Original code:
<%@ taglib prefix="c" uri="http://java.sun.com/jsp/jstl/core" %>
<%@ taglib prefix="fn" uri="http://java.sun.com/jsp/jstl/functions" %>
<%@ taglib prefix="fmt" uri="http://java.sun.com/jsp/jstl/fmt" %>
<taglib version="2.1"
xmlns="http://java.sun.com/xml/ns/javaee"
xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
xsi:schemaLocation="http://java.sun.com/xml/ns/javaee
http://java.sun.com/xml/ns/javaee/web-jsptaglibrary_2_1.xsd">

Updated code:
<%@ taglib prefix="c" uri="jakarta.tags.core" %>
<%@ taglib prefix="fn" uri="jakarta.tags.functions" %>
<%@ taglib prefix="fmt" uri="jakarta.tags.fmt" %>
<taglib xmlns="https://jakarta.ee/xml/ns/jakartaee"

Fixing SEVERE: Exception starting filter [WebResourceOptimizer]
java.lang.NoClassDefFoundError: javax/servlet/Filter Error
Fix the error when starting server – SEVERE: Exception starting filter [WebResourceOptimizer] java.lang.NoClassDefFoundError: javax/servlet/Filter.

Context
The upgrade from javax to jakarta namespace requires upgrade wro4j-core from 1.10.1 to 2.0+, because only wro4j-core 2.0+ provides full compatibility with Jakarta EE 9+​replacing its internal
javax.servlet dependencies with the new jakarta.servlet API packages.

Procedure
1. Update the code in yacceleratorstorefront/web/webroot/WEB-INF/external-dependencies.xml:
<!-- Original -->
<dependency>
<groupId>ro.isdc.wro4j</groupId>
<artifactId>wro4j-core</artifactId>
<version>1.10.1</version>
</dependency>
<!-- Updated -->
<dependency>
<groupId>ro.isdc.wro4j</groupId>
<artifactId>wro4j-core</artifactId>
<version>2.1.1</version>
</dependency>
2. Update the code in yacceleratorstorefront/web/webroot/WEB-INF/dependencies.gradle:
// Original
libraries << "ro.isdc.wro4j:wro4j-core:1.10.1"
// Updated
libraries << "ro.isdc.wro4j:wro4j-core:2.1.1"
3. Change .classpath from <classpathentry exported="false" kind="lib" path="web/webroot/WEB-INF/lib/wro4j-core-1.10.1.jar"/> to <classpathentry
exported="false" kind="lib" path="web/webroot/WEB-INF/lib/wro4j-core-2.1.1.jar"/>.
4. Execute ant clean all. If you find that the old version of the ro.isdc.wro4j:wro4j-core package is not automatically deleted or the new version is not downloaded, please refer to
Upgrading jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl from 1.2.6 to 3.0.1 in JDK 21.

Next task: Upgrading jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl from 1.2.6 to 3.0.1 in JDK 21

Follow the steps below to Upgrade jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl from 1.2.6 to 3.0.1 in JDK 21.

Context
If you encounter the following error when running ant clean all in JDK 21, it is because the yaceleratorstorefrontmodule failed to download the updated jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl-

3.0.1.jar after the dependency was upgraded from version 1.2.6.

During this JDK 21 upgrade, the following JAR packages in yacceleratorstorefront have been upgraded. If you have upgraded the version of yacceleratorstorefront packages during
the JDK 2 upgrade and executed ant clean all, but find that the old-version JAR packages are not automatically deleted or the new-version JAR packages are not automatically downloaded, you can
follow the steps in the procedure to fix this issue.

jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl: 1.2.6 -> 3.0.1

Updated code:
<extension abstractclassprefix="Generated" classprefix="YAcceleratorStorefront" name="yacceleratorstorefront" usemaven="true">
3. Re-run ant clean all.

Next: Update of Olingo Version

Update of Olingo Version
The Olingo version has been updated from 2.0.13 (public release) to 5.0.0-sap-02 (SAP-specific fork).
This upgrade introduces potentially breaking changes, particularly for any custom code built on the previous version. This is because the old version (2.0.13) is not compatible with JDK 21. Make
sure your environment is updated to the new 5.0.0-sap-02 version that is JDK 21 compatible before migrating.

Parent topic: Other Topics
Previous task: Upgrading jakarta.servlet.jsp.jstl from 1.2.6 to 3.0.1 in JDK 21
Next task: Adjust Your Configuration to Extend LocalizedHybrisConstraintViolation

Adjust Your Configuration to Extend LocalizedHybrisConstraintViolation
Refactor your classes to extend LocalizedHybrisConstraintViolation and update your constructors accordingly. Use it to ensure that your custom code is compatible with the new
configuration.

Context
Two unused fields have been removed from the de.hybris.platform.validation.services.impl.DefaultHybrisConstraintViolation class:

i18NService
bundleProvider
Additionally, the default constructor for de.hybris.platform.validation.services.impl.LocalizedHybrisConstraintViolation has been removed.
To adjust your custom code to the new configuration, carry out the necessary migration steps.

Procedure
1. Refactor your custom classes that currently extend DefaultHybrisConstraintViolation and use the i18NService and bundleProvider fields. These fields have been removed
from DefaultHybrisConstraintViolation but are still available in de.hybris.platform.validation.services.impl.LocalizedHybrisConstraintViolation.
Update your classes to extend LocalizedHybrisConstraintViolation instead.
2. The default constructor for de.hybris.platform.validation.services.impl.LocalizedHybrisConstraintViolation has been removed as it had previously been
marked as deprecated. Ensure that any classes extending LocalizedHybrisConstraintViolation are updated to use one of the other two available constructors.

Cleaning Up Orphaned Types
You can clean up the orphaned types after the upgrading.

Context
After upgrading, the types related to the deleted cockpit extensions, including cockpit and admincockpit, become orphaned types in the database. Warnings may appear during system startup, for
example:

[ComposedTypeEJBImpl] missing jalo class 'de.hybris.platform.cockpit.jalo.template.CockpitItemTemplate' for item type 'CockpitItemTemplate' - trying
[ComposedTypeEJBImpl] missing jalo class 'de.hybris.platform.cockpit.reports.jalo.JasperMedia' for item type
[ComposedTypeEJBImpl] missing jalo class 'de.hybris.platform.cockpit.jalo.CockpitUIScriptConfigMedia' for ite
......

Procedure
1. Go to

HAC

Maintenance

Cleanup

and make sure all the listed types are orphaned types.

2. Click the Clean all orphaned types button to remove them from the database.

Enabling JCache Providers in Orbeonweb
Enable the JCache providers to use the ehcache.3.x.jakarta version in orbeonweb.

Procedure
Add the following properties in hybris/config/orbeon/config/properties-common.xml:
<!-- Enabling JCache providers -->
<property as="xs:string" name="oxf.xforms.cache.provider" value="jcache"/>
<property as="xs:string" name="oxf.xforms.cache.jcache.classname" value=".*EhcacheCachingProvider"/>
<property as="xs:string" name="oxf.xforms.cache.jcache.resource" value="/ehcache3.xml"/>

public static void startResourceServerMock()
{

.getBean("resourceServerTestManager", ResourceServerTestManager.class);
resourceServerTestManager.start();
}
public static void stopResourceServerMock()
{
final ResourceServerTestManager resourceServerTestManager = Registry.getApplicationContext()
.getBean("resourceServerTestManager", ResourceServerTestManager.class);
resourceServerTestManager.stop();;
}

/*
* Copyright (c) 2025 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved.
*/
package de.hybris.cis.subscription.config;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.method.configuration.EnableMethodSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.builders.HttpSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.configuration.EnableWebSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.configurers.AbstractHttpConfigurer;
import org.springframework.security.web.SecurityFilterChain;
/**
* Configure Spring Security to force HTTPS
*/
@Configuration
@EnableWebSecurity
@EnableMethodSecurity(securedEnabled = true)
public class WebSecurityConfig
{
@Bean
public SecurityFilterChain filterChain(HttpSecurity http) throws Exception {
http.csrf(AbstractHttpConfigurer::disable);
http.requiresChannel(c -> c.anyRequest().requiresSecure());
return http.build();
}
}

web/src/main/java/de/hybris/cis/subscription/web/oauth2/OauthConfiguration.java with the following content:
/*
* Copyright (c) 2025 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved.
*/
package de.hybris.cis.subscription.web.oauth2;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.classic.HttpClient;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.config.TlsConfig;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.classic.HttpClients;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.impl.io.PoolingHttpClientConnectionManagerBuilder;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.io.HttpClientConnectionManager;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.ssl.NoopHostnameVerifier;
import org.apache.hc.client5.http.ssl.SSLConnectionSocketFactory;
import org.apache.hc.core5.http.ssl.TLS;
import org.springframework.boot.web.client.RestTemplateBuilder;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.http.client.HttpComponentsClientHttpRequestFactory;
import javax.net.ssl.SSLContext;
import java.security.NoSuchAlgorithmException;
@Configuration
public class OauthConfiguration
{
@Bean
public SSLConnectionSocketFactory sslConnectionSocketFactory()
{

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

167

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
final SSLConnectionSocketFactory sslsf;
try
{
sslsf = new SSLConnectionSocketFactory(SSLContext.getDefault(),
NoopHostnameVerifier.INSTANCE);
}
catch (NoSuchAlgorithmException e)
{
throw new IllegalArgumentException(e);
}
return sslsf;
}
@Bean
public HttpClient sbgWebHttpClient()
{
final HttpClientConnectionManager cm = PoolingHttpClientConnectionManagerBuilder.create()
.setSSLSocketFactory(sslConnectionSocketFactory())
.setDefaultTlsConfig(TlsConfig.custom()
.setSupportedProtocols(TLS.V_1_2, TLS.V_1_3)
.build())
.build();
return HttpClients.custom()
.setConnectionManager(cm)
.build();
}
@Bean
public HttpComponentsClientHttpRequestFactory requestFactory() {
final HttpComponentsClientHttpRequestFactory requestFactory = new HttpComponentsClientHttpRequestFactory();
requestFactory.setHttpClient(sbgWebHttpClient());
return requestFactory;
}
@Bean
public RestTemplateBuilder restTemplateBuilder()
{
final RestTemplateBuilder restTemplateBuilder = new RestTemplateBuilder();
return restTemplateBuilder.requestFactory(this::requestFactory);
}
}

{

.setDefaultTlsConfig(TlsConfig.custom()
.setSupportedProtocols(TLS.V_1_2, TLS.V_1_3)
.build())
.build();

.setConnectionManager(cm)
.build();
}

return requestFactory;

/*
* Copyright (c) 2025 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved.
*/
package com.hybris.cis.client.rest.subscription.oauth.service.impl;
import com.hybris.cis.client.rest.subscription.oauth.service.Oauth2Client;
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Qualifier;
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Value;
import org.springframework.boot.web.client.RestTemplateBuilder;
import org.springframework.http.HttpEntity;
import org.springframework.http.HttpHeaders;
import org.springframework.http.MediaType;
import org.springframework.http.ResponseEntity;
import org.springframework.http.converter.json.MappingJackson2HttpMessageConverter;
import org.springframework.security.oauth2.core.OAuth2AccessToken;
import org.springframework.security.oauth2.core.endpoint.DefaultMapOAuth2AccessTokenResponseConverter;

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

171

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
import org.springframework.security.oauth2.core.endpoint.OAuth2AccessTokenResponse;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Service;
import org.springframework.util.LinkedMultiValueMap;
import org.springframework.util.MultiValueMap;
import org.springframework.web.client.RestTemplate;
import org.springframework.web.util.UriComponentsBuilder;
import java.util.Map;
@Service("defaultOauth2Client")
public class Oauth2ClientImpl implements Oauth2Client
{
private static final String CLIENT_ID = "client_id";
private static final String CLIENT_SECRET = "client_secret";
private static final String GRANT_TYPE = "grant_type";
@Value("${security.oauth2.client.accessTokenUri}")
private String accessTokenUri;
@Value("${security.oauth2.client.clientId}")
private String clientId;
@Value("${security.oauth2.client.clientSecret}")
private String clientSecret;

@Autowired
@Qualifier("defaultRestTemplateBuilder")
private RestTemplateBuilder restTemplateBuilder;
@Override
public ResponseEntity<OAuth2AccessToken> getToken()
{
final UriComponentsBuilder builder = UriComponentsBuilder.fromHttpUrl(accessTokenUri);
final MultiValueMap<String, String> params = new LinkedMultiValueMap<>();
params.add(CLIENT_ID, clientId);
params.add(CLIENT_SECRET, clientSecret);
params.add(GRANT_TYPE, "client_credentials");
final HttpHeaders headers = new HttpHeaders();
headers.add(HttpHeaders.CONTENT_TYPE, MediaType.APPLICATION_FORM_URLENCODED_VALUE);
final HttpEntity<?> httpEntity = new HttpEntity<>(params, headers);
RestTemplate restTemplate = getRestTemplateBuilder().build();
restTemplate.getMessageConverters().add(new MappingJackson2HttpMessageConverter());
final ResponseEntity<Map> response = restTemplate
.postForEntity(builder.toUriString(), httpEntity, Map.class);
Map<String, Object> responseBody = response.getBody();
if (responseBody == null) {
return new ResponseEntity<>(response.getStatusCode());
}
DefaultMapOAuth2AccessTokenResponseConverter converter = new DefaultMapOAuth2AccessTokenResponseConverter();
OAuth2AccessTokenResponse tokenResponse = converter.convert(responseBody);
if (tokenResponse == null || tokenResponse.getAccessToken() == null) {
return new ResponseEntity<>(response.getStatusCode());
}
return new ResponseEntity<>(tokenResponse.getAccessToken(), response.getStatusCode());
}
public RestTemplateBuilder getRestTemplateBuilder()
{
return restTemplateBuilder;
}
public void setRestTemplateBuilder(final RestTemplateBuilder restTemplateBuilder)
{
this.restTemplateBuilder = restTemplateBuilder;
}
}

Upgrading Custom Data Hub Extensions
Migrate custom Data Hub extensions to support JDK 21 and Spring 6.

Prerequisites
To successfully perform the migration, please have the following:
Access to the source code of custom Data Hub extensions
A development environment configured for working with Maven projects

Procedure
1. Configure the OpenRewrite Maven plugin. For migration, SAP Commerce Cloud provides a special set of code transformation rules (recipes) packaged in a JAR file. Download this file and
connect it locally.
a. Locate and download the JAR file sap-commerce-framework-update-recipes-1.X.X.jar from the attachments section of 3618495

. Save this file in an accessible

location in your project, for example, in the library directory at the project root.
b. Configure the plugin in pom.xml. This configuration activates the plugin and specifies the recipe to use for migrating to JDK 21 and Spring 6. To configure it, open the root pom.xml
of your Data Hub project, and add the rewrite-maven-plugin to the <build> section. For example:

 Note
In the configuration below, replace 1.X.X with the actual version number of the file you downloaded, for example, 1.1.1, and only use the official OpenRewrite Maven plugin with
the artifactId rewrite-maven-plugin. Do not confuse it with the commercial plugin io.moderne:rewrite-maven-plugin, or use the incorrect name openrewrite-

maven-plugin, which does not exist in the Maven Central repository.
Additionally, please use the exact versions specified in the configuration below (rewrite-maven-plugin:6.0.3, rewrite-spring:5.24.1, rewrite-migrate-java:2.30.1). Newer versions of
the OpenRewrite plugin may cause build failures (NullPointerException) when processing Data Hub-specific XML configurations due to missing cache regions that exist in
Commerce but not in Data Hub.

<build>
<plugins>
...
<plugin>
<groupId>org.openrewrite.maven</groupId>
<artifactId>rewrite-maven-plugin</artifactId>
<version>6.0.3</version> <!-- Downgraded version for Datahub compatibility -->
<configuration>
<activeRecipes>
<!-- Main recipe for SAP Commerce migration -->
<recipe>com.sap.cx.rewrite.java.spring.CommerceCloudJdk21AndSpring6Update</recipe>
</activeRecipes>
</configuration>
<dependencies>
<!-- Dependency containing SAP recipes -->
<dependency>
<groupId>com.sap.commerce.platform</groupId>
<artifactId>platform-rewrite-recipes</artifactId>
<version>1.X.X</version> <!-- Replace with the actual downloaded version -->
<scope>system</scope>
<systemPath>${project.basedir}/lib/sap-commerce-framework-update-recipes-1.X.X.jar</systemPath> <!-- Ensure th
</dependency>
<!-- Additional standard OpenRewrite dependencies -->
<dependency>

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

</dependency>

</activeRecipes>

authentication by adding a server configuration to your ~/.m2/settings.xml file.
