4. Manually migrate namespaces from Javax to Jakarta. Automated OpenRewrite recipes for this task may perform incorrect import replacements, leading to compilation errors or hidden
runtime errors. To manually migrate namespaces, do the following:
a. Use the Search&Replace function in your IDE to control each modification of import statements.
b. Key packages for migration: javax.servlet.*, javax.persistence.*, javax.persistence.*.
5. Adapt code to API changes. After updating dependencies, you need to adapt the code of custom Data Hub extensions to changes in the APIs of the used frameworks. If you used
RequestHandlerRetryAdvice, you need to replace it with the standard class org.springframework.retry.interceptor.RetryOperationsInterceptor.
a. Adapt Java Code (transferr custom logic). If your old class, for example, MyCustomRetryAdvice, contains additional logic, create a new class to hold it. For example:
Before
// Old class that will no longer compile
public class MyCustomRetryAdvice extends RequestHandlerRetryAdvice {
// ... some custom logic
}
Create a new class that extends RetryTemplate and implements RetryListener. Transfer your logic to the methods of this listener, for example, onRetry, onError, and so
on.
After
// New class for custom logic
public class MyCustomRetryTemplate extends RetryTemplate implements RetryListener {
// ... your custom logic from ...RetryAdvice is now here,
// in the methods of the RetryListener interface, for example:

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

175

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
@Override
public <T, E extends Throwable> void onError(RetryContext context, RetryCallback<T, E> callback, Throwable throwable) {
// Logging or other logic on error
}
}
b. Update the spring XML configuration. Reconfigure your XML file to use the new custom class MyCustomRetryTemplate. For example:
Before
<alias name="defaultConsumerRetryAdvice" alias="consumerRetryAdvice" />
<bean id="defaultConsumerRetryAdvice" class="com.hybris.datahub.jms.ConsumerRetryAdvice">
<property name="retryTemplate" ref="publishBatchRetryTemplate" />
</bean>
<int:service-activator ...>
<int:request-handler-advice-chain>
<ref bean="consumerRetryAdvice" />
</int:request-handler-advice-chain>
</int:service-activator>
After
<!-- 1. The old 'consumerRetryAdvice' bean is completely removed. -->
<!-- 2. A new standard interceptor is created. -->
<bean id="retryInterceptor" class="org.springframework.retry.interceptor.RetryOperationsInterceptor">
<!-- 3. A reference to our RetryTemplate is specified. -->
<property name="retryOperations" ref="publishBatchRetryTemplate" />
</bean>
<!-- 4. The 'publishBatchRetryTemplate' bean now refers to our new class with custom logic. -->
<bean id="publishBatchRetryTemplate" class="com.hybris.datahub.jms.ConsumerRetryTemplate">
<!-- ... your retry policy settings (backOffPolicy, retryPolicy, etc.) remain here ... -->
</bean>
<int:service-activator ...>
<int:request-handler-advice-chain>
<!-- 5. The reference now points to the new 'retryInterceptor'. -->
<ref bean="retryInterceptor" />
</int:request-handler-advice-chain>
</int:service-activator>
c. Verify changes to HTTP response status texts. Due to library updates, status reason phrases might have changed. For example, for status 500, the text changed from "Internal

Server Error" to "Server Error". Verify these strings in your code, especially in tests, and make any necessary updates.
d. Additional API Changes to be aware of.
Changes in Spring integration. The .get() method in IntegrationFlows has been replaced with .getObject().
Before
import org.springframework.integration.dsl.IntegrationFlows;
return IntegrationFlows.from("someChannel").get();
After
import org.springframework.integration.dsl.IntegrationFlow;
return IntegrationFlow.from("someChannel").getObject();
Changes in QueryDSL. The type returned by methods for creating subqueries has changed from JPQLQuery to JPQLSubQuery.
Before
final JPQLQuery<DataHubPoolEntity> pendingActionSubQuery = createPendingActionSubQuery(...);
After
final JPQLSubQuery<DataHubPoolEntity> pendingActionSubQuery = createPendingActionSubQuery(...);
Changes in the Hibernate Statistics API. Methods for accessing statistics have been modified.
Before
import org.hibernate.stat.SecondLevelCacheStatistics;
SecondLevelCacheStatistics stats = statistics.getSecondLevelCacheStatistics(s);
After
import org.hibernate.stat.CacheRegionStatistics;
CacheRegionStatistics stats = statistics.getDomainDataRegionStatistics(s);
6. Adapt your test code. Adapting test code is a significant part of the migration, as Spring Test, Mockito, and JUnit have been updated. You should focus on updating the following key areas:
Spring Security configuration in tests. With the transition to Spring 6, the way security is loaded and configured has changed. XML security configurations (<http> ... </http>)
require significant adaptation. It may be necessary for you to switch to Java-based configuration using SecurityFilterChain for tests to work correctly.

 Note
It is best to review all custom *-security spring.xml files in your project as any changes can also affect the main application configuration.
Transition to JUnit 5. Although not strictly required for compilation, Spring Framework 6 provides native and significantly improved support for JUnit 5. Migrating from JUnit 4 to
JUnit 5 is a best practice to ensure stability and leverage the full benefits of Spring’s new testing infrastructure. This includes replacing annotations (@Before) to (@BeforeEach),
updating the handling of expected exceptions, and using the new Assertions API.
Preserving constructor parameter names. If your XML bean configurations use autowiring by constructor parameter name, add the -parameters flag to the maven-compiler-

plugin configuration. This preserves parameter names in the bytecode allowing Spring to correctly inject dependencies. For example:

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.

176

3/9/26, 4:28 PM
<plugin>
<groupId>org.apache.maven.plugins</groupId>
<artifactId>maven-compiler-plugin</artifactId>
<configuration>
<parameters>true</parameters>
</configuration>
</plugin>
This approach is a pragmatic solution for supporting existing legacy code and ensuring backwards compatibility compared to type-based injection or explicit annotations, for
example, (@Qualifier).

 Note
Be prepared to address specific issues, such as changes in constructor argument order that Spring may now resolve incorrectly, or adaptations to new versions of Mockito.

Implementing a Fixed Issue
There are additional steps to implement some fixed issues.

Fixing Issues with Open Payment Framework Tax Calculation
The document outlines the resolution to inaccuracies in the open payment framework's tax calculation by updating the essentialdata-opffacades-integrationObject.impex file to
include the lineTaxPercentage value, along with step-by-step instructions for implementing the fix through the SAP Commerce Administration Console.

Context
In the previous version of the essentialdata-opffacades-integrationObject.impex file, the opfIntegrationObject did not include the lineTaxPercentage value. As a result,
open payment framework was forced to calculate this value based on lineTotal and lineTax. However, this calculated value turned out to be inaccurate and did not match the original value in SAP
Commerce Cloud. To resolve this discrepancy, the essentialdata-opffacades-integrationObject.impex file has been updated to include the lineTaxPercentage value.

Procedure
1. Log in SAP Commerce Administration Console as administrator
2. Go to the Console tab and select ImpEx Import option.
3. Copy the ImpEx content from essentialdata-opffacades-integrationObject.impex (in folder: \opffacades\resources\impex and paste to the text box of the Import
content section.
4. Click Import content.

Enabling Card-Saving: Expose Customer ID in OPF Integration
To facilitate the card-saving functionality for supported payment service providers (PSPs), this guide details the steps to expose the customer ID field in the open payment framework (OPF)
integration object through the SAP Commerce Administration Console.

Context
To enable the card-saving feature for PSPs that support it, it is essential to expose the customer ID field in the OPF integration object. This allows the PSP to utilize the customer ID as a unique
identifier for storing card information. Follow the procedure below to implement this change in the SAP Commerce Administration Console.

Procedure
1. Log in to the SAP Commerce Administration Console as an administrator.
2. Navigate to the Console tab and select the ImpEx Import option.
3. Copy the ImpEx content from the file essentialdata-opfservices-integrationObject.impex, located in the folder \opfservices\resources\impex.
4. Paste the copied content into the text box of the Import content section.
5. Click Import content to complete the process.

This is custom documentation. For more information, please visit SAP Help Portal.
